201501	57	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Next, we’re up to item 4, “Proposed Revisions to the Authorization for Domestic Open Market Operations,” and I’d like to call on Simon to introduce this item.	41	4
201501	58	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	41	4
201501	59	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	As part of the annual review of the Committee’s authorizations for domestic open market operations and foreign currency transactions, and as discussed in the memo titled “Request for Votes on Authorization for Desk Operations” that you received prior to the meeting, the Desk recommends approving the authorization with a few changes.	41	4
201501	60	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	In addition to these proposed changes, I’d like to highlight one additional item for the Committee’s consideration: In January 2009, the Committee suspended the Guidelines for the Conduct of System Open Market Operations in Federal-Agency Issues in light of the Federal Reserve’s programs to purchase agency debt and agency MBS.	41	4
201501	61	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	The SOMA contains a significant amount of agency debt and agency MBS, and it continues to conduct transactions in agency MBS as part of the reinvestment policy adopted by the Committee.	41	4
201501	62	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Consequently, I recommend a continued suspension of these guidelines.	41	4
201501	63	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	No Committee vote is needed to continue the suspension.	41	4
201501	64	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	With respect to the domestic authorization, we recommend two sets of changes.	41	4
201501	65	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	In the first set of changes, FRBNY and Board staff collaborated on proposed updates to the text and structure of the document, with the aim of simplifying the language so that it can be more easily understood by the public.	41	4
201501	66	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	None of these changes affect the authority delegated or the policies outlined in the domestic authorization.	41	4
201501	67	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	In the second, more substantive set of changes, we recommend a set of revisions that, if approved, will affect some of the authority outlined in the domestic authorization.	41	4
201501	68	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Before discussing the changes that were highlighted in my memo, distributed last week, I’d like to go over a change in the authorization that I failed to highlight, related to the removal of explicit references to types of counterparties.	41	4
201501	69	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	I apologize for the omission of this change in the memo and thank the staff of the Federal Reserve Bank of Minneapolis for alerting me to the lack of explanation of the change.	41	4
201501	70	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	In the existing domestic authorization, outright transactions are authorized with “securities dealers,” while the term “dealer” is used to describe authorized counterparty types for the securities lending program and customer transactions conducted via the FRBNY account.	41	4
201501	71	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	It is not clear what the distinction should be between these counterparty types and whether it is important in determining who should be authorized to transact with the Desk.	41	4
201501	72	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	In particular, the primary dealer policy of the New York Fed explicitly allows for both SEC-registered broker-dealers and federally regulated banks to be counterparties.	41	4
201501	73	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Meanwhile, the authorization for temporary open market operations makes no mention of counterparties at all.	41	4
201501	74	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	The existing language is inconsistent and makes distinctions between counterparty types that may no longer be relevant.	41	4
201501	75	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	To address this, we removed references to counterparties altogether.	41	4
201501	76	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Although this change could theoretically broaden the Desk’s ability to choose a wider range of counterparties, in practice the definition of a “dealer” is so broad that the existing language is not a constraint.	41	4
201501	77	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Further, the proposed change would not affect our existing practice, and, even under the proposed streamlined language, the Desk would not add or remove counterparty types or alter the current framework for managing counterparties without seeking FOMC approval.	41	4
201501	78	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	This change was not highlighted in the memo because it was seen as a change intended to deal with inconsistent language.	41	4
201501	79	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	However, the recent discussions of counterparties in Desk operations imply that this should have been highlighted as a substantive change.	41	4
201501	80	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	My apologies, again, for not including it in the memo.	41	4
201501	81	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	If you prefer, we can retain the existing references to counterparties.	41	4
201501	82	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Please see the exhibit in your handout titled “Material for Briefing on Proposed Revisions to the Authorization for Domestic Open Market Operations,” which compares the existing language on the left panel and the proposed language on the right panel.	41	4
201501	83	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	The proposed language contains three insertions in bracketed blue text that can be made to retain the existing authority on counterparties; please see paragraphs 1, 3, and 4.	41	4
201501	84	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Returning to the four changes described in the memo, the first three of these changes are related to the desire to clarify existing practice.	41	4
201501	85	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	The fourth change is intended to update the language to account for the current operating model in which there is a large total amount of commercial bank reserves.	41	4
201501	86	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	The first change introduces the term “Selected Bank.”	41	4
201501	87	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	This conforms to a change proposed for all FOMC organizational documents and it amounts to prudent planning to simplify the transfer of authority from the FRBNY to another Federal Reserve Bank selected by the Committee in the event of a significant contingency.	41	4
201501	88	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	The second change removes paragraph 3, which authorizes the Selected Bank to transact in agency MBS through agents such as asset managers.	41	4
201501	89	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	As the Desk now conducts all trading in agency MBS internally, it no longer requires this authority.	41	4
201501	90	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	The third proposed change defines the types of collateral accepted in the Desk’s securities lending operation.	41	4
201501	91	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	The existing language does not make any such specification.	41	4
201501	92	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	The new language specifies that, for a loan of US Treasury securities, counterparties can pledge only US Treasury securities or cash; for a loan of US agency securities, counterparties can pledge US agency securities, US Treasury securities, or cash.	41	4
201501	93	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	This clarifies that the collateral pledged must be of equal or superior quality to the collateral borrowed.	41	4
201501	94	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Note that while the Selected Bank would now have the authority to conduct securities lending against cash collateral on a regular basis, it would not exercise this authority beyond current practice without the prior approval of the FOMC.	41	4
201501	95	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Currently, the Desk’s securities lending program accepts only US Treasury securities as collateral, although cash is accepted on an intraday basis as part of the settlement process.	41	4
201501	96	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Cash is accepted overnight only in instances in which a counterparty fails to deliver a security.	41	4
201501	97	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	The fourth change to the domestic authorization updates the Chair’s authority in “exceptional circumstances.”	41	4
201501	98	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	The existing authorization allows the Chair of the Committee to “adjust somewhat in exceptional circumstances the degree of pressure on reserve positions and hence the intended federal funds rate.”	41	4
201501	99	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	When the language in this existing paragraph was introduced 15 years ago, the memo proposing the language expressed a desire for the Chair to have the authority to alter the stance of policy in exceptional circumstances.	41	4
201501	100	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	However, the precise language incorporated into the domestic authorization in 2000 reflected the approach to policy implementation at the time.	41	4
201501	101	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Because adjustments to the monetary policy stance may now be implemented in a number of ways, we propose that the language be updated to take this into account.	41	4
201501	102	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	In particular, we propose that the directive provide that the Chair can “adjust somewhat in exceptional circumstances the stance of monetary policy.”	41	4
201501	103	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	The proposed language would still require that the Chair make decisions in the context of the stance of policy at the most recent meeting and consult with the Committee in advance whenever feasible.	41	4
201501	104	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Note that the side-by-side comparison we sent in the memo used “if feasible” instead of “whenever feasible.”	41	4
201501	105	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	This is corrected in the handout in front of you.	41	4
201501	106	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Under modern communications technology, we’d expect that such consultation would nearly always be feasible.	41	4
201501	107	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Before the Chairman requests a vote on the domestic authorization, we would be happy to answer any questions on the proposed changes.	41	4
201501	108	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Are there questions or comments?	41	4
201501	109	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	President Lacker.	41	4
201501	110	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	Yes.	41	4
201501	111	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	I’d like to comment on the counterparty matter that Simon raised at the beginning of his remarks, as part of our conversation yesterday about this.	41	4
201501	112	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	Clearly, the situation we had in the previous authorization wasn’t ideal.	41	4
201501	113	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	The term “dealer” is there for historical reasons.	41	4
201501	114	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	It’s not precisely defined.	41	4
201501	115	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	It has a common-sense English language meaning, however, that I think is plausibly restrictive in the sense that there are some counterparties you could imagine that wouldn’t qualify as dealers in the plain-English version of the meaning of the word.	41	4
201501	116	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	So it seemed, at first blush, to be removing an important constraint on the Desk.	41	4
201501	117	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	I totally trust the Desk not to expand the typical counterparties of open market operations and of repo and securities lending operations without consulting the Committee.	41	4
201501	118	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	I totally get that.	41	4
201501	119	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	But my concern is that making this change with such short notice doesn’t seem advisable.	41	4
201501	120	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	So I’d advocate that we do include the bracketed items.	41	4
201501	121	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	The Committee needs a chance to understand what the implications are.	41	4
201501	122	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	There’s a study under way of the entire counterparty framework, and rationalizing how the authorization and other documentary devices of the Committee deal with counterparties would be a good thing.	41	4
201501	123	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	But we should probably await that before we make any substantive change.	41	4
201501	124	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	This is a substantive change that will appear to the public.	41	4
201501	125	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	While it’s not likely to be plastered over the front pages of many newspapers, there is a set of market participants who will take notice, wonder what this implies, and perhaps spend time speculating about what this implies about the Committee’s intentions for the capability of expanding counterparties of the Desk’s operations in the future.	41	4
201501	126	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	So until we actually get through more work to understand this— and in view of the very short amount of time the Committee has had to digest these documents that were posted Friday evening—I’d urge that we retain the status quo by including the bracketed phrasing in the proposed directive.	41	4
201501	127	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	And I should mention that I fully support all of the other changes in the directive.	41	4
201501	128	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	To clarify one thing with regard to temporary open market operations, there’s no reference to counterparties in the current authorization, and that would remain if we transported that language over.	41	4
201501	129	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	Exactly.	41	4
201501	130	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	I misspoke.	41	4
201501	131	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Let me ask if there are other comments on the matter that President Lacker has raised here.	41	4
201501	132	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	President Kocherlakota.	41	4

201501	136	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Whenever we change language of this kind, we should have an opportunity to have careful deliberation over it, and so I would prefer to keep the status quo for that reason.	41	4
201501	137	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Similarly, I don’t know if I would counsel this at this meeting, but I think that, with the technological changes that have occurred in the past 15 years, it’s reasonable for the Committee to rethink whether there are any situations in which it would not be feasible for the Committee members to be called on to decide on a monetary policy issue.	41	4

201501	174	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	We’re ready to move on to item 5, which is a set of three related authorizations pertaining to foreign currency operations.	41	4
201501	175	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Again, I’d like to ask Simon to introduce this item.	41	4
201501	176	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	41	4
201501	177	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	We also recommend that the Committee approve the foreign authorization with two amendments.	41	4
201501	178	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	The first change, as with the domestic authorization, is to adopt the “Selected Bank” language.	41	4
201501	179	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	The second change reflects the ongoing challenges we face in managing the euro foreign exchange reserves portfolio in the current interest rate environment.	41	4
201501	180	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	As yields on European sovereign debt and money market instruments have fallen in recent months, we’ve increased somewhat the duration of the euro portfolio, and the Desk has, at times, faced difficulty finding short-term, positive-yielding investments.	41	4
201501	181	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Consequently, we propose increasing the maximum duration of the foreign currency portfolio from 18 months to 24 months, as discussed at the December FOMC meeting.	41	4
201501	182	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Increasing this limit will give us more flexibility to manage the portfolio.	41	4
201501	183	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Note that approval of these documents includes approval of the System’s warehousing agreement with the Treasury.	41	4
201501	184	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	As has been the case since February 5, 1997, the limit on warehousing is set at $5 billion.	41	4
201501	185	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	There are currently no outstanding balances.	41	4

201501	378	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	But if we should debate that, then we should debate that.	92	9

201501	380	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	Periodically, I have heard people make comments along the lines that they’re not worried about low inflation today because it is very unlikely it will go below zero.	92	9
201501	381	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	Let me just state the symmetric dual for this observation and ask if there’s any doubt that everyone would be bothered by it.	92	9
201501	382	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	Let me put this in language that the minutes might reflect:  “Participant X stated that they were not worried about inflation being well above our objective, because it was very unlikely to go above 4 percent.”	92	9
201501	383	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	My view of our consensus statement is that both extreme conditions require a policy response to get inflation back to our 2 percent objective.	92	9
201501	384	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	I view our consensus statement as consistent with these modest views I’ve expressed today, and I will vote to reaffirm the statement before us.	92	9
201501	385	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201501	386	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	92	9

201501	390	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	In my view, the consensus statement has provided real value to the Committee by laying out for the general public the Committee’s broad approach to carrying out its responsibilities under the law, particularly—if I can echo President Kocherlakota—in the 2 percent inflation objective.	92	9
201501	391	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	I see it as constitutional in nature, and it therefore represents many compromises among the authors, some of which are obvious to the reading public from the language and some of which are less so.	92	9

201501	393	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	It is reasonable, in my view, to expect that, when arriving at a common statement by a large group of people dealing with conflicts and controversial issues, there will be unresolved issues and compromises.	92	9
201501	394	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	All of that could easily be said of the US Constitution, which has worked well over these years.	92	9

201501	406	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	So I guess I’m more convinced than ever that this statement reflects an agreement on language, without any genuine consensus on the aims of monetary policy, something that is of particular significance now, in the immediate past, and perhaps in the immediate future.	92	9

201501	412	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	The Constitution was agreed- upon language, which then has a different authority doing the interpretation—thereby not allowing everyone who agreed on the original to be his or her own interpreter.	92	9
201501	413	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	I think that’s an important point of distinction, which is why one has to look to something more like an international agreement to see whether there is a genuine consensus underlying the agreed-upon language, even though, inevitably, ambiguities will result.	92	9

201501	501	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	I’d like to now call on Simon to deliver the first part of the Desk briefing, which focuses on market developments.	61	6
201501	502	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	61	6
201501	503	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	As you noted, Lorie and I will be splitting the Desk briefing into two parts.	61	6
201501	504	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	I will first discuss financial market developments.	61	6
201501	505	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Lorie will then review domestic operations, before discussing results of our year-end overnight and term reverse repo operations and a staff proposal for further testing.	61	6
201501	506	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Longer-run nominal rates in developed economies continued to decline over the intermeeting period, as shown in the top-left panel of your first exhibit.	61	6
201501	507	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Market participants have attributed the declines to a variety of factors, including increased downside risks to the outlooks for economic growth and inflation stemming from overseas developments.	61	6
201501	508	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Growing expectations of an expansion of ECB asset purchases, and then the announcement of the new program, also contributed to the declines while also supporting risk assets, especially in the euro area.	61	6
201501	509	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Market participants are increasingly focused on spillover effects from low rates abroad as a key factor pushing down interest rates in the United States.	61	6
201501	510	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Market commentary also continues to cite the possibility of “secular stagnation” across developed economies as underpinning the sustained declines over the past year.	61	6
201501	511	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Declining levels of inflation compensation account for an important portion of the moves in longer-dated nominal rates.	61	6
201501	512	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	As shown in the top-right panel, market-based measures of five-year, five-year-forward inflation compensation have fallen across major developed economies over the past year, with the most pronounced moves in the euro area and the United States.	61	6
201501	513	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Over the intermeeting period, US forward inflation compensation measures declined further, while euro-area inflation compensation increased, on net, partly because of growing expectations of ECB policy action.	61	6
201501	514	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Despite the very low levels of domestic inflation compensation, survey measures of longer-term inflation expectations, including those from the Desk’s surveys of primary dealer and buy-side participants, remain relatively stable and close to the Committee’s longer-run inflation goal.	61	6
201501	515	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Contributing to the falls in forward inflation compensation in the United States and abroad have been low and declining realized inflation, continued steep declines in commodity prices, and questions regarding the ability and commitment on the part of central banks to move inflation back to target.	61	6
201501	516	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	As shown in the middle-left panel, commodity prices have fallen substantially since last summer, and these declines continued during the intermeeting period.	61	6
201501	517	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Front-month crude oil futures prices fell another 18 percent over the period and have declined over 55 percent since last July.	61	6
201501	518	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	For a better understanding of the declines since July, the most recent Desk surveys asked respondents to rate the importance of supply, demand, and technical factors in explaining the move.	61	6
201501	519	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Respondents were nearly unanimous in expressing their belief that supply-related factors have been the most important driver of the decline in oil prices.	61	6
201501	520	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Consistent with these responses, copper and other industrial metals prices, which many use as proxies for global economic growth, were relatively little changed during the early stages of the oil price declines.	61	6
201501	521	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	However, more recently, these industrial metals have also declined sharply, also shown in the middle-left panel, to the lowest levels in over five years.	61	6
201501	522	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Market participants have suggested that this likely reflects increased concerns regarding the demand outlook stemming from Europe and China.	61	6
201501	523	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	To counter building disinflationary pressures stemming from increased downside risks to the global growth outlook and commodity price declines, numerous developed economy and some emerging market central banks eased policy or signaled an easing bias over the intermeeting period, as shown in the middle-right panel.	61	6
201501	524	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	To counter the effects of ECB measures on their exchange rates, both the Swiss and Danish central banks cut interest rates, moving policy rates into deeply negative territory.	61	6
201501	525	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	The SNB also abandoned its floor on the exchange rate between the Swiss franc and the euro.	61	6
201501	526	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	The Swiss, Danish, Swedish, and European central banks now all have negative deposit rates, and there are expectations that the SNB deposit rate could be cut a further 25 basis points to negative 1 percent.	61	6
201501	527	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	The experience of these central banks with negative interest rates and the limited market-functioning effects to date may reduce concerns about lowering deposit rates below zero for some other central banks.	61	6
201501	528	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Beyond continental Europe, the Bank of Canada unexpectedly cut its policy rate in response to recent oil price declines, and the Bank of England minutes signaled a slight shift in the distribution of MPC views as two longstanding dissenting members stopped voting for higher rates.	61	6
201501	529	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Some emerging market central banks also cut rates earlier than expected, while expectations of EM policy rates more broadly continue to be revised downward.	61	6
201501	530	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Of these policy actions, the ECB announcement was the most eagerly anticipated.	61	6
201501	531	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	As the bottom-left panel details, the ECB announced that it would expand its existing asset purchase programs and will purchase €60 billion of public- and private-sector assets per month.	61	6
201501	532	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	The expanded purchases will start in March, and the ECB stated that it intends to continue purchases until at least September 2016 and, in any case, until it sees a sustained adjustment in the path of inflation that is consistent with achieving its inflation objective.	61	6
201501	533	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	The purchases would total €1.1 trillion if continued through September 2016, which, all else being equal, would bring the ECB’s balance sheet above early 2012 levels.	61	6
201501	534	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	The purchases will be allocated according to the ECB capital key, and the ECB will purchase securities with maturities of 2 to 30 years.	61	6
201501	535	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	The ECB announcement was interpreted by market participants as more accommodative than expected due to the larger-than-anticipated size and open-ended structure of the purchases.	61	6
201501	536	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	As shown in the bottom-right panel, following the announcement, euro-area sovereign yields declined, particularly at longer maturities, as some were surprised by the inclusion of very long-dated bonds in the purchase program.	61	6
201501	537	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Longer-dated peripheral spreads narrowed and euro-area equities rose broadly, led by financial institutions and peripheral equity indexes.	61	6
201501	538	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	The euro also continued its recent sharp depreciation, weakening by more than 3 percent against the US dollar to its lowest level in a decade, and options prices moved to suggest increased demand for protection against further euro depreciation.	61	6
201501	539	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	These moves generally extended previous price movements as expectations for ECB sovereign debt asset purchases gradually built over the course of this past fall and winter in the wake of President Draghi’s remarks at Jackson Hole.	61	6
201501	540	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	As a result of substantial cumulative policy actions abroad and the subdued outlook in many countries, rates in many sovereign debt markets are at historically low levels.	61	6
201501	541	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	As shown in the top-left panel of your next exhibit, German and Japanese yields out to the 5-year tenor are either negative or zero.	61	6
201501	542	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Swiss interest rates are negative out past 10 years.	61	6
201501	543	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Further, the German yield curve looks remarkably similar to that of Japan, an economy that has battled deflation for the better part of two decades.	61	6
201501	544	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	These negative rates have posed challenges to many global investors, particularly official managers of foreign exchange reserves, and have required many to increase the duration of their investments in order to achieve positive returns.	61	6
201501	545	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	We have, of course, faced similar challenges in the SOMA foreign portfolio, prompting the increase in the authorized duration limit.	61	6
201501	546	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	We will continue to update the Committee on our management of the portfolio in this negative-rate environment.	61	6
201501	547	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Over recent months, outsized declines in foreign interest rates have contributed to a widening in two-year sovereign interest rate differentials between the United States and other major developed economies.	61	6
201501	548	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	This shift in rate differentials has continued to support a broad appreciation of the dollar, as shown in the top-right panel.	61	6
201501	549	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Over the intermeeting period, the DXY dollar index increased more than 7 percent.	61	6
201501	550	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Although not included in the DXY index, Chinese authorities have recently allowed their currency to depreciate, which is adding to further broad dollar strength.	61	6
201501	551	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	The shift in short-tenor interest rate differentials reflects the fact that most market participants continue to expect the FOMC to increase the target federal funds rate in the middle of this year while other major central banks are undertaking substantial actions to promote a highly accommodative policy stance.	61	6
201501	552	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Indeed, in the most recent Desk surveys, respondents continue to place the highest probability on liftoff occurring in June, as shown in the middle-left panel, though there has been a modest increase in the perceived odds of a later liftoff since the December survey.	61	6
201501	553	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Survey respondents attributed the slight shift to slowing core inflation, tepid wage growth, and increasing downside growth risks overseas.	61	6
201501	554	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Some market participants have suggested that recent declines in inflation and inflation compensation should prompt the Committee to hold off on beginning to normalize the stance of monetary policy until direct signs of upward inflation pressures emerge.	61	6
201501	555	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	The Chair’s press conference following the December FOMC meeting appears to have effectively pushed back against the view that low near-term inflation will delay liftoff, and Desk survey respondents increasingly expect that liftoff will occur against a backdrop of low realized inflation.	61	6
201501	556	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	The median response for the most likely level of 12-month headline PCE inflation at liftoff declined 80 basis points from the December surveys, to a level of 80 basis points, as shown in the leftmost column of the middle-right panel.	61	6
201501	557	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	The next column of the table shows that, in contrast to this decline, the central expectation for PCE inflation one to two years after liftoff has remained close to 2 percent.	61	6
201501	558	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	However, as shown in the final two columns, respondents, particularly those on the buy side, increased the probability they attach to inflation over that one-to-two-year horizon following liftoff remaining below 1.75 percent.	61	6
201501	559	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Looking beyond liftoff, expectations with regard to the federal funds rate path through 2017 declined modestly in the most recent surveys.	61	6
201501	560	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	These declines may reflect an increase in perceived risks of a premature tightening in the federal funds rate, an event that could subsequently lead the Committee to slow the pace of rate increases, pause the tightening cycle, or potentially cut rates and return to the zero lower bound.	61	6
201501	561	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	However, Desk survey responses suggest that the probability of returning to the zero bound within two years of liftoff is little changed since December at around 20 percent, and most respondents do not view premature tightening as the main factor in their assessment of the likelihood of returning to the zero bound.	61	6
201501	562	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Instead, they view future adverse shocks as the most important factor.	61	6
201501	563	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	While beliefs about the timing of liftoff and the federal funds rate path are relatively little changed as measured by the Desk surveys, market pricing continues to give a different read on market expectations and shows substantial changes in the risk-neutral expected path of policy, as shown in the bottom-left panel.	61	6
201501	564	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Over the intermeeting period, the market initially priced in an additional 25 basis point increase in the target rate by the end of 2017, with the implied end-of-2017 rate reaching its recent peak following better-than-expected third-quarter US GDP data on December 23.	61	6
201501	565	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Then, despite better-than-expected employment data, the market reversed course and is now pricing in one less 25 basis point rate increase by the end of 2017 relative to the path immediately before the December meeting.	61	6
201501	566	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Survey-implied term premiums embedded in 2016 and 2017 interest rate futures contracts—measured as the difference between the market-implied funds rate and the mean expectation from the Desk surveys—became more negative over the intermeeting period, as shown in the bottom-right panel.	61	6
201501	567	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	As discussed at the December meeting, such negative term premiums may reflect concerns about negative shocks to the global economic outlook in an environment of low nominal rates.	61	6
201501	568	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	An alternative and more benign interpretation is that the recent steep drop in term premiums largely results from spillover effects related to lower interest rates abroad and QE-related portfolio-rebalancing flows, which may have also supported the intermeeting increase in global equities and other risk assets.	61	6
201501	569	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Thomas Laubach will discuss some of the policy implications of these alternative views in his briefing tomorrow.	61	6
201501	570	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	Before handing over to Lorie, we’d be happy to answer any questions on financial market developments.	61	6

201501	596	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	They will buy across the curve, so that’s similar to what the Bank of Japan and the Bank of England do.	62	6

201501	615	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	61	6
201501	616	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	I’ll begin on exhibit 3 with a review of Desk operations and end with a proposal for additional testing of the Committee’s policy normalization tools.	61	6
201501	617	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	The Desk’s MBS reinvestment operations continue to proceed smoothly.	61	6
201501	618	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	Notably, the size of those purchases is projected to increase meaningfully, as shown in the top-left panel.	61	6
201501	619	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	We now project that MBS reinvestments in 2015 will total almost $400 billion, approximately 30 percent higher than projected ahead of the December FOMC meeting.	61	6
201501	620	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	The projected increase is primarily due to the substantial decline in longer-term Treasury yields, a decline that has put downward pressure on mortgage rates and boosted expected refinancing activity.	61	6
201501	621	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	To enhance operational readiness should the Committee decide in the future to sell any of the SOMA MBS holdings, the Desk executed five small-value MBS sales operations totaling about $440 million over the intermeeting period.	61	6
201501	622	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	The sales were executed successfully and helped highlight a few technical and procedural improvements to our operating framework, which we’ll begin implementing in the near term.	61	6
201501	623	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	As we discussed at the October meeting, the Desk continues work on enhancing the calculation of the effective federal funds rate and publishing a new overnight bank funding rate, as detailed in the top-right panel.	61	6
201501	624	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	We intend to announce the planned changes in a Desk statement on February 2 and will circulate a draft of the announcement for comment ahead of the release.	61	6
201501	625	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	The statement will describe the change in the data source for the effective rate, from brokered to Federal Reserve 2420 data, as a technical enhancement to the calculation process made in the context of recent international efforts to improve reference rates.	61	6
201501	626	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	The statement will characterize the new overnight bank funding rate, which will include both Eurodollar and federal funds transactions of US-based banking offices, as a broader measure of banks’ marginal borrowing costs that will be published for purposes of transparency.	61	6
201501	627	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	We’re planning to implement these changes within a year, but, in the statement, we’ll leave some flexibility in the timing in case there are substantive comments to the Federal Register notice describing the data revisions.	61	6
201501	628	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	Over the intermeeting period, the Desk completed the test of the term RRP operations that covered year-end.	61	6
201501	629	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	The $600 billion combined capacity of the term and overnight RRPs appears to have been effective at supporting money market rates by providing greater certainty to investors about the availability of investments spanning year-end.	61	6
201501	630	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in the middle-left panel, the first two operations were oversubscribed, with the rates determined by the auction process, while the final two operations were undersubscribed and awarded at the maximum bid rate of 10 basis points.	61	6
201501	631	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	Government money market funds were the main participants in the early term RRP operations, reportedly because they have fewer investment alternatives than prime funds and wanted to secure investments over year-end early.	61	6
201501	632	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in the middle-right panel, there was a substantial amount of substitution between term RRP—shown in the blue bars—and overnight RRP—shown in the red bars—during the first two term operations.	61	6
201501	633	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	As a result, overnight RRP take-up declined, reaching just $35 billion after the second term RRP operation.	61	6
201501	634	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in the dark-blue bars in the bottom-left panel, overnight RRP take-up over year-end increased to $171 billion but was well below the authorized cap, and thus all funds were awarded at the maximum rate of 5 basis points.	61	6
201501	635	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	Total participation in the term and overnight operations was around $400 billion, similar to the amount of bids received at the overnight operation on the September quarter-end but far less than the $600 billion in available capacity authorized by the Committee.	61	6
201501	636	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	Consistent with recent quarter-end dates, prime money funds accounted for most of the overnight RRP take-up on the year-end date.	61	6
201501	637	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	All of the term RRPs matured on January 5, which had led some market participants to express concern about operational risk associated with having a large portion of their portfolio mature on a single day.	61	6
201501	638	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	However, the unwind of the term RRPs was orderly.	61	6
201501	639	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	Overnight RRP take-up did increase notably on January 5, absorbing some of the maturing term investments, a development you can also see in that bottom-left panel.	61	6
201501	640	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	As with previous quarter-ends, the increase in RRP take-up reflected the decline in private-sector money market activity primarily associated with foreign banking organizations’ desire to shrink their balance sheets on financial statement dates.	61	6
201501	641	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in the bottom-right panel, the decline in money market volumes over year-end was broadly in line with previous year- and quarter-ends.	61	6
201501	642	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	Conversations with market participants suggest that the combination of term and overnight RRP operations was effective in supporting money market rates leading into and at year-end.	61	6
201501	643	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	As shown in the top-left panel of your final exhibit, although some money market rates declined on year-end, they generally stayed at or above the overnight RRP rate both prior to and on year-end.	61	6
201501	644	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	Recall that, in contrast, some money market rates fell below the overnight RRP rate leading into and over the September quarter-end.	61	6
201501	645	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	As also shown in the top-left panel, with the exception of a brief decline on year- end, the effective federal funds rate has remained between 12 and 13 basis points in recent weeks, even as the overnight RRP rate—the red line in the chart—was lowered back to 5 basis points in mid-December.	61	6
201501	646	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	Market participants have been somewhat surprised by this, as most anticipated that the effective rate would return to the level prevailing prior to the increases in the overnight RRP rate.	61	6
201501	647	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	The top-right panel provides more detail regarding the recent elevated levels of the federal funds rate by examining the distribution of rates on federal funds trades.	61	6
201501	648	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	In the weeks prior to the changes in the overnight RRP rate, the majority of federal funds trading occurred around 7 to 8 basis points, as shown by the dark-blue line.	61	6
201501	649	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	Following the increase in the overnight RRP rate to 10 basis points, the distribution shifted higher—shown by the light-blue line.	61	6
201501	650	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	Since the overnight RRP rate returned to its pretest level of 5 basis points, the distribution has remained near the levels observed when the overnight RRP rate was 10 basis points.	61	6
201501	651	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	The distribution of Eurodollar trading, which includes a much wider set of cash lenders than in federal funds, followed a similar pattern, as shown in the middle-left panel.	61	6
201501	652	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	Federal funds and Eurodollars have remained higher even as secured rates have declined.	61	6
201501	653	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	The middle-right panel shows the same distributions as in the prior two panels, but for triparty repo rates.	61	6
201501	654	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	These rates also shifted higher with the increase in the overnight RRP rate but have generally moved back since the overnight RRP rate was decreased back to 5 basis points.	61	6
201501	655	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	It’s not entirely clear why unsecured rates did not decline after the overnight RRP rate test ended.	61	6
201501	656	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	Some market participants have told us that cash lenders learned during the ON RRP test that many foreign banking organizations engaged in IOER arbitrage were willing to pay higher rates for funding, even though this meant accepting a smaller profit, and that this information has had a lasting effect on competitive dynamics in unsecured markets.	61	6
201501	657	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	Notably, the uptick in recent months in unsecured rates does not seem to reflect a rise in perceived credit risk, as the movement in rates appears broad based across firms.	61	6
201501	658	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	Finally, I’ll turn to staff recommendations for further testing of TDFs and RRPs.	61	6
201501	659	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	These recommendations were described in two memos you received prior to this meeting.	61	6
201501	660	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	Beginning with TDFs, as outlined in the bottom-left panel, the staff proposes conducting a series of three test operations, beginning in February and maturing by mid-March.	61	6
201501	661	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	The operations would incorporate two changes relative to the testing thus far.	61	6
201501	662	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	First, they would introduce same-day settlement, which may encourage participation and allow the effects of the tool to be realized more quickly.	61	6
201501	663	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	Second, the proposed operations would have overlapping maturities so that the quantity of outstanding TDFs would gradually increase.	61	6
201501	664	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	The staff recommends limiting the individual award per operation to $20 billion and offering a spread of 3 basis points over the IOER rate.	61	6
201501	665	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	With respect to further testing of term RRPs, the Committee may wish to conduct operations at the March quarter-end in order to test refinements to the term RRP operational framework.	61	6
201501	666	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	If the Committee thought it appropriate to do so, the Desk proposes testing that incorporates four operational refinements, which are based on lessons learned from the tests over year-end and outlined in your bottom-right panel.	61	6
201501	667	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	First, we recommend that the term RRP offered amount be reduced to $200 billion to improve our understanding of the effect of decreasing the available capacity.	61	6
201501	668	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	This is also consistent with the Committee’s interest in limiting its footprint in markets.	61	6
201501	669	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	Second, we recommend that the term RRPs mature across multiple days in early April to avoid operational risks associated with all of the operations maturing on the same day.	61	6
201501	670	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	Third, we propose modest changes to the frequency and tenor of term RRP operations that would result in fewer operations and shorter maturities.	61	6
201501	671	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	Finally, rather than stating a specific maximum bid rate in our communications, the bid rate would be expressed as a spread above the overnight RRP rate on the day of the operation.	61	6
201501	672	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	This would be consistent with the possibility of a change in the target for the federal funds rate following the announcement of the term RRP test offerings but before the actual operations.	61	6
201501	673	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	If the Committee would like to proceed with the proposed term RRP test, the Desk could release a statement following this meeting, with a more detailed operational schedule announced through a second Desk statement in early March.	61	6
201501	674	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	A draft resolution authorizing this test is provided in a separate handout titled “Term Reverse Repurchase Operations Resolution.”3 Finally, the staff outlined a few additional ways of testing RRPs in the memo circulated to the Committee in advance of the meeting.	61	6
201501	675	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	These potential additional tests are also described in the bottom-right panel.	61	6
201501	676	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	If your discussion at this meeting regarding options during normalization suggests a need for additional testing, the staff could come back with detailed proposals along these lines.	61	6
201501	677	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	For example, depending on the preferred approach for the initial stage of normalization, the Committee may be interested in testing term RRP operations that don’t span quarter-ends.	61	6
201501	678	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	The Committee could direct the Desk on a one-time basis to offer a few consecutive term RRPs, with weekly maturities and in modest sizes, to learn more about the extent to which term RRPs could support overnight RRPs in controlling short-term market rates away from quarter-end.	61	6
201501	679	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	The Committee might also be interested in further testing the effect that changes in the overnight RRP rate have on short-term market rates, volumes, and overnight RRP take-up, which could provide additional insight into the desired setting of the IOER–overnight RRP rate spread during normalization.	61	6
201501	680	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	Thank you, and that concludes our prepared remarks.	61	6
201501	681	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	61	6

201501	684	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	Yes.	62	6
201501	685	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	I’m going to make a procedural suggestion, Madam Chair.	62	6
201501	686	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	This has to do with RRP testing.	62	6
201501	687	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	According to the January Survey of Primary Dealers, they already believe we will offer a term facility regularly at quarter-end.	62	6
201501	688	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	This is buried in the back of the primary dealer survey.	62	6
201501	689	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	This has to do with this tension we’ve faced throughout the time we’ve been testing.	62	6
201501	690	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	We’ve wanted to learn more.	62	6
201501	691	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	It’s a genuinely positive benefit of testing.	62	6
201501	692	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	But, at the same time, we’ve been anxious about the extent to which testing encourages broad expectation of a relatively permanent or overly large facility that’s going to persist for some time.	62	6
201501	693	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	And it looks as though, again, our testing over the year-end of a term RRP facility has led expectations to run a bit ahead of where the Committee is on the likelihood of using it.	62	6
201501	694	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	We haven’t even actually decided this yet.	62	6
201501	695	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	I note that our next agenda item, agenda item 9, is where we’re going to discuss our liftoff options.	62	6
201501	696	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	The staff memo presented us with an option 1 and an option 2, and option 1 does without term RRPs.	62	6
201501	697	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	It’s an option I favor, and I think we can do fine without that, with a larger cap and a wide spread to 25 basis points, as I’ll argue later.	62	6
201501	698	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	But our decision about whether we test again a term facility at quarter-end might be usefully informed about whether we think we’re likely to use it on an ongoing basis when we raise rates.	62	6
201501	699	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	Now, I understand that there’s the standard boilerplate whenever we announce these things, and that we can test until the cows come home and it doesn’t mean anything about how we’re going to do things when we actually liftoff.	62	6
201501	700	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	But, in point of fact, we see that what we do leads markets to expect us to use the things we test and roll out.	62	6
201501	701	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	So, if the majority of the Committee coalesces around option 1 and views us as likely to be able to lift off quite smoothly without the use of term RRPs, it might be useful to forgo testing term RRPs.	62	6

201501	715	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	But, at the same time, it’s not unreasonable for the markets to see how well the tests do and, from how well the tests do, make inferences about how likely the Committee is to actually adopt that facility.	62	6

201501	917	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	We’re next going to turn to liftoff tools and options, and, before turning it over to Jim for the staff presentation, I want to make a couple of comments myself.	92	9
201501	918	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	First, I’ll say again that, personally, I consider it absolutely critical that, when we announce liftoff, the federal funds rate move into our increased target range in a smooth, efficient, and prompt manner.	92	9
201501	919	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Personally, I think we need a very high degree of confidence that our normalization tools, in whatever configuration we settle on, will provide sufficient control over interest rates right out of the gate.	92	9
201501	920	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	To me, this is the highest priority.	92	9
201501	921	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Second, our policy tools vary in terms of their benefits, costs, and risks.	92	9
201501	922	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	So we clearly need to strike the right balance in their use.	92	9
201501	923	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	While we may differ to some degree in weighing these various factors, I believe we’ll be best served by an operational plan that’s relatively simple to implement and communicate.	92	9
201501	924	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	For liftoff to go smoothly, it seems essential that market participants will need to have a reasonable idea of what types of investment opportunities will be available to them.	92	9
201501	925	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Of course, the plan needs to be feasible for the Desk to execute with manageable operational risk.	92	9
201501	926	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Third, as noted in the staff memo, the particular choices we make about our tools at the time of liftoff need not constrain us subsequently.	92	9
201501	927	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	I am quite amenable to temporary alterations in the parameters of our tools, such as the cap on the overnight RRP facility, with the expectation that we will dial back the potential size of the facilities over time as we learn more about what’s needed to put a firm floor under rates once we move away from the zero lower bound.	92	9
201501	928	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	For example, we could substitute term RRPs outside quarter-ends for reliance on the overnight RRP facility.	92	9
201501	929	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	But with those preliminary comments of my own, I look forward to hearing your views, and I’m next going to turn the floor over to Jim for a presentation.	92	9
201501	930	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	Thank you very much, Madam Chair.	92	9
201501	931	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	I’ll be referring to the handout labeled “Material for Discussion of Liftoff Tools and Possible Liftoff Options.”	92	9
201501	932	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	As noted in exhibit 1, in its Policy Normalization Principles and Plans, the Committee provided a broad outline of its high-level approach to policy normalization.	92	9
201501	933	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	However, the Committee has not yet described exactly how it plans to use its various tools to implement these general principles and plans.	92	9
201501	934	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	To facilitate your discussion of these issues, the staff prepared a memo that highlights some key issues that policymakers may wish to consider in this regard.	92	9
201501	935	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	An underlying theme of the memo is that policymakers may face some tradeoffs in developing an operational strategy for liftoff that seeks to maximize the odds that liftoff will proceed smoothly from the start while, at the same time, minimizing the risks that could be associated with heavy reliance on particular tools.	92	9
201501	936	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	To explore those issues further, the memo outlined two illustrative options that differ primarily in their relative reliance on overnight and term RRP operations.	92	9
201501	937	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	As noted in the first box in exhibit 2, the recent testing of term RRPs around the year-end provided the backdrop for structuring the options in this way.	92	9
201501	938	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	The year-end tests suggested that there was an important degree of substitutability between overnight RRP and term RRP, at least at the year-end.	92	9
201501	939	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	If that substitution relationship holds at other times as well, it may be possible to use term RRP operations to help manage the level of the take-up in overnight RRP operations.	92	9
201501	940	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	In addition, term RRP operations would be fixed in size, they would be offered only on specific dates, and the rate would always be determined at auction.	92	9
201501	941	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	As a result, the financial stability risks associated with term RRP operations may be viewed as lower than those associated with daily overnight reverse repo operations.	92	9
201501	942	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	On the other hand, term RRP operations are more operationally complex than overnight RRP operations, and heavy reliance on term RRP could result in distortions in term financing markets.	92	9
201501	943	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	In addition, term RRP operations with maturities that extend over FOMC meeting dates could present some potential challenges in avoiding perceptions of signaling policy actions in advance.	92	9
201501	944	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	With these observations in mind, as shown in the middle box, under the first of the two illustrative options, the FOMC would rely principally on overnight reverse RP operations at the time of liftoff to establish a floor for overnight rates.	92	9
201501	945	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	For this tool to provide effective support for short-term interest rates, market participants would require sufficient assurance that the aggregate cap on overnight reverse repos would bind only rarely.	92	9
201501	946	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	To provide this assurance while accounting for the possibility of significant shifts in investor preferences, the FOMC, in this option, would indicate its intention to temporarily increase the cap on overnight reverse repo operations to a level of, say, $600 billion.	92	9
201501	947	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	(Again, the particular numbers here are purely hypothetical at this stage.)  In addition, the FOMC would note that it intends to conduct term RRP operations after liftoff, if necessary, to help control the federal funds rate and to help avoid scenarios in which the cap on overnight reverse repo operations binds regularly.	92	9
201501	948	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	Policymakers might be attracted to option 1 if they judged that the financial stability and footprint risks associated with a sizable temporary increase in the overnight RRP cap are modest and were concerned that the costs of conducting sizable term reverse repo operations could be significant, or that the communications associated with undertaking term operations before liftoff could prove complicated.	92	9
201501	949	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	Policymakers might also be attracted to option 1 if they were confident that they could avoid a situation in which a sizable temporary increase in the overnight RRP cap became very long lived.	92	9
201501	950	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	For example, policymakers might judge that the Federal Reserve could communicate in advance its intention to reduce the overnight reverse repo cap if overnight reverse repo take-up did not increase much after liftoff and the additional capacity proved unnecessary.	92	9
201501	951	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	In addition, if overnight reverse repo take-up were quite elevated following liftoff, policymakers could indicate an intention to build up a sizable term reverse repo book or take other steps to return the size of overnight reverse repo operations and the overnight reverse repo cap to lower levels.	92	9
201501	952	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	Under option 2, shown in the far-right box, the FOMC would rely more heavily on the use of term reverse repos as a supplementary tool and would indicate its intention to boost the cap temporarily on overnight reverse repo operations by a more modest amount from, say, $300 billion to $400 billion.	92	9
201501	953	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	In addition, it would note that it intends to conduct term reverse repo operations in advance of liftoff, to help ensure that the overnight reverse repo cap does not bind at liftoff and thereafter.	92	9
201501	954	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	Option 2 might be attractive to policymakers who were concerned that a sizable increase in the overnight RRP cap, even if only temporary, could present financial stability and “footprint risks” and might also send a signal that the overnight reverse repo facility will remain quite large for an extended period.	92	9
201501	955	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	For policymakers who are confident that term reverse repo can be used to manage the size of the overnight reverse repo program, the advance use of term reverse repo operations envisioned in option 2 might be viewed as an effective way to mitigate such risks.	92	9
201501	956	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	It bears emphasizing that, while term reverse repo operations play an important role in both options 1 and 2, this potential role hinges importantly on an assumption that term reverse repo can substitute for overnight reverse repo to a significant degree.	92	9
201501	957	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	As Lorie noted earlier, it may be useful to conduct additional tests of term reverse repo away from quarter-ends to get a better handle on whether this assumption is correct.	92	9
201501	958	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	As noted in exhibit 3, apart from options 1 and 2, the memo notes some additional steps that policymakers could consider that might help to enhance control over short- term rates at the time of liftoff.	92	9
201501	959	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	These involve marginal adjustments in the spread between the IOER rate and the overnight RRP rate, changes in the level of the IOER and overnight RRP rates relative to the target range for the federal funds rate, and the possible use of term deposits.	92	9
201501	960	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	All of these steps arguably could help put upward pressure on short-term rates, but they have not figured prominently in the Committee’s discussions to date.	92	9
201501	961	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	Whatever operational strategy the Committee chooses to adopt, the memo notes that policymakers may wish to communicate at least some aspects of that strategy in advance to provide greater clarity to market participants and to enhance confidence that the Federal Reserve is well prepared to conduct a smooth liftoff.	92	9
201501	962	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	For example, it might be useful to provide additional information about the likely calibrations of policy tools and the likely ways they would be used in combination.	92	9
201501	963	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	This information, for example, could be provided in the minutes of future meetings, the Chair’s postmeeting press conference remarks, speeches, and testimonies.	92	9
201501	964	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	Shifting gears a bit, exhibit 4 summarizes some key takeaways from a memo that focused on aspects of the payment of interest on excess reserves that could raise some issues at the time of liftoff.	92	9
201501	965	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	Under our current approach, interest payments on excess reserves are based on the 14-day average concept of excess reserve balances.	92	9
201501	966	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	In particular, there is a single interest rate—currently calculated as the arithmetic average interest rate on excess reserves over the maintenance period—that is assumed to apply over the entire reserve maintenance period in computing the payment of interest on excess reserve balances.	92	9
201501	967	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	As noted in the memo, this can create some complications during those reserve maintenance periods in which policymakers may change the interest rate on excess reserves in the middle of the period.	92	9
201501	968	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	The memo offers a couple of possibilities for addressing this issue.	92	9
201501	969	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	In one option, the Federal Reserve could change the length of the reserve maintenance period from 14 days to 7 days.	92	9
201501	970	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	As long as the FOMC continued to announce its policy decisions on Wednesdays, changes in the IOER rate could then be aligned with the beginning of a new reserve maintenance period.	92	9
201501	971	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	This option is attractive in many respects, but it would also require thousands of depository institutions to change their internal systems to incorporate a 7-day maintenance period.	92	9
201501	972	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	Another option noted was to base the effective interest rate on excess reserves for the entire maintenance period on the interest on excess reserves rate at the end of the reserve maintenance period.	92	9
201501	973	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	This would help ensure that an increase in the IOER rate in the middle of a maintenance period fully supports the FOMC’s decision to raise the target range for the federal funds rate.	92	9
201501	974	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	However, it could also put upward pressure on the federal funds rate prior to the FOMC announcement if it was at least partly anticipated by market participants.	92	9
201501	975	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	A third option, not discussed in the memo, is to base interest payments more heavily on balances held each day and the interest rate on excess reserves in effect each day.	92	9
201501	976	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	This approach appears promising, and we are investigating the feasibility of that approach further.	92	9
201501	977	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	The final exhibit repeats the questions for discussion during the go-round that were provided to you earlier.	92	9
201501	978	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	In addition, we’ve added a question at the end that seeks your views on the usefulness of additional testing of term reverse repo away from quarter-ends along the lines Lorie described earlier as a way to get a better handle on the degree of substitution between overnight and term reverse repo.	92	9
201501	979	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	Thanks, and we’ll be happy to take your questions.	92	9

201501	982	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	Jim, getting back to that question that President Rosengren posed earlier, based on what we’ve seen so far and the analysis you’ve been able to do, is there a nontrivial financial-stability benefit of using term RRP as opposed to ON RRP?	92	9

201501	984	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	I guess I had implicitly assumed, without thinking too much about it, that there was some benefit, if only because there would be a limitation on the ability to rush for the exits from other investments if it was term, as opposed to overnight.	92	9
201501	985	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	But, further thinking about this matter led me to think that if the terms are short enough to be consistent with SEC rules, then maybe there’s not much benefit after all.	92	9
201501	986	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	One way or another, as long as we’re providing a lot of absorption capacity, concerns about whether we are creating a new model for money market funds or making it easier for them to do this are what they are.	92	9
201501	987	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	But maybe it doesn’t make that much difference whether we use more overnight or term.	92	9

201501	989	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	But at least that’s the only thing to be discussed, as opposed to whether we get a lot of benefit through a mix of the two.	92	9
201501	990	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	I’m sorry, Eric.	92	9
201501	991	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	Does that fairly capture your point?	92	9
201501	992	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	Yes.	92	9
201501	993	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	Why don’t I do a follow-on after they address your question?	92	9
201501	994	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	Okay.	92	9
201501	995	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	I’ll offer my view, and Lorie and Simon may have others.	92	9
201501	996	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	I should preface my remarks by saying there’s a little bit of murkiness regarding these issues of financial stability, so I should admit that up-front.	92	9
201501	997	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	As you well know, the financial-stability arguments regarding the overnight reverse repo suggested that there’s an option value associated with it.	92	9
201501	998	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	In the case when financial markets are upset, investors can run to it because it’s a standing facility—or, more precisely, a standing facility with a cap that binds only in rare circumstances.	92	9
201501	999	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	For term reverse repo, you might argue that it presents somewhat less of a financial-stability risk, because people can’t go to it as readily.	92	9
201501	1000	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	It would be offered only on particular dates, not every day.	92	9
201501	1001	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	Moreover, we’d be fixing the size that we would be auctioning.	92	9
201501	1002	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	In addition, there is an immediate price response.	92	9
201501	1003	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	If a crisis happened to occur on the day on which we were auctioning term reverse repo, that would drive down the rate that we would get on the term reverse repo.	92	9
201501	1004	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	So I certainly wouldn’t argue that it’s devoid of the financial-stability risks of the type we discussed with regard to overnight reverse repo, but I think you could argue that it’s probably somewhat less.	92	9
201501	1005	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	There may also be another aspect to it.	92	9
201501	1006	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	This has a little bit of the flavor of the types of arguments that Governor Stein made about a crowding-out effect.	92	9
201501	1007	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	Insofar as you were auctioning term reverse repo on a regular basis and putting some upward pressure on term rates, you might induce some investors, like money funds, not to invest in things that they would flee from in a crisis.	92	9
201501	1008	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	That, at the margin, might also reduce financial-stability risks.	92	9
201501	1009	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	It’s very hard to quantify this.	92	9
201501	1010	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	I think that’s a pretty good summary.	92	9
201501	1011	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	The other, simple part is that the amount of headroom that might be available in the overnight RRP, which is what people have been concerned about, would probably run a little bit lower if we had the term out there because you still have the overnight RRP at the same time.	92	9
201501	1012	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	And the concern most people expressed around this table is just a big rush, around noon sometime, into the overnight RRP.	92	9
201501	1013	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	The idea would be to run with slightly lower headroom, on average, if we have the term than with just the ON RRP by itself.	92	9
201501	1014	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	Although this is a slightly different perspective, thinking in terms of stress building as opposed to happening in an instantaneous fashion.	92	9
201501	1015	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	If we’re doing the term RRP, then, as in 2011, when the money market funds began to pull back, they get a couple of weeks to do it?	92	9
201501	1016	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	That’s what I was wondering.	92	9
201501	1017	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	To me, the two situations depend entirely on how stable the overnight RRP take-up is.	92	9
201501	1018	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	As an example, if it was completely stable and the headroom didn’t change, then moving some of it to term doesn’t really add any benefit.	92	9
201501	1019	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	If the overnight RRP take-up is very variable and moves around a lot, then moving some of it to term can improve financial stability because that headroom can fluctuate quite a bit.	92	9
201501	1020	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	So I think it depends on your assumption about the stability of the daily take-up.	92	9
201501	1021	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	But one thing that seems clear from looking at the tables you attached to this January 22 memo is that it is virtually all about money market funds, right?	92	9

201501	1023	2015-01-28	meeting	LOGAN	But the money funds are fairly stable, except on quarter- end, when you see the prime funds come in and really move around.	92	9
201501	1024	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	Right.	92	9

201501	1030	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	President Rosengren.	92	9

201501	1087	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	This is actually an issue associated with our plain-vanilla excess reserve calculations, and we apologize for tormenting you with this very technical issue.	92	9
201501	1088	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	We pay interest every maintenance period based on the excess reserves as we calculate them over the reserve maintenance period.	92	9
201501	1089	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	We have a single rate that we apply against those excess reserves, and that has these funny issues arise when there is an anticipated change in the IOER in the middle of the maintenance period.	92	9
201501	1090	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	We’re stuck with that because, historically, interest on reserves had always been tied to reserve concepts—required reserves and excess reserves.	92	9
201501	1091	2015-01-28	meeting	CLOUSE	So, to pull this off—to switch to a system in which we’re paying more on daily balances—we actually have to kick off a rather extensive programming effort in the very near future to make this happen.	92	9
