201501	1245	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	President Lacker.	92	9
201501	1246	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201501	1247	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	I think we should be confident that increasing the IOER is going to result in a sufficiently smooth rise in short-term market rates when we raise the target range for the funds rate.	92	9
201501	1248	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	That’s my reading of the wide evidence we’ve gotten from the Desk operations and everything we’ve done so far.	92	9
201501	1249	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	I think we should stick with our plan to use the overnight RRP program as insurance only against the possibility that there’s more slack, perhaps, in the relationship between IOER and market rates than we’ve seen at any time over the past six years.	92	9
201501	1250	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	Using it as a backstop means a relatively wide spread to IOER, so I support the staff’s proposed spread of 25 basis points.	92	9
201501	1251	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	It’s wider than anything we’ve tested so far and, apart from quarter-ends, take-up has not exceeded $300 billion.	92	9
201501	1252	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	With a 25 basis point spread, I’d expect significantly smaller take-up.	92	9
201501	1253	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	But in any event, I’d be comfortable with a large cap at a 25 basis point spread.	92	9
201501	1254	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	So, $600 billion is the size suggested in option 1.	92	9
201501	1255	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	I wouldn’t be against $800 billion or $1 trillion, just to be sure.	92	9
201501	1256	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	With such a large cap and a 25 basis point spread, I think we could be very confident that rates will be in that corridor.	92	9
201501	1257	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	I think we should just make the cap temporarily as large as it needs to be for us to be comfortable that we’re going to be in that corridor.	92	9
201501	1258	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	I think that’s the way to solve our problems.	92	9
201501	1259	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	We’re going to have volatility.	92	9
201501	1260	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	We could well have volatility on quarter-ends.	92	9
201501	1261	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	We always have had volatility on quarter-ends, and there probably always will.	92	9
201501	1262	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	The Desk has historically taken measures over quarter-end, back when we were in the old regime, to try to anticipate the shift in demand for reserves and to counteract that, but everyone recognized that that was a much more uncertain endeavor than off quarter-ends.	92	9
201501	1263	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	So markets realized that volatility—sort of the forecast error of the funds rate—was going to be exceptionally large over quarter-ends and recognized that it didn’t pose a fundamental problem for monetary policy effectiveness.	92	9
201501	1264	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	And I think that’s going to be the case now, even though quarter-end comes a week after one potential prominent liftoff date.	92	9
201501	1265	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	On the strictly macroeconomic side of thinking about liftoff, I agree with others who made the argument that the path for the policy rate we take over time is going to be more important than a particular date at which start raising rates.	92	9
201501	1266	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	For interest rate volatility, I think the behavior that interest rates display over the course of the month after liftoff is going to be much more consequential than what happens on the last day of June, if that’s when we choose to lift off.	92	9
201501	1267	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	So I don’t think one day’s movement a couple of days after our liftoff should concern you.	92	9
201501	1268	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	I think simplicity is a virtue, and, as I said, it is clear we can implement monetary policy without a term RRP program.	92	9
201501	1269	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	I think a term program might be tricky to introduce before a liftoff meeting without tipping our hand or signaling.	92	9
201501	1270	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	I think that’s a delicate problem, but I suppose we could probably figure out a way to do that.	92	9
201501	1271	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	I don’t think the alternative of making the program available now on a continuous basis is attractive because it would further encourage markets to believe that our whole RRP machinery, overnight and term, is more of a permanent feature of the financial landscape than I think we’re intending.	92	9
201501	1272	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	And as I said earlier, we face this tension between expectations getting out of control and wanting to learn some things, and I think we’ve learned what we need to learn.	92	9
201501	1273	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	It’s pretty clear that the pressure on rates going into quarter-end is related to the probability that the overnight facility caps out at quarter-end and rates get driven down.	92	9
201501	1274	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	With a large enough cap, that concern should be minimal, and we’re not likely to get any of the downward pressure leading into quarter-end that motivated the term RRP; the staff recognized this before we did the tests over the year-end.	92	9
201501	1275	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	So in the arguments made—why not use the tool just in case, kind of a belt-and-suspenders approach—I think we see and have seen that our rolling out of facilities like this on a sustained basis builds a constituency.	92	9
201501	1276	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	Building a constituency for a program makes it difficult or costly for us to contemplate pulling back, and I think we’ve seen that in the primary dealer survey data that I talked about.	92	9
201501	1277	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	So I would favor option 1, and I’d be opposed to any further testing of term RRPs now.	92	9
201501	1278	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	I think we know enough about how they work.	92	9
201501	1279	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	I think rolling them out, if it seems warranted, in the weeks after we raise rates is the way to keep that extra capability in reserve.	92	9
201501	1280	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201501	1281	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	92	9
201501	1282	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	President Rosengren.	92	9
201501	1283	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201501	1284	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	Raising rates as announced at the time of liftoff is essential for maintaining our credibility.	92	9
201501	1285	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	In particular, quickly moving the federal funds rate into the range we announce should be our primary operational goal at liftoff.	92	9
201501	1286	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	To enforce the range we set, we need to guarantee a floor.	92	9
201501	1287	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	If we are using the reverse repo facility to set the floor price, we need to be flexible on the quantity of reverse repos.	92	9
201501	1288	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	Hence, setting the floor may require the forceful use of our tools at the time of liftoff.	92	9
201501	1289	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	It is likely that the more vigorous use of the reverse repo facility will be temporary, so we should be able to quickly reduce it as we better understand the factors that influence the spread between the IOER and the reverse repo rates.	92	9
201501	1290	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	To avoid disruption to financial markets, we should announce our intention to use the reverse repo facility as a temporary measure to ensure a smooth liftoff.	92	9
201501	1291	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	Assuming that we announce a target range of 25 to 50 basis points at liftoff, I would set the IOER at a level where we can expect to achieve at least the 25 basis point floor with our usual reverse repo cap.	92	9
201501	1292	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	However, I would announce no reverse repo cap at first in order to allow the overnight reverse repo to enforce the floor, should our estimates prove wrong.	92	9
201501	1293	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	We have a lot to learn about managing the federal funds rate using a method that we have not used before.	92	9
201501	1294	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	We could then make a technical correction of the IOER, if needed, to maintain the federal funds rate within the 25 to 50 basis point range without needing to rely so heavily on overnight reverse repos.	92	9
201501	1295	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	Removing the reverse repo cap during the time of liftoff would convincingly convey our commitment to raise rates, possibly requiring less use of reverse repos.	92	9
201501	1296	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	Two financial-stability concerns about the reverse repo facility have been raised.	92	9
201501	1297	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	The first is that use of the facility could alter the structure of the money markets.	92	9
201501	1298	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	Announcing the temporary nature of the program should lower this risk.	92	9
201501	1299	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	By keeping the window short when we lift off and making appropriate adjustments without delay, it should be clear through our actions that our thinking on permanence has not changed.	92	9
201501	1300	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	The other financial stability concern is the possible flight to the facility during times of severe stress.	92	9
201501	1301	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	However, if there is a significant negative shock that results in a substantial flight of funds to the reverse repo program, the appropriate response would be to postpone liftoff until the effects of the negative shock were better understood.	92	9
201501	1302	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	Allowing for a significant temporary increase in the overnight reverse repo facility would be advisable.	92	9
201501	1303	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	I would go one step further and announce no path at the time of liftoff.	92	9
201501	1304	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	In terms of part b of that question, if the Committee is willing to have no reverse repo cap at liftoff, term reverse repos would not be necessary.	92	9
201501	1305	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	The lower the cap, the more we need to use term repos.	92	9
201501	1306	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	I would note that I do not see a financial-stability preference for term reverse repos over overnight reverse repos.	92	9
201501	1307	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	Term reverse repos would also likely be transacted primarily with money market funds.	92	9
201501	1308	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	They do expand our footprint, and they lock us into longer periods than may be advisable.	92	9
201501	1309	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	They will also be more expensive than overnight reverse repos.	92	9
201501	1310	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	The memos seem to imply that caps supplemented with term reverse repos will result in a lower risk of financial stability than a program with only overnight reverse repos.	92	9
201501	1311	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	I’d like to understand this argument better.	92	9
201501	1312	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	Finally, the strategy of using term reverse repos prior to liftoff as a way of smoothing the withdrawal of reserves seems like an unusual strategy, because the higher rate announced on term reverse repos would, in effect, be the action of lifting off.	92	9
201501	1313	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	In terms of part c of the question, if the Committee is willing to proceed without a cap at the outset, then there is not much advantage to making other adjustments.	92	9
201501	1314	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	In contrast, if we are going to cap the reverse repo at liftoff, we will need to make flexible use of term reverse repos.	92	9
201501	1315	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	However, because I do not find the financial-stability concerns significantly reduced by lengthening the maturity of reverse repos, and because they are more costly, using term reverse repos to enable arbitrarily limiting the cap on overnight reverse repos seems suboptimal.	92	9
201501	1316	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	I do not see much benefit in narrowing the IOER–reverse repo spread or using term deposits, at least until we have obtained a better sense of the effectiveness of our initial move to liftoff.	92	9
201501	1317	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	One final point.	92	9
201501	1318	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	There has not been much discussion of how international flows would affect our liftoff.	92	9
201501	1319	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	With bank reserves in many countries receiving a negative interest rate, announcing an increase in our overnight risk-free rates may make reverse repos very attractive to foreign capital.	92	9
201501	1320	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	Better understanding that dynamic would be useful.	92	9
201501	1321	2015-01-28	meeting	ROSENGREN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201501	1322	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	92	9

201501	1327	2015-01-28	meeting	LOCKHART	When we first discussed the overnight reverse repo proposal at the July meeting, I had more confidence than some others in the power of the interest on excess reserves as a tool of monetary control, much like President Lacker’s sentiments.	92	9
201501	1328	2015-01-28	meeting	LOCKHART	The consensus of the Committee has gravitated to the view that a smooth liftoff is paramount, and I accept that and I consider that to be the starting point for discussion of the questions presented for this round.	92	9
201501	1329	2015-01-28	meeting	LOCKHART	All things considered, for planning purposes, I think smooth-liftoff considerations trump more speculative concerns about financial stability at the point of implementation of the liftoff decision and the near-term aftermath.	92	9
201501	1330	2015-01-28	meeting	LOCKHART	As a practical matter, financial stability concerns are not likely to be center stage at the time we would choose to lift off.	92	9
201501	1331	2015-01-28	meeting	LOCKHART	Today I am reacting to the questions posed to this go-round in general terms without stating definite preferences regarding configuration details.	92	9

201501	1333	2015-01-28	meeting	LOCKHART	Specifically, I would appreciate hearing more about an exit plan for the reverse repo tool.	92	9
201501	1334	2015-01-28	meeting	LOCKHART	This would address both the need for reverse repo programs as normalization proceeds and the potential methods of phasing out the programs.	92	9
201501	1335	2015-01-28	meeting	LOCKHART	At the back of my mind is the concern that once liftoff has been accomplished with a facility larger, say, than the current $300 billion, it will be difficult to argue that continuing with a large program is not required for exactly the reasons we are considering a larger program now, and that is uncertainty about monetary control with a smaller program.	92	9
201501	1336	2015-01-28	meeting	LOCKHART	On the question of other possible adjustments, again, I’d like to hear more discussion, and I could get more comfortable, but at this point I’m disinclined to favor using spread tightening and relative range adjustments unless clearly needed to correct a situation of demonstrated inadequate control.	92	9
201501	1337	2015-01-28	meeting	LOCKHART	I also think this type of tactical option has to be looked at in light of exit ease or difficulty.	92	9
201501	1338	2015-01-28	meeting	LOCKHART	So if I had my druthers, I would use the March meeting to refine and come to closure on the detailed implementation plan and the guidelines for the use of tools informed by more thinking on how reverse repo programs would ultimately be phased out.	92	9
201501	1339	2015-01-28	meeting	LOCKHART	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9

201501	1343	2015-01-28	meeting	MESTER	I think it’s very important that at liftoff we demonstrate that we have the necessary tools to move short-term interest rates up and into our target range.	92	9
201501	1344	2015-01-28	meeting	MESTER	Unlike some of the speakers so far, I have a slight preference for using the term RRPs in conjunction with the overnight RRPs rather than raising the size of the overnight facility too high.	92	9
201501	1345	2015-01-28	meeting	MESTER	At the margin, I prefer a smaller facility to help limit risk to financial stability, and I guess I see the term RRPs as having slightly less risk in that respect.	92	9

201501	1352	2015-01-28	meeting	MESTER	The testing to date has provided some good information suggesting that a $600 billion combined capacity of term and overnight RRPs may give us enough control of interest rates.	92	9
201501	1353	2015-01-28	meeting	MESTER	But I think we need to remember that what works in a testing environment may not work as well in production.	92	9
201501	1354	2015-01-28	meeting	MESTER	We need to be prepared to make necessary adjustments along the way and be open to using different combinations of our tools.	92	9
201501	1355	2015-01-28	meeting	MESTER	We might decide we prefer heavier use of term RRPs rather than an even larger overnight facility.	92	9
201501	1356	2015-01-28	meeting	MESTER	We are going to gain information as we begin liftoff.	92	9
201501	1357	2015-01-28	meeting	MESTER	I wouldn’t rule out dynamic caps on overnight RRPs, narrowing the spread between the IOER and the overnight RRP rate, or using term deposits, although I don’t see a need to start there.	92	9
201501	1358	2015-01-28	meeting	MESTER	No matter what approach we take, the communication explaining what we’re doing and why we’re doing it is going to be, perhaps, nearly as important as the actual approach.	92	9
201501	1359	2015-01-28	meeting	MESTER	We should give the markets and the public an outline of the approach we’re using, but be clear that some things are unknowable in advance and that aspects may very well need to be adjusted as we go.	92	9
201501	1360	2015-01-28	meeting	MESTER	We said this in our normalization principles, and it is probably worth reiterating at liftoff.	92	9

201501	1363	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	President Plosser.	92	9
201501	1364	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201501	1365	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	A smooth liftoff is desirable for establishing confidence in the ability of the FOMC to normalize the conduct of monetary policy.	92	9
201501	1366	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	I think we all agree with that.	92	9
201501	1367	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	By smooth, I mean a liftoff in which the funds rate trades somewhere between IOER and the ON RRP rate on a fairly consistent basis.	92	9
201501	1368	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	That does not mean every moment of every day.	92	9
201501	1369	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	Whether those trades are near the midpoint or not of the range is also not important, as far as I’m concerned, and we should not suggest that that’s part of our objective.	92	9
201501	1370	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	In this regard, I would be comfortable starting off with a somewhat generous cap and a spread of 25 basis points between the IOER rate and the ON RRP.	92	9
201501	1371	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	However, I also would be comfortable with a smaller cap and a larger spread or range.	92	9
201501	1372	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	This is a tradeoff along these dimensions of program design that really exists, but it depends on the Committee’s tolerance for volatility of the effective funds rate.	92	9
201501	1373	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	I probably have a greater tolerance for that volatility than some in this regard, but I think it’s a discussion worth continuing to have.	92	9
201501	1374	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	Regarding cap size, research done by my staff indicates that the $400 billion cap would probably be sufficient.	92	9
201501	1375	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	As rates rise, the federal funds market should be able to absorb a substantial portion of any increase in the supply of funds.	92	9
201501	1376	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	I would also note that in our experiments to date, even at the quarter-ends, the $400 billion cap has been pretty close to being sufficient, and those are pretty good experiments.	92	9
201501	1377	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	But I also wouldn’t mind a $600 billion cap.	92	9
201501	1378	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	However, accompanying the announcement of whatever the size of our cap is, I believe it is crucial for us to reemphasize that the ON RRP facility is intended to be temporary and that we will reduce its size if circumstances allow.	92	9
201501	1379	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	Indeed, perhaps by starting with the somewhat larger cap, say the $600 billion, like in option 1, we could get through quarter-end in June, and maybe for a few weeks, and then actually announce that it’s going to be smaller because it doesn’t need to be.	92	9
201501	1380	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	And so that first directional change in the size of the cap might be useful and important to get us started and to signal to the market that we really do intend to shrink this facility.	92	9
201501	1381	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	I also agree with the Chair that we should keep things as simple as possible.	92	9
201501	1382	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	In particular, operating with two instruments, the IOER and the ON RRP, should be sufficient for normalization.	92	9
201501	1383	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	I’m leery of the complexity of other policy tools, particularly the term RRPs.	92	9
201501	1384	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	Term RRPs have more moving parts; we are less certain of their effectiveness and the substitutability they have with the overnight RRPs.	92	9
201501	1385	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	I do not favor us getting into the business of complicated financial engineering.	92	9
201501	1386	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	Too many policy tools that operate along too many different margins are liable to confuse us as well as the markets, with relatively little benefit.	92	9
201501	1387	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	Dealing with more margins also opens the door for a wide range of unintended consequences when it comes to the longer-term ramifications for market structure, something this Committee has expressed concern about.	92	9
201501	1388	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	While I could imagine a term RRP facility that would primarily serve to help smooth window-dressing-induced funds volatility at the end of quarters, I’m dubious of this benefit and would be inclined to oppose it.	92	9
201501	1389	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	In other words, doing something separate at the end of quarters seems to me to draw attention to it rather than just making the cap on overnight RRPs large enough to accommodate at least in the first instance.	92	9
201501	1390	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	This type of year-end or quarter-end volatility is self-induced by reporting practices and the efforts of firms to report balance sheets that may not truly be representative of their average positions.	92	9
201501	1391	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	I see no reason for us to care or to be complicit in subsidizing this behavior.	92	9
201501	1392	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	Let the firms pay the price for this practice if they are inclined to do so.	92	9
201501	1393	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	It is unlikely to have any material effect on macroeconomic performance or our goals and objectives.	92	9
201501	1394	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	It is just too transitory.	92	9
201501	1395	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	It would serve us well at the outset to be explicit about this perspective up front to avoid having market participants expect us to intervene on these occasions.	92	9
201501	1396	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	And once we set up separate term RRPs just for the quarter-end—once we do that once—the expectation is going to be set and it’s going to be hard to unwind from that.	92	9
201501	1397	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	More generally, I’m simply not concerned about infrequent or occasional volatility that leads the funds rate to trade above or below our target range.	92	9
201501	1398	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	We were asked about what things could help during this normalization.	92	9
201501	1399	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	I would remind us that we are facing these operational issues surrounding liftoff because we have a very large balance sheet.	92	9
201501	1400	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	In view of the uncertainty we face going forward during normalization, I think it would be helpful if we would begin reducing the size of the balance sheet and, thus, the quantity of excess reserves that we have to deal with in these circumstances.	92	9
201501	1401	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	We could easily begin by immediately ceasing to reinvest maturing principal payments.	92	9
201501	1402	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	And as we saw in the Desk report, the prospects for ever-larger purchases of MBS just to solve our reinvestment problem is going to get bigger rather than smaller over time.	92	9
201501	1403	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	So I see now might be a good time to stop that, so that we don’t have to intervene even more.	92	9
201501	1404	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	I see very little cost or risk in taking such a step.	92	9
201501	1405	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	The sooner we start, the sooner we’ll arrive at a situation in which we can start reducing the size of the ON RRP facility and return to business as usual.	92	9
201501	1406	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	Only then will we achieve full normalization.	92	9
201501	1407	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201501	1408	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	92	9
201501	1409	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	President Bullard.	92	9
201501	1410	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201501	1411	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	I have three remarks and a general conclusion.	92	9
201501	1412	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	The general conclusion is that I support the use of a temporarily larger cap on the overnight reverse repo program at the time of liftoff, along the lines of option 1.	92	9
201501	1413	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	I also support the use of term repos in sizes viewed as helpful during this period.	92	9
201501	1414	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	My three remarks concern the following areas.	92	9
201501	1415	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	One, the likely timing and source of possible market volatility impinging on federal funds rate control.	92	9
201501	1416	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	Two, the risk of financial instability associated with a larger overnight reverse repo program than presently contemplated.	92	9
201501	1417	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	And, three, the size of the Federal Reserve footprint in financial markets.	92	9
201501	1418	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	Considering the first area, the likely timing and source of possible market volatility, the memoranda for this meeting touching on this subject seemed to suggest that the date of liftoff is special with respect to the possible implications for market volatility, and, therefore, for control of the federal funds rate.	92	9
201501	1419	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	It is possible, however, that market volatility may not be especially high at liftoff versus other times.	92	9
201501	1420	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	This may be especially true if we telegraph our date of liftoff fairly accurately, as we seem destined to do.	92	9
201501	1421	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	The memo on initialization of normalization cycles in foreign countries suggested that the liftoff itself was often not a moment of confusion and volatility in financial markets, but that when such moments occurred they were often at some other critical juncture in the normalization process.	92	9
201501	1422	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	Indeed, financial market volatility is more likely to be caused by a violent reconciliation of a mismatch between financial market expectations of monetary policy and Committee intentions.	92	9
201501	1423	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	We have a grand example of such a reconciliation in the so-called taper tantrum during the summer of 2013.	92	9
201501	1424	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	That episode did not involve raising rates, nor did it even involve any actual change in the pace of excess purchases.	92	9
201501	1425	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	We do have considerable mismatch today, arguably, based on differences in the Committee intentions as suggested by the SEP versus market expectations as suggested by futures markets trading, as outlined in the staff memo relating to this subject.	92	9
201501	1426	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	When and how this mismatch will be resolved remains an open question at this point, but potentially any reconciliation could involve substantial market volatility and could occur at a point in the normalization cycle other than the liftoff date itself.	92	9
201501	1427	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	These considerations suggest that use of a higher cap or other method to mitigate any risk should not be confined only to the time period around liftoff.	92	9
201501	1428	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	For this reason, I would advocate expanding the notion of “temporary” to include most of the normalization period and not just the time around liftoff.	92	9
201501	1429	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	The second area I wish to address is the nexus between the size of the overnight reverse repo program and the risks of financial instability.	92	9
201501	1430	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	In discussions with my staff, I have concluded that I simply do not think we have a credible and compelling story concerning the nature of this risk sufficient to suggest that a $600 billion program is more risky than a $300 billion program in a meaningful way.	92	9
201501	1431	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	For this reason, I lean toward a larger program and the tangible benefits that that may bring with respect to our normalization policy.	92	9
201501	1432	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	The third area I wanted to comment on concerns the Federal Reserve’s footprint in financial markets, which some wish to keep to a minimum.	92	9
201501	1433	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	Normally, I would find this a reasonable goal, but in the current situation I think we are already such a large player in financial markets that we may be better advised to manage our risk carefully rather than to try to keep our interventions to a minimum.	92	9
201501	1434	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	For this reason, I again come down on the side of using available tools to our advantage in securing a successful liftoff.	92	9
201501	1435	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201501	1436	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	92	9
201501	1437	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	President George.	92	9
201501	1438	2015-01-28	meeting	GEORGE	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201501	1439	2015-01-28	meeting	GEORGE	As I weigh these issues, I view a lack of control over short-term rates at liftoff as an unlikely but a very costly event and one to be avoided.	92	9
201501	1440	2015-01-28	meeting	GEORGE	So I, too, favor option 1, as outlined by the staff.	92	9
201501	1441	2015-01-28	meeting	GEORGE	The testing experience of the overnight RRP and our communication of policy normalization principles and plans give me confidence that the overnight RRP, on a temporary basis, can be an effective way to support rates at liftoff, if necessary, but also to temper the financial stability issues associated with its use.	92	9
201501	1442	2015-01-28	meeting	GEORGE	If needed, I would also support the use of term RRPs after liftoff to ensure the funds rate trades in our targeted range.	92	9
201501	1443	2015-01-28	meeting	GEORGE	In terms of the other possible adjustments that were outlined in the memo, I support maintaining a wide spread between IOER and the ON RRP rate, along with a sufficiently large cap that rarely binds, as well as using term deposits.	92	9
201501	1444	2015-01-28	meeting	GEORGE	I’d prefer keeping the option of adjusting the IOER and the ON RRP band or narrowing the spread between these two rates.	92	9
201501	1445	2015-01-28	meeting	GEORGE	This approach is to be used only after liftoff and only in the event that the federal funds rate fails to trade within our targeted range.	92	9
201501	1446	2015-01-28	meeting	GEORGE	Thank you.	92	9
201501	1447	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	92	9
201501	1448	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	President Williams.	92	9
201501	1449	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201501	1450	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	To best achieve our mandated goals, it is crucial that we’re able to maintain effective monetary control at the time of liftoff and throughout the normalization process.	92	9
201501	1451	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Equally important, we must leave no doubt in the public’s mind that we have effective control over interest rates during this period when all eyes will be on the Federal Reserve.	92	9
201501	1452	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	I’ve been taking notes to see if I’ve got the whole list right, but basically my remaining comments echo very much those of Presidents Evans, Lacker, Rosengren, and Bullard, which is for sure the first time I’ve ever said that.	92	9
201501	1453	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	[Laughter]	92	9
201501	1454	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	And President George, too, actually.	92	9
201501	1455	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Our communications regarding policy normalization or testing of different facilities have helped prepare market participants.	92	9
201501	1456	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	We’ve consistently assured the public that we have the tools to raise rates when needed.	92	9
201501	1457	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	We’ve explained the broad outlines of how we will use these tools.	92	9
201501	1458	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	In looking ahead, we really need to minimize the risk of any missteps coming out of the gate that could raise concerns about the effectiveness of our tools to keep the funds rate in its target range.	92	9
201501	1459	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Indeed, demonstrating monetary control when we start normalization will increase market confidence in our ability to steer the economy, reduce market volatility, and facilitate the pursuit of our objectives.	92	9
201501	1460	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	And I view the approach described in option 1 as most likely to achieve this outcome.	92	9
201501	1461	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	I want to remind everyone that we made clear in our policy principles and plans back in September that we will primarily use the IOER rate to move the federal funds rate into the relative target range, and the overnight reverse repo facility supplements it as needed to increase monetary control.	92	9
201501	1462	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Importantly, we also indicated that the reverse repo facility will be phased out when it’s no longer needed to help control the federal funds rate.	92	9
201501	1463	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	So we’ve already told everybody that this will be temporary and will only be used as needed.	92	9
201501	1464	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	I therefore view option 1 as entirely consistent with the strategy that we’ve laid out.	92	9
201501	1465	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	It keeps the approach as clear and simple as possible.	92	9
201501	1466	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	And one issue, of course, is the size of the cap on the repo facility, and I, like many of the others, have difficulty in saying, you know, it’s $400, $600, $800, $1 trillion.	92	9
201501	1467	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	What are the costs in terms of financial stability and the benefits there?	92	9
201501	1468	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	I think it’s really impossible to judge ex ante the optimal size of the facility and the tradeoffs between financial stability, footprint issues, and effectiveness.	92	9
201501	1469	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Now, I do think that the analysis that’s been done so far suggests that what is really important is that we have sufficient headroom for this to be effective, and in my own view it would be prudent to set a cap that’s significantly high.	92	9
201501	1470	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	I thought the $600 billion would be viewed by this group as already pretty high, but clearly people have suggested even higher might be optimal.	92	9
201501	1471	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	And I’m going to make kind of a nuanced point.	92	9
201501	1472	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	I don’t see this as raising the cap—and this actually gets back to President Lacker’s point earlier.	92	9
201501	1473	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	When we did the testing of $300 billion, that was clearly stated not to be our policy decision of how big the overnight reverse repo facility was going to be.	92	9
201501	1474	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	This is not raising it from $300 billion to $600 billion.	92	9
201501	1475	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	This is just setting what it will be initially, whatever that number is.	92	9
201501	1476	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	So I would prefer not to communicate this as saying that we’re raising this in some way.	92	9
201501	1477	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	We’re setting the cap at the level that is the most appropriate to achieve monetary control, and, of course, as time goes on and we learn more, we can reduce the cap as appropriate.	92	9
201501	1478	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	And, again, I don’t see the risk to financial stability or regarding footprint issues to be that significant.	92	9
201501	1479	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	This is a temporary program.	92	9
201501	1480	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	We’ve indicated that, and we will reduce it and phase it out as appropriate.	92	9
201501	1481	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	I’m confident that, under option 1, we have the necessary tools to maintain monetary control during the normalization period.	92	9
201501	1482	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	I really think that this is an appropriate option when viewed in terms of our basic strategy.	92	9
201501	1483	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	It’s simple, and I think it follows the plans and principles we laid out.	92	9
201501	1484	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	On the other issues, in terms of spreads, I agree, like others, that with a wide spread initially, as we discussed, I would only see adjusting the spread of the IOER and the overnight reverse repo rates as something you would only do if it was necessary, if the other tools that we were using weren’t working.	92	9
201501	1485	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	I see the TDF as always a backup facility—again, there to support if needed.	92	9
201501	1486	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	In terms of testing the term reverse repo facility, I am in favor of continuing the test for March.	92	9
201501	1487	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	I think that there is an open question about the value of further testing of a daily or a regular term reverse repo facility as, again, another backstop.	92	9
201501	1488	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	So we’re now talking about belts and suspenders, more belts, more suspenders.	92	9
201501	1489	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	I do think if you were to test it too extensively, it would lead people to think this is something we were going to use, and something to think about, although I don’t see any problems with the testing around the quarter-end because I think that, to me, would be limited.	92	9
201501	1490	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	I do think I’m not opposed to the further testing of the term reverse repo, but again, I think it just creates some additional communication challenges for us.	92	9
201501	1491	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	I think IOER is our first line of defense.	92	9
201501	1492	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Overnight reverse repo with a sizable cap is the support, and then we have these other tools behind.	92	9
201501	1493	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	It is already pretty complicated.	92	9

201501	1538	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	That promise was made for good reasons.	92	9
201501	1539	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	We shouldn’t take lightly actions that might lead the public and financial institutions to doubt our intention to honor it.	92	9
201501	1540	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	I believe under the previous Chairman I actually quoted my mother—who I think stole it from Kierkegaard or maybe Santayana, and certainly not from the Kardashians—on the following:  “Skepticism is the chastity of the intellect, and it needs to be carefully guarded before it’s surrendered.”	92	9
201501	1541	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	[Laughter]	92	9
201501	1542	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201501	1543	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	I won’t tell you what she said after that, but—okay, after that she said, “And then have a lot of fun,” but that’s a separate thing.	92	9
201501	1544	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	I do think there is some skepticism in the marketplace about the temporary nature of this facility, and here’s why I mention this.	92	9
201501	1545	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	We can throw out numbers like $1 trillion or $600 billion.	92	9
201501	1546	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	However, I think we have to be very careful about whatever number we choose and not be indiscriminate with a large number because it might undermine the confidence that this is a temporary facility and, again, indicate that we’re not so chaste in the use of this facility.	92	9
201501	1547	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	I would be very, very careful about throwing out numbers.	92	9
201501	1548	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	My second point is—I think President Lockhart makes an excellent suggestion—I don’t know how we do it, but we should at least have in our own mind what the exit strategy should be for using the program.	92	9
201501	1549	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	In summary, I would prefer to start with an ON RRP program, maybe $600 billion but no larger.	92	9
201501	1550	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	I’d supplement with term RRPs at quarter-ends, perhaps term deposits, and only move to a more aggressive use of RRPs if it’s critical to maintain the floor.	92	9
201501	1551	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	And I’d be very careful in using it in any way that would undermine the confidence of the markets that this is a temporary facility.	92	9
201501	1552	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	With regard to term RRPs, I understand from our discussion today that there are pros and cons, but they could be close substitutes, and we have established a precedent of engaging in term RRP operations at times when there is predictable temporary increase in demand for safe short-term assets.	92	9
201501	1553	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	If liftoff occurs near the quarter-end, as seems likely, it would be perfectly natural for us to auction term RRPs coincident with liftoff and spanning the quarter-end.	92	9
201501	1554	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	If the maturity dates on term RRPs are staggered, we’ll have a chance to see how overnight rates respond as the term RRPs roll off, and we can decide, depending on that response, whether the current cap on ON RRP operations are too small, additional RRPs need to be auctioned, or term deposits should be offered at a premium over the IOER rate.	92	9
201501	1555	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	One of the things that caught my eye in the memo was a suggestion of a 5 basis point increase in the ON RRP rate relative to the lower end of the target range for the federal funds rate.	92	9
201501	1556	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	I was discussing this with Governor Brainard.	92	9
201501	1557	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	I understand that might be a short-term tactic, but I feel pretty strongly that we should maintain the 25 basis point spread between ON RRP and the IOER rates—and we should be careful that, as we go through time, I would suggest we perhaps use that spread as a way to limit demand for RRP.	92	9
201501	1558	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	So I can see widening it.	92	9
201501	1559	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	I don’t like the idea of temporarily shortening it, because I think it may undermine our commitment to widening it over time.	92	9
201501	1560	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	I may be wrong.	92	9
201501	1561	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	And then last, with regard to term RRPs, again, I mentioned that I think it would be a useful tool at quarter-end.	92	9
201501	1562	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	There was a number of $200 billion somewhere.	92	9
201501	1563	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	Why not do $300 billion?	92	9
201501	1564	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	In other words, why not keep an extra $100 billion on hand in case we need to have it?	92	9

201501	1570	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Vice Chairman Dudley.	92	9
201501	1571	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201501	1572	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	For me, just like everybody else, having a smooth liftoff is my top priority.	92	9
201501	1573	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	That’s more important than the size of the facility or the potential financial stability concerns.	92	9
201501	1574	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	First of all, over a very short period of time, when our credibility with respect to liftoff will either be won or lost, the financial-stability risks are pretty small.	92	9
201501	1575	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	Also, I think we can address the issue of footprint by making it clear that this overnight RRP facility will be used only to the extent needed to maintain monetary policy control, and when it’s not needed, it will be phased out.	92	9
201501	1576	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	It’s temporary, not permanent.	92	9
201501	1577	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	With respect to the options in the memo, I think it’s essential that we have sufficient headroom, and I think there’s a lot of ways to generate sufficient headroom.	92	9
201501	1578	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	You can have a very large overnight RRP facility or you can have a somewhat smaller overnight RRP facility supplemented by term RRP.	92	9
201501	1579	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	As long as there’s sufficient headroom and this expectation is realized, then I think the facilities are likely to be effective in putting a floor under short-term rates.	92	9
201501	1580	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	We have been talking about a lot of details over the past couple of hours, but I think we should get some confidence from the tests that we’ve done.	92	9
201501	1581	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	I mean, the tests do seem to suggest that these facilities actually do work in terms of putting a floor under short-term rates.	92	9
201501	1582	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	In terms of the split between overnight RRP and term RRP, I think the simplest solution is just to go with option 1 and have a high cap initially on the overnight RRP facility or no cap at all.	92	9
201501	1583	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	The advantage of having a high cap, a cap that they are not going to reach, is to signal that this is not unlimited, and it allows you then to move the cap down as you see that you have a lot of extra headroom.	92	9
201501	1584	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	You can then move that cap down in order to reinforce the message that this thing is going to go away over time.	92	9
201501	1585	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	If you decided that you wanted to have term RRPs, I think the way I would do it is I would have term RRPs that just address quarter-end, and I would have a testing program for term RRPs in place for the June quarter and the September quarter.	92	9
201501	1586	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	So if you lifted off in June or you lifted off in September, you wouldn’t even really have to announce the term RRPs.	92	9
201501	1587	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	They are to be tested.	92	9
201501	1588	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	The tested RRPs would just turn into the actual term RRPs.	92	9
201501	1589	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	In looking at the increase in demand over quarter-end, what you see is about a $200 billion increase in demand over quarter-end.	92	9
201501	1590	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	So that would suggest that if you had a term RRP program of $200 billion, you could have that tested in June, September, et cetera.	92	9
201501	1591	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	You could just roll right into it if you actually happened to lift off in the quarter, and if you didn’t lift off in the quarter, you’re just doing another test.	92	9
201501	1592	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	That, to me, has the advantage of it all being announced ex ante.	92	9
201501	1593	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	There’s no surprises to the market in terms of what you’re going to do.	92	9
201501	1594	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	If you roll it out after the fact, you’re just inserting more noise into the market that you’re going to have to communicate about.	92	9
201501	1595	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	In terms of other steps to ensure a smooth liftoff, I think that we all agree that good communication is important.	92	9
201501	1596	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	I think what I would hope that we could do is reach a consensus in March about how this is all going to work and then have the Chair communicate that to the markets or communicate that in speeches or the minutes.	92	9
201501	1597	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	I think there is broad enough consensus here that I think we could get to something in March where we could sort of tell the markets what we’re doing prior to liftoff.	92	9
201501	1598	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	Regarding term RRP testing away from quarter-end, I’m fine with it if we’re actually going to do it.	92	9
201501	1599	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	But if the sense of the Committee is that we’re not going to do term RRP away from quarter-end, then I sort of ask myself the question, why are we testing it?	92	9
201501	1600	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	I think we just have to ask ourselves.	92	9
201501	1601	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	I don’t think we should test things that we’re not going to do because I think that just confuses markets and starts to influence their expectations.	92	9
201501	1602	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9

201501	1612	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	The reason I say that is because I don’t know whether this is just reacting to words, but I’m not sure we should be encouraging firms to window-dress by making it cheaper for them to window-dress, and that’s what the term RRP does.	92	9
201501	1613	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	I’m interested in when we are going to become independent of the ON RRP, and I think we’re very optimistic if we think we can describe the scenarios under which we are going to exit.	92	9
201501	1614	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	It is going to take a while until we get the balance sheet down to $1 trillion, at which point I guess we’ll start possibly becoming able to see an end to this program, unless there is something we’re missing about President Lacker’s position—namely, that we could do it all by IOER.	92	9
201501	1615	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	And maybe there is something that says: that’s not true at $4 trillion, but it is true at $3½ trillion.	92	9

201501	1620	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	The last point, again, is just to support the need for explaining what we’re going to do— preparing answers to frequently asked questions, et cetera—so that even people who are not engaged in buying and selling these things know what it is that we’re going to do.	92	9
201501	1621	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	There are probably tens of millions of American citizens who learned about open market operations in their economics textbooks and have trouble figuring out what on earth all this is about.	92	9

201501	1626	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Governor Tarullo.	92	9
201501	1627	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201501	1628	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	I began this exercise, whenever we started talking about it months ago, with a strong set of financial stability concerns, which, unlike many of you, have not abated during the course of these discussions.	92	9
201501	1629	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	But it has become apparent to me over time—and I think part of today’s discussion was a reaffirmation of this point—that the financial-stability difference between just ON RRP and a mix of ON RRP and term RRP is probably not that great relative to my source of concerns.	92	9
201501	1630	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	And I think President Lockhart and President Kocherlakota have put their finger on the source of my concerns, which is, as President Lockhart put it, an exit plan.	92	9
201501	1631	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	And I guess I disagree with Governor Fischer.	92	9
201501	1632	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	I think we’d better think about an exit plan for a reason I’ll explain in a minute.	92	9
201501	1633	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	There are two ways that things could go here.	92	9
201501	1634	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	One, with a large-ish ON RRP, we begin liftoff at some point in the future, and it turns out that things go pretty smoothly, and the take-up is nowhere near the cap—if there is a cap—that we’ve put in place.	92	9
201501	1635	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	And as President Plosser suggested, at the next meeting we can reduce the cap without any concerns about what happens.	92	9
201501	1636	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	A powerful message will be sent to the money market fund industry and, indeed, to everybody else.	92	9
201501	1637	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	The other scenario is one in which it turns out that there is substantial take-up.	92	9
201501	1638	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	And in subsequent meetings, there is still concern that—as Narayana was suggesting—in the absence of the continued use of a very large ON RRP, there may be some difficulty in getting within the target range, or at least in having confidence that we’ll be within the target range.	92	9
201501	1639	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	It seems to me that this is the scenario to worry about.	92	9
201501	1640	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	I don’t know what the probabilities are regarding that scenario.	92	9
201501	1641	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	I don’t know that anybody could say with any great assurance even the order of magnitude for what the probabilities are, but I think they’re nontrivial.	92	9
201501	1642	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	And here is where the question of, as Dennis put it, the exit plan comes into play, because I think what we confront is a variant of a time-consistency problem: That is, at any given meeting, it always seems like the best thing is to make sure you hit the range with confidence with a big ON RRP facility, and any financial stability issue is speculative.	92	9
201501	1643	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	It’s not around right now, of course, and is probably for tomorrow’s Committee, not even the members who are on the Committee right now.	92	9
201501	1644	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	This is precisely why, in general, policymakers pay more attention to short-term issues and why long-term problems often don’t get addressed—because of the decision pressures that we all face.	92	9
201501	1645	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	So I think, under those circumstances, there are two ways to deal with those longer-range contingencies.	92	9
201501	1646	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	One, which I’m going to come back to in a second, is some variant on a commitment device—that is, sort of an ex ante approach.	92	9
201501	1647	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	The second is having more options as you go forward, a kind of ex post approach.	92	9
201501	1648	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	Several people have already stated why, notwithstanding their preference for option 1, they think it might be a good idea to continue to investigate, through testing and otherwise, other tools that may be available, and I would agree with them.	92	9
201501	1649	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	So my instinct would be to let the Desk test anything it thinks might be useful at some point to give us as an option.	92	9
201501	1650	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	With respect to the first way—that is, the commitment device—the only thing I have heard, and I have heard it from almost everybody who has spoken to this point, “Well, we said it’s temporary.”	92	9
201501	1651	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	Well, you know, this is what a time-consistency problem is defined by.	92	9
201501	1652	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	You have a stated policy, which of course is the preference.	92	9
201501	1653	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	But when you come to the point of making the decision, it turns out that that gets trumped by the shorter-term considerations, and that at some point other actors begin to figure out that that’s the circumstance you’re in.	92	9
201501	1654	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	So stating that something is temporary, I don’t think, in and of itself, can be hugely reassuring, even though it helps, and there is no question that it is better to say it and to say it repeatedly than not to say it.	92	9
201501	1655	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	But I do think that other kinds of commitment devices should at least be thought about: for example, whether there is some way to tie the maximum size of an ON RRP over time, even to the balance sheet, which may not change for quite some time, so that at least there would be a clear ending point.	92	9
201501	1656	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	I don’t know what other ideas there are, and I think Governor Fischer is right in suggesting it’s going to be hard to come up with them.	92	9
201501	1657	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	But I’m left quite uncomfortable just relying on our saying, “Well, it’s temporary.”	92	9
201501	1658	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	And I heard many people say, “As appropriate, we would bring it down,” or “As possible, we would bring it down.”	92	9
201501	1659	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	Well, what if that decision still seems a hard one?	92	9
201501	1660	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	It then becomes hard to bring it down.	92	9
201501	1661	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	The problem with a commitment device is that, of course, it puts a constraint on discretion.	92	9
201501	1662	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	That’s the definition of a commitment device.	92	9
201501	1663	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	But you’ve got to do it.	92	9
201501	1664	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	If you don’t do it, and you’re not willing to do it ex ante to some degree, then it suggests to me that we’re not putting any value on financial stability considerations, which I think is different from saying we put dominant value on the precision of the monetary policy execution but are still placing some value on financial stability considerations.	92	9
201501	1665	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	As I say, I can’t value it, but it does seem to me that we don’t want to have our children or somebody looking back at some point and saying, “You know, the Fed just slipped into this.	92	9
201501	1666	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	At every point, it was easier to make that decision.	92	9
201501	1667	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	They allowed this industry to get started, and then what happened?	92	9
201501	1668	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	There was a major run circumstance in which everybody ran to the Fed, and their successors were sitting there saying, ‘We’d better increase the ON RRP.	92	9
201501	1669	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	Otherwise, there’s financial instability.’”	92	9
201501	1670	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	So that’s why, whether you call it a decision tree as President Fisher suggests, or President Lockhart’s exit plan, or just gaming it through—I think which was what Narayana was suggesting—I do hope that we can think more about this between now and March and see whether we can get beyond mere words with something ex ante, then allow Simon and Lorie to test a bunch of stuff that may help us develop some ex post options as needed later on.	92	9
201501	1671	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9

201501	1689	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	Again, if it’s thought through a bit beforehand, and it’s communicated, including to the public, you then begin to alter the lay of the land, and maybe you are creating a soft commitment device.	92	9
201501	1690	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	But that’s really what I’m calling for, not just relying on the fact that at some point in the future we’ll think better of it.	92	9
201501	1691	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Vice Chairman.	92	9
201501	1692	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	My conception is very similar to that of President Williams in terms of having these other tools.	92	9
201501	1693	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	And if you don’t like the tradeoff that you find after liftoff, you can adjust these other tools in a way to achieve a better tradeoff.	92	9
201501	1694	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	I think in terms of the simplicity/complexity argument, simplicity at liftoff is particularly important.	92	9
201501	1695	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	And after liftoff, I think you can introduce more complexity if you want to set the tradeoffs at a different place than you do in liftoff.	92	9
201501	1696	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	So I would distinguish liftoff, in terms of the need for simplicity at liftoff, from later, when I think you could have different tradeoffs.	92	9
201501	1697	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	I know everybody has done that, Vice Chairman Dudley, but I don’t quite understand why that’s so—why I should believe or why any of us should believe that we are really going to feel that way.	92	9
201501	1698	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	I mean, maybe we will, but—	92	9
201501	1699	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	If we truly don’t like the tradeoffs, why wouldn’t we pick some other parameters to adjust to get to a better place?	92	9
201501	1700	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	What I was suggesting is the calculus of a tradeoff at any given moment will weigh heavily toward as precise an execution of one’s monetary policy objectives as one can achieve.	92	9
201501	1701	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	And, thus, other norms, just as now I think they are being pushed—not obliterated, and nobody denies them—but I think they are being downplayed now.	92	9
201501	1702	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	I think the same dynamic, psychological and otherwise, takes effect at any given point along the way.	92	9
201501	1703	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	And there is a very rational, logical reason why you should be right, which is to say that credibility having been established initially, we would all be more comfortable with more softness.	92	9
201501	1704	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	But I don’t know that that’s the way everyone, or even the majority, of the Committee, or some future Chair will feel about it.	92	9
201501	1705	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	So that’s why I think talking it through first and communicating upfront the way we’re thinking about it does, as I say, serve as a form of soft commitment device—not as hard of one as I would like, but at least a soft commitment device—as opposed to just telling ourselves, if we don’t like the tradeoff later, we can do it differently, but not getting beyond that.	92	9
201501	1706	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	I don’t think there is any disagreement conceptually with what the options are.	92	9
201501	1707	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	I’m just thinking in terms of institutional dynamics.	92	9

201501	1769	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Governor Brainard.	92	9
201501	1770	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201501	1771	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	We are in quite unique circumstances.	92	9
201501	1772	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	Monetary policy has now been at the lower bound for about six years, and we have excess reserves at a level that we have never dealt with before.	92	9
201501	1773	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	So at this very unique moment, it’s of paramount importance to demonstrate decisively that we can maintain the federal funds rate within the range that we target.	92	9
201501	1774	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	I think the failure to do so could potentially have long-term corrosive effects on the efficacy of our monetary policy.	92	9
201501	1775	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	Any initial inability to move the rate within its desired range, particularly if it persists for any period of time, would call into question that we have the tools or the will.	92	9
201501	1776	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	And the risk is amplified by the slight awkwardness of the timing.	92	9
201501	1777	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	The likeliest meetings for liftoff, which are those that coincide with a press conference, all happen to take place very close to quarter-end.	92	9
201501	1778	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	And they raise a specter of the liftoff announcement being followed immediately by a downward drift and a possible breach in the new floor.	92	9
201501	1779	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	Fortunately, we have already seen that we can have pretty strong confidence that we have the necessary tools well within our authority.	92	9
201501	1780	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	The use of the IOER in tandem with the reverse repo facility should provide the requisite monetary control if we set the cap on the reverse repo at a sufficient level to have high confidence in achieving that target.	92	9
201501	1781	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	Our experience so far with using that facility to impose a soft floor has been limited to periods in which the federal funds rate has been close to zero and, therefore, likely receiving some support from that threshold.	92	9
201501	1782	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	As rates move away from the zero bound, we should be prepared for the possibility that the amount of reverse repos that are needed to support that floor initially might increase temporarily.	92	9
201501	1783	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	We should also be prepared, as was suggested in the memo, to temporarily narrow the spread between the IOER and the RRP rates at the outset with a view that it will increase over time.	92	9
201501	1784	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	I agree with those who have said that they are less worried about the exact size of the increment in the cap.	92	9
201501	1785	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	The cap itself is less important as a safeguard against risks from the ON RRP to financial stability and changes to market structure than the perceived impermanence of this facility.	92	9
201501	1786	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	In terms of making sure that we don’t lead to a permanent change in market structure or introduce some risk of a flight to this market during periods of elevated stress, it is very important that we firmly commit that this facility will be temporary and used only for the extent and duration necessary.	92	9
201501	1787	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	I think apart from stating that very clearly at the outset, there are a number of ways that we talked about doing that around the table.	92	9
201501	1788	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	We will not be in these unique circumstances for very long, and we should see over time that the IOER rate starts to exert more of a pull on the federal funds rate and that it trades closer to IOER rate.	92	9
201501	1789	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	At that juncture, we’ll have the option to widen the spread and make the RRP rate much less attractive.	92	9
201501	1790	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	So there’s a natural potential exit path that I think we have talked about using, and I hope we will, in fact, use that along with some of the other tools.	92	9
201501	1791	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	So with those strong reservations about making sure that we are clear that this not a permanent addition to the structure of the short-term money market, I very much support option 1.	92	9

201501	1856	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	And it does have some issues related to how we describe it, as Governor Powell suggested, that there is some risk that people will take more signal from doing a test like this than we’d like.	92	9
201501	1857	2015-01-28	meeting	POTTER	That also suggests keeping it quite small.	92	9
201501	1858	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	Madam Chair, I just want to clarify my hand-raising here.	92	9
201501	1859	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	I’m not against testing things, because I want to have the best toolkit that we can possibly have, as long as it doesn’t send the wrong signal.	92	9

201501	1872	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	Yes, switching things up.	11	1
201501	1873	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	Because some of the key influences on the US economy’s prospects—especially oil prices and the dollar—are indeed emanating from the international sphere, David and I thought we would switch our usual order, with me going first.	11	1
201501	1874	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	I will be referring to the materials that are labeled “The Foreign Outlook.”	11	1
201501	1875	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	Before getting to oil prices and the dollar, I will address our forecast for foreign economic growth, shown as the black solid line in panel 1.	11	1
201501	1876	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	In putting together this forecast, we steered a middle course between giving in to the anxiety about prospects abroad evidenced in financial markets and succumbing to excessive enthusiasm about the positive effects of lower oil prices, weaker currencies, and more accommodative monetary policy.	11	1
201501	1877	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	As before, our forecast of foreign growth strengthening to its potential pace of about 3 percent rests on a number of difficult judgment calls.	11	1
201501	1878	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	First, in our projection, China’s economic growth declines only gradually in the next few years, from 7¼ percent in 2014 to 6¾ percent in 2017, and the country avoids sharp disruptions associated with the ongoing correction of its housing market.	11	1
201501	1879	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	Fourth-quarter GDP came in at 7 percent, a touch lower than our projection in December, and we marked down our outlook going forward by about ¼ percentage point, in part reflecting the appreciation of the renminbi that has occurred as the currency followed the dollar up.	11	1
201501	1880	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	Second, in our forecast, Brazil and other ailing economies in South America pull out of their recessions and eventually regain near-trend rates of growth.	11	1
201501	1881	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	The appointment by reelected Brazilian President Dilma Rousseff of a new, market- friendly economic team is encouraging, but the region faces critical challenges, and we’ve marked down the pace of the projected recovery.	11	1
201501	1882	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	Finally, our forecast of quickening growth depends on the euro-area economy shaking off its malaise.	11	1
201501	1883	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	Despite the doom and gloom of much commentary, a number of recent indicators came in stronger than expected, and we’ve marked up our fourth- quarter GDP estimate to 1 percent, roughly its current rate of potential growth.	11	1
201501	1884	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	Going forward, as shown by the solid black line in panel 2, GDP growth picks up to 2½ percent by 2017, driven, among other things, by the substantial monetary stimulus announced by the ECB last Thursday and described by Simon earlier today.	11	1
201501	1885	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	By our reckoning, the ECB’s prospective purchases of €300 billion in private assets and about €900 billion in public bonds—carried out through September 2016—should raise the level of euro-area GDP by more than 1 percent.	11	1
201501	1886	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	Some of these purchases were already anticipated in our December forecast (the dashed red line) and much of them were built into our January forecast (the dashed blue line), but the announcement on the following day nevertheless surprised us on the upside, and over the weekend we boosted our euro-area projection a bit further.	11	1
201501	1887	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	To be sure, there are many downside risks to the euro-area outlook, including those posed by Greece.	11	1
201501	1888	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	The far-left and anti-austerity Syriza party won nearly a majority of seats in Sunday’s parliamentary election and will form a coalition government with another populist party.	11	1
201501	1889	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	We expect contentious negotiations between the new government and its official creditors, the IMF and EU, on the terms of new lending, and difficulties in these talks will likely create financial stresses that spill over into the rest of Europe.	11	1
201501	1890	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	However, as failure of these talks could lead to Greece defaulting and exiting the euro area, our best guess is that agreement will ultimately be reached, with only limited damage to the euro-area recovery.	11	1
201501	1891	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	Returning to panel 1, our forecast for total growth (the black solid line) is nearly unchanged from the December forecast (the dashed red line).	11	1
201501	1892	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	As I noted earlier, we revised down the projections for China and South America.	11	1
201501	1893	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	However, other developments have boosted the outlook and largely offset these downward revisions.	11	1
201501	1894	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	First, as shown in panel 3, oil prices are down further since the time of the December Tealbook, and we estimate this should add about 0.1 percentage point to overall foreign growth.	11	1
201501	1895	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	The boost would be bigger, except that lower oil prices led us to mark down the outlook for Mexico and Canada, oil exporters that account for a large share of our trade-weighted aggregate for foreign growth.	11	1
201501	1896	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	Second, the broad dollar is up another 3 percent (panel 4), which adds another 0.1 percentage point to foreign economic growth.	11	1
201501	1897	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	Finally, monetary policy is more accommodative than in the December Tealbook not only in the euro area, but also in Canada, where the policy rate was cut to ¾ percent, and in the United Kingdom, where we now see liftoff being delayed to the end of this year.	11	1
201501	1898	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	If these easing actions were in response to a weakening of economic activity that was not already anticipated in our outlook, they would not necessarily boost our economic growth forecast.	11	1
201501	1899	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	But, especially in the euro area, monetary loosening appears to be importantly motivated by risks that falling oil prices may push down headline inflation (panel 5), so far as to unhinge inflation expectations.	11	1
201501	1900	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	Much the same considerations led the BOJ to amp up its QQE program late last year.	11	1
201501	1901	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	Thus, all told, these monetary easings are a plus for global economic growth.	11	1
201501	1902	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	As Simon has described, financial markets are evidencing some gloom about the global outlook, and there is certainly no shortage of downside risks.	11	1
201501	1903	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	Nevertheless, it is worth noting some risks on the upside as well.	11	1
201501	1904	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	For starters, we’ve built a reasonably limited boost from falling oil prices into our forecast for foreign economic growth, and taking into account the uncertainty attending estimates of these effects, we would not be surprised if lower energy costs triggered stronger improvements in confidence and spending than we’ve written down.	11	1
201501	1905	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	Additionally, the decline in oil prices may have further to go.	11	1
201501	1906	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	As shown in panel 3, our projection regarding oil prices, based on futures markets, turns back up over the forecast period.	11	1
201501	1907	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	This partly reflects expected increases in the demand for oil as global economic growth picks up and users respond to lower oil prices.	11	1
201501	1908	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	In addition, lower oil prices are expected to damp oil production in higher-cost producers such as the United States.	11	1
201501	1909	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	But the extent to which US oil production will fall off in response to lower prices is quite uncertain.	11	1
201501	1910	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	Although rig counts are down and oil investment projects are being scaled back, future extraction will be concentrated in the most productive wells.	11	1
201501	1911	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	The Department of Energy is projecting that US oil production will still move up through the early part of the year.	11	1
201501	1912	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	We would not be greatly surprised if oil supply held up well enough to push oil prices below levels called for by futures markets.	11	1
201501	1913	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	This would likely push US and foreign growth up further, although it is possible that as oil prices fall to very low levels, some financial vulnerabilities—especially in EMEs most dependent on oil revenues—might be exacerbated.	11	1
201501	1914	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	Finally, I’d like to turn to the dollar, shown in panel 4.	11	1
201501	1915	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	Since your December meeting, the dollar has risen further as expectations mounted for additional monetary easing abroad, mainly in the euro area.	11	1
201501	1916	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	Looking ahead, we expect the broad real dollar to move sideways as our monetary tightening boosts the dollar a bit further against other industrial-country currencies, while the dollar depreciates a touch against EME currencies.	11	1
201501	1917	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	Since last summer, we have been regularly underpredicting the rise in the dollar, and we could certainly be doing so again.	11	1
201501	1918	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	But as the dollar gets higher, the chances that it could surprise us on the downside have also grown.	11	1
201501	1919	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	The dollar’s current valuation partly reflects material probabilities of very adverse developments abroad, such as renewed crisis in the euro area or a hard landing in China.	11	1
201501	1920	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	If these downside risks do not materialize and confidence in the global outlook improves, much of the dollar’s recent run-up could be reversed, as shown by the red line in panel 1 of your next exhibit and as we discussed in the alternative scenarios in the Risks and Uncertainty section of the Tealbook.	11	1
201501	1921	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	As well, oil prices, in panel 2, might rise more steeply than in our baseline forecast.	11	1
201501	1922	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	Panels 3 and 4 show the effect of these developments in our general equilibrium model SIGMA, whose results may differ from those encompassed in the staff’s judgmental projection.	11	1
201501	1923	2015-01-28	meeting	KAMIN	The decline of the dollar in this scenario leads to a rise in GDP above its baseline path, which is only partially offset by the effect of the higher oil price, while these developments work together to deliver a large but transitory run-up in inflation.	11	1

201501	1937	2015-01-28	meeting	WILCOX	The latest tranche of data suggests that real activity here at home was on a somewhat stronger footing during the second half of last year than we thought at the time of the December Tealbook.	11	1
201501	1938	2015-01-28	meeting	WILCOX	For example, as shown in panel 1, real GDP is now estimated to have increased at an annual rate of 5 percent in the third quarter.	11	1
