201501	3777	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	President Plosser.	22	2
201501	3778	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	22	2
201501	3779	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	As I said earlier, I thought the memo regarding the risks associated with lifting off too soon versus too late is very helpful and useful.	22	2
201501	3780	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	The risks highlighted in the comparison between an earlier, gradual liftoff as opposed to a later and steeper liftoff indicate that those risks are not particularly substantial and are of similar magnitudes in either case.	22	2
201501	3781	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	The results depend, of course, on the types of shocks that affect the economy in the future, which, thus, makes it very difficult to rank these options with any certainty to speak of.	22	2
201501	3782	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	Given my view of the underlying strength of the US economy and the greater stability of our financial system currently, I find the earlier and gradual policy more appealing.	22	2
201501	3783	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	However, the memo on foreign experiences point out it is particularly important, as exhibited in Canada, that the policy be data driven, as President Mester was suggesting.	22	2
201501	3784	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	Further, the models do not point to any serious economic consequences in the event that the policy rate needs to return to the zero bound.	22	2
201501	3785	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	With a policy that is data driven, as indicated by the staff’s consideration of both various rules and historical experience, we should be lifting off immediately, as has been pointed out earlier.	22	2
201501	3786	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	More immediate liftoff also indicates that there will be less of a need to raise the funds rate aggressively in the future.	22	2
201501	3787	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	Indeed, an earlier liftoff does more to ensure that we can be patient after liftoff than does continued delay.	22	2
201501	3788	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	The fly in the ointment, of course, is the rapid decline in oil prices and the subsequent effects they will have on headline and, to some extent, core inflation in the months to come.	22	2
201501	3789	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	These effects will make policy deliberations unusually challenging for the Committee, and I think it increases the danger that we will fail to see an underlying firming in inflation, and in so doing delay normalization by more than would occur absent the oil price decline.	22	2
201501	3790	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	It is true that by waiting until the smoke clears, the Committee can offset nominal pressures by raising interest rates at a faster pace.	22	2
201501	3791	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	That is easy for us to say now.	22	2
201501	3792	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	When the time comes, doing so could be politically difficult and far from a certain outcome of policy deliberations.	22	2
201501	3793	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	Governor Tarullo gave a great case for this in the financial-stability go-round yesterday.	22	2
201501	3794	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	This risk, I fear, concerns me and is one that is not captured in the model exercises.	22	2
201501	3795	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	As to what conditions I would like to see at liftoff, my short answer is they are staring us in the face today.	22	2
201501	3796	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	As I have argued many times, and as Governor Fischer noted yesterday, being data dependent, according to most data rules and historical experience, the assessment is that the current low inflation and its expected gradual move up is not sufficient to justify or continue with zero rates.	22	2
201501	3797	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	It only justifies more accommodative rates than usual.	22	2
201501	3798	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	Unfortunately, the fall in oil prices is masking, to some extent, any potential increase in underlying inflationary price pressures.	22	2
201501	3799	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	For that reason, I would place more weight, as I said yesterday, on things like trimmed means or medians, and they are not showing any appreciable declines in inflationary pressures.	22	2
201501	3800	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	In particular, if falling oil prices were to have little appreciable effect on those data, I’d have greater confidence that the inflation would return to target once the oil prices stabilize.	22	2
201501	3801	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	Witnessing consistent declines in those types of measures, however, would lead me to undermine that confidence.	22	2
201501	3802	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	As to statement language, I have been concerned for some time that our statement should concisely articulate the economic factors that are governing both the current setting and future path of policy.	22	2
201501	3803	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	Policy should be data driven.	22	2
201501	3804	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	Forward guidance directly relating the path of policy and its link to forecasts of relevant data should be made as explicit as possible.	22	2
201501	3805	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	To indicate that data dependence and uncertainty surrounding the path, the Committee may also wish to contain relevant ranges of alternative paths that could occur if the economy were to evolve somewhat differently.	22	2
201501	3806	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	That is, look for alternative robustness of some kind.	22	2
201501	3807	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	To that end, I believe paragraph 4 of the pre-liftoff statement—it becomes paragraph 3 of the liftoff statement—could actually be made more precise.	22	2
201501	3808	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	It should indicate what the anticipated trajectory of the relevant variables are forecast to be and why those trajectories would call for a gradual approach to tightening.	22	2
201501	3809	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	Or, if those variables would not call for a gradual approach, the specific economic factors that are leading to deviations from normal policy should be stated.	22	2
201501	3810	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	By doing this, financial market participants, firms, and households can better gauge when and how future policy will evolve.	22	2
201501	3811	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	I do like the general direction that the statement language is headed.	22	2
201501	3812	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	It appears to be headed, in my view, to a more data-dependent reaction function.	22	2
201501	3813	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	Having said that, the devil will be in the details.	22	2
201501	3814	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	For example, I would caution the Committee to be careful about the formulation so as to be consistent with our longer-term strategies.	22	2
201501	3815	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	We are fairly clear there that we do not have an explicit employment target, and we explain why.	22	2
201501	3816	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	We don’t want to have a statement that will corner us into creating an explicit employment target in order to define one of the metrics for policy.	22	2
201501	3817	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	I think the language in alternative C and in the pre-liftoff statement that refers to “deviations of employment and inflation from its objectives” may trigger questions and pressure on the Committee about those objectives or goals, and perhaps calls for more specificity on employment than we might be comfortable providing.	22	2
201501	3818	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	I think we have to be very careful about how we set that up.	22	2
201501	3819	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	I would also draw attention to the language in paragraph 4 regarding the funds rate being below some normal level for some period of time.	22	2
201501	3820	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	I never liked this language.	22	2
201501	3821	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	It remains confusing to the public, and they don’t know what it means or what, indeed, we intend.	22	2
201501	3822	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	I think different people on the Committee may interpret it differently.	22	2
201501	3823	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	Some may view this as a lower neutral rate, others may view it as simply a slower adjustment to a neutral rate, and others may mean both.	22	2
201501	3824	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	That’s fine.	22	2
201501	3825	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	But I think this paragraph needs to be rethought or allowed to disappear so that the infamous dot charts could provide more guidance.	22	2
201501	3826	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	Perhaps even a better way would be to adopt a monetary policy report in which such discussions could be elaborated on and dealt with in a more fulsome and transparent manner.	22	2
201501	3827	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	22	2

201501	3829	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	President Evans.	22	2
201501	3830	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	 Thank you, Madam Chair.	22	2
201501	3831	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	If I could build on President Mester’s analogy, I feel a little bit like I got up to go to the kitchen, make a snack, and somebody changed the channel on me.	22	2
201501	3832	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	I’ve got to do some more channel surfing back to where we were before.	22	2
201501	3833	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	For several meetings, I have already voiced my position regarding the first question on weighing the risks of lifting off prematurely versus waiting too long to raise rates.	22	2
201501	3834	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	For me, prudent risk management dictates that we should remain patient for some time before initiating our policy liftoff.	22	2
201501	3835	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	One of the biggest risks we face today is a premature policy tightening.	22	2
201501	3836	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	If the Committee misjudges the strength of current conditions and then the economy is hit with a disinflationary shock soon after liftoff, we could find ourselves in the extremely uncomfortable position of being forced back to the zero lower bound.	22	2
201501	3837	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	We would again have to turn to second- best unconventional policies, but this time it would be in the context of a policy reversal.	22	2
201501	3838	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	The most powerful of these unconventional policies is our credible expression in support of policy actions that we will do what it takes to achieve maximum employment and price stability.	22	2
201501	3839	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	Returning to the zero lower bound would be a large blow to our credibility.	22	2
201501	3840	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	This would reduce our future ability to provide stimulus through such guidance.	22	2
201501	3841	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	In contrast, what if we wait too long and inflation picks up faster than we expect?	22	2
201501	3842	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	I don’t see a high cost to this scenario.	22	2
201501	3843	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	We have far to go to reach our inflation target.	22	2
201501	3844	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	Some greater- than-expected pickup in inflation would be welcomed to speed this policy achievement.	22	2
201501	3845	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	Furthermore, there is no great cost if we end up, for a period of time, with inflation running moderately above 2 percent.	22	2
201501	3846	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	If inflation did overshoot our target by an uncomfortable margin, we know how to address this problem with moderate increases in interest rates.	22	2
201501	3847	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	Our tools are powerful instruments in that event.	22	2
201501	3848	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	The alternative scenarios in the Tealbook showed that.	22	2
201501	3849	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	Now let me turn to the economic conditions I would have to see to justify liftoff.	22	2
201501	3850	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	I mentioned these in December, too.	22	2
201501	3851	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	I have tried to capture these with some suggested language that I circulated earlier.	22	2
201501	3852	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	I think if you look at that, it shows a great deal of data dependence, which is something that we all talk quite a lot about desiring.	22	2
201501	3853	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	First, economic growth would have to continue to run at a solid pace.	22	2
201501	3854	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	On the inflation side, I would need to have good confidence not only in a point forecast that inflation would get back up to 2 percent within two years, but also that once inflation rose to 2 percent, the odds of inflation running modestly above or modestly below 2 percent were equal.	22	2
201501	3855	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	That is, I want to be confident that we have put a policy in place that is designed to achieve our target in a sustainable and symmetric fashion.	22	2
201501	3856	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	Notably, it seems to me much too timid if we adopt an assessment that is hoping to thread the needle and bring inflation up to 2 percent from below without ever risking crossing over 2 percent.	22	2
201501	3857	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	In addition, at the time of liftoff, I would like to see clear signs that nominal wages are beginning to increase toward the 3 to 4 percent growth range that I associate with neutral cost pressures—that is, cost increases that would be more consistent with an underlying inflation rate of 2 percent.	22	2
201501	3858	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	I would also expect to see at least the beginnings of an increase in year-over-year core inflation.	22	2
201501	3859	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	I agree quite a lot with President Lockhart’s suggestion that if we’re below 1½ percent on core that is not encouraging.	22	2
201501	3860	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	I know this is difficult for many, but as raw forecasting tools go, current core inflation is at the top of the list of useful inflation indicators.	22	2
201501	3861	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	Regarding yield-curve data, I would have to see one of the following two developments:  some upward movement in nominal 10-year Treasury rates and inflation breakevens and other market- based measures of inflation compensation, or I would need a lot more confidence than I have today that the declines in these measures over the past year are due to relatively innocuous factors and are not reflecting lower inflation expectations, nor elevated risk premiums associated with unfavorable inflation outcomes.	22	2
201501	3862	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	Those are key data that I’m monitoring.	22	2
201501	3863	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	Now, let me turn to the suggested language.	22	2
201501	3864	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	I look at the “in a couple of meetings” wording in the proposed pre-liftoff statement and ask myself, is it plausible to have this language in place and then not raise rates in two meetings?	22	2
201501	3865	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	As it stands, I think the answer is, “Not really.”	22	2
201501	3866	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	That would present a high hurdle for my agreement to adopt such language.	22	2
201501	3867	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	I was disappointed that the suggested language didn’t make more reference to these data issues directly.	22	2
201501	3868	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	I find only small comfort in the language that allows for a delay in the rate hike if we see slower-than-currently-expected progress on inflation.	22	2
201501	3869	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	This puts an ill-defined marker down today, and then, to trigger a delay, it assigns the task of proving that the outlook has turned worse than this marker.	22	2
201501	3870	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	Instead, the onus should be on proving that we have enough growing confidence in our forecast of increasing inflation to justify the rate increase.	22	2
201501	3871	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	I circulated suggested language that provides a more explicit conditional set of inflation indicators.	22	2
201501	3872	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	It seems important for us to affirm the need for the policy tightening, not just to say we don’t have enough evidence for a delay.	22	2
201501	3873	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	Being confident that inflation is sustainably headed back to 2 percent just seems to be good policymaking under uncertainty.	22	2
201501	3874	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	We are highly uncertain about the path for inflation, and we currently are well below our inflation target.	22	2
201501	3875	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	Continuing a patient monitoring for signs that inflation will increase over the next two years still seems prudent.	22	2
201501	3876	2015-01-28	meeting	EVANS	Finally, with regard to the pace of firming after liftoff, I think the language in the proposed statement, in conjunction with the SEPs, will work adequately to convey the slow pace of rate increases just about all of us have in our assumptions regarding appropriate policy.	22	2

201501	3880	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	22	2
201501	3881	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Well, I thought long and hard about this issue of whether we should be earlier and gradual versus later and steeper.	22	2
201501	3882	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	After careful consideration, I came to the conclusion that it would actually be best to be on time and on track.	22	2
201501	3883	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	[Laughter]	22	2
201501	3884	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Now, I realize as soon as I say that, the Board staff is going to start working on a memo that discusses the pros and cons of that approach, and probably it’s going to find some arguments why that’s not the optimal approach to take.	22	2
201501	3885	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	But, anyway, that’s my view.	22	2
201501	3886	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Really, what we’re talking about is the challenge of delivering on this on time and on track in the current circumstances.	22	2
201501	3887	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	I’ve actually found the discussion already this morning to be really excellent in addressing a lot of these issues.	22	2
201501	3888	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Now, as suggested by my own research earlier with Dave Reifschneider, there are conditions that warrant a lower-for-longer stance for policy.	22	2
201501	3889	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Indeed, given the evolution of the economy, it’s clear that we have been more patient than suggested by many simple monetary policy rules, and even the optimal-control simulation reported in the Tealbook.	22	2
201501	3890	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	That patience has been partly guided by several factors that are not directly taken into account by these approaches, especially the possible future downside risks associated with the zero lower bound.	22	2
201501	3891	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Yet I think it’s important to remember that “lower for longer” does not mean forever.	22	2
201501	3892	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Even accounting for the reasons to be very patient, we are nearing conditions that would warrant the start of normalization of our policy, in my view.	22	2
201501	3893	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	In weighing when to lift off, obviously, the first task is to assess the distance from our goals.	22	2
201501	3894	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	If we lift off later this year, which is what I currently view as appropriate, the full employment part of our mandate would essentially be fulfilled.	22	2
201501	3895	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	But inflation would still be well below our 2 percent goal.	22	2
201501	3896	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Even after liftoff, we can manage the pace of normalization to make sure that inflation moves back to target.	22	2
201501	3897	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Our continuing extraordinarily accommodative policy stance, coupled with a solid and strengthening labor market, overall stable longer-run inflation expectations, and the time-honored lags in monetary policy, make it likely that inflation will return to our 2 percent objective over the medium term.	22	2
201501	3898	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Of course, events may play out differently, but to lose confidence in that basic forecast, I would need to see a serious slowdown in economic growth or clear signs that underlying inflation is falling.	22	2
201501	3899	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Again, I think it’s important in thinking about liftoff just to remind ourselves how extraordinarily accommodative the stance on monetary policy is today.	22	2

201501	3901	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Not only do we have very low interest rates, but also a balance sheet of more than $4 trillion that is providing substantial stimulus, at least based on the best estimates we have on the effects of LSAPs.	22	2
201501	3902	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Before I turn to the evolution of our statement language, there have been a couple of comments on our inflation target, and President Evans made a comment about how overshooting inflation would not be that problematic.	22	2

201501	3915	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	That’s the difference between June 1965, when the debate about tightening in that cycle was really starting to happen, and December 1966.	22	2
201501	3916	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	It’s just a reminder that our ability to forecast is not that good.	22	2
201501	3917	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	The second is that wages can lag the cycle, as President Mester said and I argued yesterday.	22	2
201501	3918	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Again, I think that the history on this is maybe not as reassuring about how quickly things can change when monetary policy is very accommodative.	22	2

201501	3920	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	It’s obviously crucial that we communicate our intentions to the public as well as we can, especially given how low market expectations of future rates are right now.	22	2

201501	3925	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	One possible evolution of our forward guidance is reflected in the handout, and in alternative C, and refers in paragraph 3 to a potential increase in the target rate in a couple of meetings.	22	2
201501	3926	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	One advantage of this approach that I see is it clearly communicates our intentions.	22	2
201501	3927	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	I actually think it’s extremely clear in what we’re going to do.	22	2

201501	3929	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	The flip side of this clarity is, I think, that it’s a negative—it makes a June rate hike seem like it’s baked in the cake.	22	2
201501	3930	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Let me suggest a possible alternative approach that both signals that liftoff is approaching but leaves open options regarding the precise timing of liftoff.	22	2
201501	3931	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Specifically, we could say, “Based on its current assessment of economic conditions and the outlook, the Committee judges that in the months ahead the economy will likely be moving closer to conditions warranting an increase in the target range for the federal funds rate.”	22	2
201501	3932	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Going back to President Evans’s comment earlier, it does have both “likely” and “moving closer,” which leaves a lot of optionality—something that I think is appropriate, given where we are and where we are likely to be in the next few meetings.	22	2
201501	3933	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	At least as a basis for thinking about future language, I think this language conveys the view that depending on the data, liftoff is possible two, three, or four meetings ahead.	22	2
201501	3934	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Such language also has the advantage of being applicable for multiple statements and could be modified relatively easy with minor adjustments.	22	2
201501	3935	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	We’ll also start the process of weaning financial markets and other Fed watchers off the belief that we will always be telling them exactly what we plan to do and when.	22	2
201501	3936	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	Precision in our forward guidance was a very useful approach under the extraordinary conditions of recent years, but something that I hope we eliminate as part of the normalization process.	22	2

201501	3942	2015-01-28	meeting	WILLIAMS	As we contemplate the normalization of our policy stance, I think this is as good an opportunity as any we will get to take a fresh start, think about simplifying and restructuring our statements to make them more effective for a more normalized environment.	22	2

201501	3949	2015-01-28	meeting	GEORGE	Thank you, Madam Chair.	22	2
201501	3950	2015-01-28	meeting	GEORGE	Though the discussion about moving sooner or later is about balancing risk, I see it as somewhat neglecting that we have already built risk- management considerations into our decision about liftoff.	22	2
201501	3951	2015-01-28	meeting	GEORGE	As the Board memos discuss, nearly all of the standard rules we use to evaluate policy have already called for liftoff.	22	2
201501	3952	2015-01-28	meeting	GEORGE	In addition, the real federal funds rate has been below the Tealbook-consistent measure of r* for about a year.	22	2
201501	3953	2015-01-28	meeting	GEORGE	Analysis by my staff also assesses to what extent the period in which policy was constrained from being sufficiently accommodative due to the zero lower bound has been offset during the recent period when the funds rate has been held below prescriptions from an estimated policy rule.	22	2
201501	3954	2015-01-28	meeting	GEORGE	They find the cumulative shortfall of accommodation earlier in the recovery has been more than offset by the subsequent cumulative excess accommodation.	22	2
201501	3955	2015-01-28	meeting	GEORGE	These factors suggest to me that the Committee has effectively already made a decision to move later and assume the associated risk rather than move in line with prescribed policy rules.	22	2
201501	3956	2015-01-28	meeting	GEORGE	In terms of the specific questions, I see liftoff in the middle of this year, which is in line with current expectations, and at a gradual pace consistent with a data-dependent approach and one that balances risks.	22	2
201501	3957	2015-01-28	meeting	GEORGE	Waiting for liftoff until we reach full employment and inflation of 2 percent does not seem appropriate, particularly with an elevated balance sheet that continues to provide accommodation.	22	2
201501	3958	2015-01-28	meeting	GEORGE	The temptation to see one more data point will always be present.	22	2
201501	3959	2015-01-28	meeting	GEORGE	History shows this can lead central banks to move too late.	22	2
201501	3960	2015-01-28	meeting	GEORGE	Because of the lags we face in monetary policy, we likely will need to move before full attainment of our objectives.	22	2
201501	3961	2015-01-28	meeting	GEORGE	Alternatively, the risk of moving even later than in the middle of the year is that we may fall behind the curve and would need to move rates up more quickly.	22	2
201501	3962	2015-01-28	meeting	GEORGE	Of course, a rapid increase in rates could surprise financial markets and pose risks to financial stability.	22	2
201501	3963	2015-01-28	meeting	GEORGE	Along these lines, I found the Board staff memo assessing the likelihood of these various events useful, though as the memo itself points out, the scenarios do not take into account reputation risk or financial-stability concerns.	22	2
201501	3964	2015-01-28	meeting	GEORGE	Still, the combined likelihood of one of the adverse scenarios occurring was higher in the later and steep scenario than under the early and gradual scenario.	22	2
201501	3965	2015-01-28	meeting	GEORGE	Also according to the simulations, the early and gradual approach effectively takes off the table a scenario in which we would have to raise rates aggressively.	22	2
201501	3966	2015-01-28	meeting	GEORGE	In terms of what developments I’d like to see, I’m a bit hesitant about drawing any bright lines regarding conditions that I’d have to see before liftoff, and I thought the Chair’s set of criteria from the December press conference was reasonable in that regard.	22	2
201501	3967	2015-01-28	meeting	GEORGE	Further progress in labor market conditions along with confidence that inflation would be moving back to target are sufficient in my mind to consider liftoff.	22	2
201501	3968	2015-01-28	meeting	GEORGE	I’m also willing to look through some soft readings on near-term inflation rates.	22	2
201501	3969	2015-01-28	meeting	GEORGE	Of course, I’ll also be listening to anecdotes received from business contacts to confirm or contradict issues of wage and price pressures and stability in the price of oil.	22	2
201501	3970	2015-01-28	meeting	GEORGE	Appreciation of the dollar and five-year, five-year-ahead inflation breakevens will also be important to that confidence.	22	2
201501	3971	2015-01-28	meeting	GEORGE	Regarding statement language, I’m generally comfortable with the suggested language in the Board staff memo.	22	2
201501	3972	2015-01-28	meeting	GEORGE	It highlights that March is going to be an important decision point, and if I look at my current outlook, removing “patient” would be appropriate in March.	22	2
201501	3973	2015-01-28	meeting	GEORGE	Given the emphasis on data dependence, we will clearly calibrate those first paragraphs of the statement to reflect any change in the outlook.	22	2
201501	3974	2015-01-28	meeting	GEORGE	If the data soften, these paragraphs can convey a shift in the outlook, which will presumably cause expectations to adjust, but overall I see removing “patient” as giving us flexibility around the timing of liftoff.	22	2
201501	3975	2015-01-28	meeting	GEORGE	Alternatively, if we keep it in this March statement it will most like push expectations back and limit our flexibility.	22	2
201501	3976	2015-01-28	meeting	GEORGE	Finally, I support President Mester’s proposal for recalibrating our statement, and, as others have noted, would welcome further discussion of that.	22	2
201501	3977	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	22	2
201501	3978	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	President Fisher.	22	2
201501	3979	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	22	2
201501	3980	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	I’m just going to give some thoughts regarding the questions that were asked.	22	2
201501	3981	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	I would say, generally, the Board memo on the timing and pace of policy firming demonstrates that it’s possible to build a plausible case for unusual accommodation in current circumstances along the lines of the Tealbook baseline policy rate path.	22	2
201501	3982	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	But “plausible” isn’t the same thing as “convincing.”	22	2
201501	3983	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	You remember during the previous meeting I referred to the religious agnostic that wasn’t sure he believe in D-O-G, and I’m similarly agnostic or I’m not convinced for several reasons that I’d like to lay out here.	22	2
201501	3984	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	The first is that it’s possible that the Tealbook baseline inflation forecast is too pessimistic.	22	2
201501	3985	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	It builds in 1.8 percent longer-run inflation expectations.	22	2
201501	3986	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	Of great concern to me and my staff is that it doesn’t include a speed effect, whereby inflation responds to the change in the unemployment rate as well as its level.	22	2
201501	3987	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	With the higher inflation path, the optimal control and Taylor rule policy prescriptions shift upward.	22	2
201501	3988	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	The Tealbook policy prescriptions ignore what I think are very serious recession risks attached to any appreciable overshoot of full employment, and, as I’ve said, almost ad nauseam, they ignore the nonlinearity or convexity of the Phillips curve.	22	2
201501	3989	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	Sooner or later, to ensure that inflation converges to target, you’ll have to correct any employment overshoot, and that’s just not something the FOMC has ever been able to pull off without triggering a recession.	22	2
201501	3990	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	I’d like to see the staff convince you—because I won’t be here—that these fears are overblown, and I think they should develop for you and show you in stochastic stimulations using a realistic policy rule what the risks are of this occurring.	22	2
201501	3991	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	I’m not a big fan of ad hoc inertia in policy rules, such as that built into the Tealbook baseline policy prescription.	22	2
201501	3992	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	Post-liftoff, the baseline path is from the Taylor (1999) rule with inertia.	22	2
201501	3993	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	Ad hoc inertia perpetuates past policy errors.	22	2
201501	3994	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	If you’ll forgive me for saying so, it’s a very crude way of trying to capture effects that are more fundamental effects than genuine inertia effects—especially the potential disruption to financial markets from too-large unexpected movements in rates or possibly policymakers’ desires to offset past inflation target misses.	22	2
201501	3995	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	Policy may respond to a weighted average of expected future, current, and past inflation rates, not just current inflation.	22	2
201501	3996	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	The burden of proof needs to be especially high when the course of action being advocated happens to be an easy or expedient road.	22	2
201501	3997	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	It’s tempting to say that we can clean up after ourselves later if policy turns out to be too accommodative.	22	2
201501	3998	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	It’s tempting to leave that hard work to a future Federal Open Market Committee.	22	2
201501	3999	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	We save ourselves a lot of criticism and political grief in the short run if we downplay the risks attached to keeping policy exceptionally accommodative longer.	22	2
201501	4000	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	My only advice—this is highly didactic and will probably be ignored—is we need to resist these temptations at this table.	22	2
201501	4001	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	We need to be what Ken Rogoff calls conservative central bankers or at least lean in that direction.	22	2
201501	4002	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	As regards memo number seven on the stochastic implications of alternative strategies for the beginning of policy normalization, I’m very much concerned about the credibility problems attached to the later and steep policy strategy.	22	2
201501	4003	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	It’s possible—indeed, I would say it’s even likely, on the basis of my background as a market operator—that the public will interpret a decision to defer a liftoff as a signal that the Committee is generally dovish and disinclined to raise rates quickly.	22	2
201501	4004	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	In other words, I think there’s a risk that the public and the markets might see the choice as between “earlier and gradual” and “later and gradual” rather than between “earlier and gradual” and “later and steep.”	22	2
201501	4005	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	If we lift off in March 2015, as I had suggested, or April 2015, which is apparently not going to happen, people would be able to see as early as June 2015 that you’re serious about “gradual” and “earlier and gradual.”	22	2
201501	4006	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	On the other hand, my gut tells me that if you are going to say you are going to defer liftoff, say, to September or January of the following year, but then plan to raise rates quickly thereafter, people will have to wait until January 2016 or March 2016 to know whether you’re serious.	22	2
201501	4007	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	Early and gradual is quickly verified.	22	2
201501	4008	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	Later and steep requires a great deal of trust.	22	2
201501	4009	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	In the context of the Taylor (1999) rule with inertia, the public might interpret delayed liftoff as signaling an especially large amount of interest rate inertia stemming from concerns about having to reverse course should the economic outlook deteriorate, as President Evans articulated very well earlier.	22	2
201501	4010	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	Alternatively, they might interpret delayed liftoff as signaling that the Committee believes that the equilibrium real short-term interest rate is unusually low and likely to remain so well beyond the end of 2015.	22	2
201501	4011	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	Alternatively, they might believe that due to concerns about stability of longer-term inflation expectations or about the unreliability of standard measurements of slack, the Committee has decided to downweight the output gap in its deliberations relative to the inflation gap, or they might believe that the FOMC cares not just about the current inflation shortfall, but also shortfalls in previous years.	22	2
201501	4012	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	Every one of these arguments for patience, Madam Chair, has been cited by one or another FOMC participant in public communications or around the FOMC table, as I remember it.	22	2
201501	4013	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	So it’s no stretch to think that the public will not completely buy into later and steep.	22	2
201501	4014	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	I would suggest the staff provide some simulation showing what happens to the economy if the public should misinterpret the Committee’s decision to delay liftoff.	22	2
201501	4015	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	What about the incentive to renege?	22	2
201501	4016	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	Say that September 2015 or even January 2016 arrives.	22	2
201501	4017	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	I wonder if we can be sure that the Committee will follow through on the steep half of the later and steep.	22	2
201501	4018	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	Consider, especially, the possibility that the public may have misinterpreted the reasons for the late liftoff and made financial bets and commitments accordingly.	22	2
201501	4019	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	Might not future Committee members be tempted to then depart from the Taylor rule prescriptions?	22	2
201501	4020	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	With regard to the question as to what you would pay attention to in terms of information, personally, I would pay close to zero attention to realized headline inflation, and I’d give a very strong nod to the trimmed-mean indexes.	22	2
201501	4021	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	We’ve heard a lot about that around the table.	22	2
201501	4022	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	I would encourage, even though it’s hard work, the staff to incorporate that and give more fulsome explanations of what they see as indicators.	22	2

201501	4024	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	What I would want to see is evidence that households and professional forecasters expect inflation to rise toward target fairly promptly over time.	22	2
201501	4025	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	I’d like to see their 5-year inflation expectations reasonably consistent with the 2 percent inflation rate, and their 10-year expectations and 5-year, 5-year-forward expectations very much consistent with the 2 percent inflation rate.	22	2
201501	4026	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	I would want to see evidence the economy is likely to continue to expand at a rate that implies further declines in the unemployment rate.	22	2
201501	4027	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	I’m taking into account not only the momentum we see in the economy, but also the anecdotal evidence we pick up from our contacts.	22	2
201501	4028	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	I would be very mindful of the nonlinearity or convexity of the Phillips curve, and I would be mindful that, as President George reminded us just now, monetary policy acts with a lag.	22	2

201501	4032	2015-01-28	meeting	FISHER	If you wait until seeing the whites of the eyes, you’re going to shoot someone in the back of the head, and I don’t think that’s a prudent way to conduct monetary policy.	22	2

201501	4083	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	I think the main idea to keep in mind here is that we are tasked with developing a good monetary policy, and the path of that good policy will depend on the shocks that arrive during the normalization process.	22	2

201501	4087	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	I don’t think we should deviate from the good policy based on what that policy may or may not call for in the future based on the arrival of information.	22	2

201501	4104	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	But this is a problem of market expectations on policy being somewhat misaligned with the intentions of the Committee as outlined in the SEP.	22	2
201501	4105	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	What we should do, if we think that’s a problem, is bolster the credibility of our SEP paths, either by reinforcing that this really is what the Committee thinks or, if it’s not what the Committee thinks, then we should change what our SEP numbers are.	22	2
201501	4106	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	If we do not have a credibility problem where people don’t believe we’re going to raise rates, then, should shocks force us to raise rates abruptly, this would be well understood by markets and would not cause unnaturally high levels of volatility.	22	2
201501	4107	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	So we wouldn’t have any special problem associated with that, as long as we didn’t have any credibility problem.	22	2
201501	4108	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	The bottom line is good policy has to be shaped by shocks as they arrive.	22	2
201501	4109	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	There is always the possibility that these will lead us back to the zero interest rate policy or that they would lead us to abruptly raise rates in the future, but these branches of the tree do not have especially high probability right now.	22	2
201501	4110	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	And I don’t think they should necessarily be an argument figuring into current monetary policy decisionmaking.	22	2
201501	4111	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	The main issue for the Committee, I think, and really the elephant in the room is that regardless of how we approach normalization within current thinking, we have essentially already committed to a policy path that will be exceptionally easy over the next several years.	22	2
201501	4112	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	Whether this is good or wise is a great question.	22	2
201501	4113	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	Unemployment will now likely fall substantially below our estimates of the natural rate over the next two years.	22	2
201501	4114	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	The past two times this happened in the US economy, in the late 1990s and the mid-2000s, large, tangible, noticeable asset price bubbles developed.	22	2
201501	4115	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	Both of those were hotly debated around this table.	22	2
201501	4116	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	Both ultimately ended in recession.	22	2
201501	4117	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	The second one ended in global macroeconomic disaster.	22	2
201501	4118	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	Does the Committee wish to risk a replay of these bubble episodes?	22	2
201501	4119	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	What developments give me pause in the wisdom of normalization?	22	2
201501	4120	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	Here I want to address a simmering argument around the table as to whether it is even a good idea to be thinking about normalization at this point.	22	2
201501	4121	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	Governor Fischer said yesterday that he was uncomfortable with the zero interest rate policy.	22	2
201501	4122	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	I’m very much aligned with that.	22	2
201501	4123	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	I’m uncomfortable with the zero interest rate policy.	22	2
201501	4124	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	If we can normalize, I think we should.	22	2
201501	4125	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	Presidents Kocherlakota, Rosengren, and Evans eloquently argued that low inflation and low inflation expectations have to get more attention, or even a decisive level of attention, on this decision.	22	2
201501	4126	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	I have, over the past five years, placed heavier emphasis than most on the Committee on inflation and inflation expectations as a key determinant of the direction of policy.	22	2
201501	4127	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	In this sense, I am concerned and I have some sympathy, maybe some substantial sympathy, for the arguments of Presidents Kocherlakota, Rosengren, and Evans.	22	2
201501	4128	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	I take the ECB as a case in point.	22	2
201501	4129	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	Some of you know that in the summer of 2013 I went to Frankfurt, and I gave a speech that QE was their best option.	22	2
201501	4130	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	At that point, inflation was only somewhat below target and falling.	22	2
201501	4131	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	I talked with policymakers, ECB staff, and financial market people about this.	22	2
201501	4132	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	I got a cold reception.	22	2
201501	4133	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	But 18 months later, the ECB has come to a decision and has adopted QE.	22	2
201501	4134	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	I think it’s probably late.	22	2
201501	4135	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	They let inflation and inflation expectations drift a long way from their objectives.	22	2
201501	4136	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	Now it’s going to take quite a few years probably to get inflation back to target in Europe.	22	2
201501	4137	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	That’s a cautionary tale for us.	22	2
201501	4138	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	We don’t want to ignore this problem too long.	22	2
201501	4139	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	We don’t want to make excuses for too long of a time.	22	2
201501	4140	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	I am sympathetic to the arguments on this.	22	2
201501	4141	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	I want to make two points.	22	2
201501	4142	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	First, low inflation as it exists today cannot rationalize the zero interest rate policy.	22	2
201501	4143	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	A gap in inflation of something on the order of ½ percentage point is simply not large enough to rationalize a policy rate of zero.	22	2
201501	4144	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	It can rationalize a lower-than- normal policy rate, but not a zero policy rate.	22	2
201501	4145	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	I understand that the natural rate of interest could also be low, but, in my mind, that also is not low enough to rationalize the zero interest rate policy.	22	2
201501	4146	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	The bottom line is that the zero interest rate policy is an emergency measure that no longer fits the given data that we have.	22	2
201501	4147	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	Even if we raise rates, it will be to a very low level, about 50 basis points or 75 basis points, and by conventional metrics we will still be putting upward pressure on inflation and inflation expectations.	22	2
201501	4148	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	That’s one point.	22	2
201501	4149	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	I don’t think that we can rationalize the current policy based on inflation alone.	22	2
201501	4150	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	Inflation expectations have declined precipitously in recent quarters.	22	2
201501	4151	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	I am very concerned about this.	22	2
201501	4152	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	I do not place much signal value on surveys, and I agree with President Rosengren’s characterization of some of the drawbacks of looking at surveys.	22	2
201501	4153	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	They are not, in my view, sufficiently sensitive to incoming information to give us real-time information on policy judgments.	22	2
201501	4154	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	I would also, as others have, remind you of the Japanese experience, in which surveys continually said expectations were for normal levels of inflation, even though actual inflation continued to come in at low levels.	22	2
201501	4155	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	They actually didn’t have a target during that point.	22	2
201501	4156	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	However, despite all of these comments about how concerned I am about the decline in inflation expectations, I think that the oil shock is having special influence on the TIPS-based measures at this time.	22	2
201501	4157	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	The oil dislocation is substantial.	22	2
201501	4158	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	This is no ordinary oil price shock.	22	2
201501	4159	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	This is a 50, 60 percent reduction, and it’s causing a lot of volatility and a lot of repricing in markets; some of it that does not seem totally rational in the context of TIPS markets.	22	2
201501	4160	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	The bottom line is, I want to wait and see for now.	22	2
201501	4161	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	I think when the oil markets shake out and settle down, probably at a lower price than what was previously considered normal, then we’ll see if the TIPS-based inflation measures move up.	22	2
201501	4162	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	If they do, then that will give me confidence.	22	2
201501	4163	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	If they don’t, I’d be worried that the Committee’s credibility really is eroding.	22	2
201501	4164	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	I am anxious to see how that is going to develop in the coming months and quarters.	22	2
201501	4165	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	My final point is about language suggestions.	22	2
201501	4166	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	I agree with others that the language is generally okay, but I would pose the following question to the Committee.	22	2
201501	4167	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	Do we really want to telegraph as directly as we are sometimes suggesting here?	22	2
201501	4168	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	I agree with President Lockhart’s characterization at the beginning of this discussion that once we signal that we are on the road, we are turning a machine on and it’s a fait accompli.	22	2
201501	4169	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	Do we really want to be doing that?	22	2
201501	4170	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	If you’re on the Serengeti, and you’re a lion, and you’re hunting the zebra, you may not want to telegraph your intentions quite as precisely as we are talking about here.	22	2
201501	4171	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	My alternative vision for how to do this really involves a change in attitude, I think, around the table about how to do the tightening process.	22	2
201501	4172	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	I agree with President Williams, who made comments in this direction.	22	2
201501	4173	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	You want to eliminate the telegraphing during the normalization process.	22	2
201501	4174	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	Sure, it has been valuable at the zero bound.	22	2
201501	4175	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	There has been a lot of talk about forward guidance.	22	2
201501	4176	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	But this is may not be the right way to approach the normalization process.	22	2
201501	4177	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	What I want to do is just three things:  one, keep options open; two, be able to move at any juncture—and, for this reason, I keep harping on the issue of the press conference, which I think remains critical in this regard; and, three, seize favorable data and move at that point.	22	2
201501	4178	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	You don’t want to have to move when the data are going in the wrong direction.	22	2
201501	4179	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	I think it will send very mixed signals, especially at the beginning of the normalization process.	22	2
201501	4180	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	Keep options open.	22	2
201501	4181	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	Be able to move at any juncture.	22	2
201501	4182	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	Seize favorable data.	22	2
201501	4183	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	That’s how we want to do this normalization process.	22	2
201501	4184	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	Further moves after that, I think, should also seize on relatively good data coming in, both on the real economy and on inflation and inflation expectations.	22	2
201501	4185	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	I think if we do that, we’ll get a smooth ride.	22	2
201501	4186	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	If we try to do it on what looks like more of a calendar basis, there is a risk that we will be moving at times when the data are not in synch with us, and then people will say, “Well, I don’t understand what the FOMC’s reaction function really is.”	22	2
201501	4187	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	Those are my comments.	22	2
201501	4188	2015-01-28	meeting	BULLARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	22	2

201501	4190	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	President Kocherlakota.	22	2
201501	4191	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Thank you, Madam Chair.	22	2
201501	4192	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	As I have expressed, my thinking about policy is at a somewhat different place than the basic view that underlies the staff’s questions.	22	2
201501	4193	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I’m increasingly concerned about substantial downside risks to the credibility of our inflation target.	22	2
201501	4194	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Others have expressed concerns about upside risks to the credibility of our inflation target and about the risks to the financial stability.	22	2
201501	4195	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I want to emphasize that the downside risks to the credibility of our inflation target are actually mirrored already in our FOMC statement, in the sense that for a long period of time running up until July of last year, we made reference to inflation expectations being well anchored.	22	2
201501	4196	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	That reference has now disappeared from the opening paragraph of the FOMC statement because the data no longer are in a position to support that as definitively as before.	22	2
201501	4197	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think my concerns are, as I say, reflected in the evolution of the statement itself.	22	2
201501	4198	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Given my concerns, I see our biggest policy problem as not how to tighten further, but, rather, how to bolster the credibility of our inflation target.	22	2
201501	4199	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	My answers to the staff’s questions will reflect that perspective.	22	2
201501	4200	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	On the first question, there are risks associated both with tightening prematurely and with tightening too late.	22	2
201501	4201	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	On the tightening too late, I think that others have covered this ground well.	22	2
201501	4202	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We have a tool that we can use.	22	2
201501	4203	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	It takes will, as President Plosser has emphasized in his comments, and President Williams emphasized in his, but I look around the table and I don’t have any concerns on that dimension.	22	2
201501	4204	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I see that will around the table.	22	2
201501	4205	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	On the other hand, I think the risks associated with a premature liftoff seem considerably more challenging.	22	2
201501	4206	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think the staff memo works through the simulations associated with this.	22	2
201501	4207	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	But the risk that I am mainly concerned about is one that was not well addressed in the simulation, and it is one that we don’t really understand that much about, as Governor Tarullo talked about, something that is so critical in our formulation of our policy and our thinking about policy: inflation expectations.	22	2
201501	4208	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	It’s not really that well modeled.	22	2
201501	4209	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The main risk that I’m concerned about, the downside risk to the credibility of our 2 percent target, is not well captured in those simulations.	22	2
201501	4210	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	If we were to lift off against a backdrop of low and/or falling inflation and inflation compensation—I’m afraid I actually heard a number of people basically expressing a willingness to do that around the table—I think we would be failing to show resolve to bring inflation back up to our target.	22	2
201501	4211	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	However we think inflation issues are shaped, the messaging that we are willing to tighten policy, even though inflation is low or falling and inflation compensation measures also look like that, would surely worsen any existing credibility risk.	22	2
201501	4212	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think the reason to be concerned about this unanchoring to the downside is that it just seems extremely challenging for central banks to address this situation.	22	2
201501	4213	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The recent experiences in Sweden, Japan, and the euro zone just show how difficult it can be for central banks to recover if inflation falls following premature tightening.	22	2
201501	4214	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	That talks through some of my thinking about the first question.	22	2
201501	4215	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In terms of the second question, what data would we need to see at liftoff, I see two necessary conditions for liftoff.	22	2
201501	4216	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I might want to see more than those.	22	2
201501	4217	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	But the data need to be consistent with the economy meeting the 2 percent inflation objective over a one-to-two-year horizon.	22	2
201501	4218	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	One key sign of that outlook would be a Board staff forecast that inflation will be greater than or equal to 2 percent within two years.	22	2
201501	4219	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	It would be good for the Committee to be able to say in its statement, “We expect inflation to be greater than or equal to 2 percent within two years.”	22	2
201501	4220	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	If we felt comfortable doing that, I think that would be consistent with the kind of data flow that I’m looking for.	22	2
201501	4221	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Now, there is skepticism about point forecasts.	22	2
201501	4222	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	For me, a point forecast is just a way to summarize a probability distribution.	22	2
201501	4223	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	What I’m trying to say here is that actually the risk of inflation being above 2 percent is at least as large as the risk of inflation being below 2 percent.	22	2
201501	4224	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I’m just using that number as a summary of a mass of probabilities.	22	2
201501	4225	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The second piece of information I would need to see is that longer-term market-based inflation expectations have to have risen back to their historically normal ranges, and that would give me confidence that longer-term inflation expectations are indeed well anchored on our 2 percent goal.	22	2
201501	4226	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I haven’t specifically mentioned wage pressures.	22	2
201501	4227	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think that would feed into my inflation outlook.	22	2
201501	4228	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	There are reasons to think that wage pressures are going to lag as opposed to lead inflation, and there are reasons to think changes in productivity growth could influence the relationship between wages and inflation.	22	2
201501	4229	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	But my two necessary conditions are confidence in the inflation outlook and that the longer-term market-based measures are again well anchored.	22	2
201501	4230	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In terms of language, I echo President Williams and President Mester.	22	2

201501	4233	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	My research director, Sam Schulhofer-Wohl, is a former journalist.	22	2

201501	4235	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	For myself, one thing I would emphasize is that there is a lot of backward-looking language in the statement—where we have been, how has it influenced policy decisionmaking.	22	2
201501	4236	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Monetary policy operates with a lag, as others have noted.	22	2

201501	4241	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	Thank you, Madam Chair.	22	2
201501	4242	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	I view the first question—how the Committee should weigh the risks of lifting off prematurely versus the risks of waiting too long—as an instance of the universal risk of monetary conditions being too accommodative or too restrictive.	22	2
201501	4243	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	The former keeps the real rate below what the evolving needs of the economy would require and would generate excessively accommodative monetary conditions, and the opposite, too-restrictive policy, generates too little inflation and real activity.	22	2
201501	4244	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	My sense is that a substantial increase in real economic growth is occurring now, and together with the continued tightening of labor markets suggests rising nominal interest rates are warranted.	22	2
201501	4245	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	The public generally expects us to wait until June or so, and inflation expectations remain stable—they aren’t elevating.	22	2

201501	4247	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	Regarding the second question, given the data we have on hand now, I am already reasonably confident that inflation will move back to 2 percent over time.	22	2

201501	4271	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	I like other suggestions President Mester made.	22	2
201501	4272	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	I like moving “reinvestments” to the beginning of the policy passage, because it’s a key component of our policy stance.	22	2
201501	4273	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	I like “realized and expected progress” better than “deviations,” because the latter, as President Plosser points out, connotes excessive precision about our estimate of the maximum employment objective.	22	2
201501	4274	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	I also prefer her version of conditionality.	22	2
201501	4275	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	It strikes me as more direct and straightforward.	22	2
201501	4276	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	I think the choice in these simulations, “early and gradual” versus “late and steep,” is really not a realistic set of options available to us.	22	2
201501	4277	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	If we delayed an expected liftoff at a time when people were expecting us to lift off, I’m trying to think of what statement we would write that would preserve the average expected path of the funds rate.	22	2
201501	4278	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	In the case in which we delay liftoff, it’s hard for me to think of something that doesn’t at the same time cause market participants to lower their expected path of the funds rate.	22	2
201501	4279	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	I just don’t see how we can do that.	22	2
201501	4280	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	I don’t think it’s a real choice available to us.	22	2
201501	4281	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	I agree, in that regard, with Presidents Bullard and Fisher that counting on being able to make up for delay with a faster pace of tightening is really unrealistic.	22	2
201501	4282	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	I’d also say I’m not favorably disposed to a laundry list of economic indicators in our statement along the lines President Evans suggests.	22	2
201501	4283	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	There’s something inevitably clunky and inevitably distracting about that, and I think we should keep our statement at a high level.	22	2
201501	4284	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	Those are my remarks, Madam Chair.	22	2
201501	4285	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	22	2
201501	4286	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Vice Chairman.	22	2
201501	4287	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	Thank you, Madam Chair.	22	2
201501	4288	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	I’m going to take each of the questions in turn.	22	2
201501	4289	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	I think the risks are asymmetric in terms of the timing, and the cost of lifting off too early and having to reverse course are higher than the cost of lifting off later and having to catch up.	22	2
201501	4290	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	There are two reasons why I reached that conclusion.	22	2
201501	4291	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	First, if you lift off too early, you increase the risk that you’ll have to reverse course and then you end up back at the zero lower bound.	22	2
201501	4292	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	That’s bad because the zero lower bound is not a good place to be, as our tools are limited, and because reversal back to the zero lower bound could prove damaging to our credibility.	22	2
201501	4293	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	Second, it strikes me in terms of risk diversification later and faster is preferable to early-and-slower because, in the former case, any regret about being late should at least be somewhat mitigated by the fact that the economy is stronger than expected and you are making more rapid progress back toward your objectives.	22	2
201501	4294	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	I think of the outcome as a lose-win type of situation.	22	2
201501	4295	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	In the case where you lift off too early, not only are you stuck with your policy mistake, but you also have an economy that is further away from your objectives.	22	2
201501	4296	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	I think of that outcome as more of a lose–lose case.	22	2
201501	4297	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	Now, that all being said, I think this debate doesn’t really get you that far because I have no idea about whether, when we lift off, we’re early and gradual or we’re late and fast.	22	2
201501	4298	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	Because we don’t have any certainty about that, I just don’t think it gets us very far.	22	2
201501	4299	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	This question doesn’t really speak to me that much.	22	2
201501	4300	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	In terms of developments, I would need to be confident about inflation heading back toward our 2 percent objective.	22	2
201501	4301	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	I think, just like everybody else, it’s hard to characterize all the necessary conditions that you would have to see.	22	2
201501	4302	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	Obviously, where you are, what you expect in the future, and the degree of confidence you have in that forecast are all very important.	22	2
201501	4303	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	That said, I think there are several things that are important for me.	22	2
201501	4304	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	First, what happens to labor compensation?	22	2
201501	4305	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	I think this is important in several respects.	22	2
201501	4306	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	I consider two alternative scenarios in terms of nominal wage growth over the next few months.	22	2
201501	4307	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	First, trends in nominal wage growth stay flat or firm.	22	2
201501	4308	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	In that case, there’s two inferences from that.	22	2
201501	4309	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	One is that real income trends will be quite solid because inflation will be falling relative to growth in compensation.	22	2
201501	4310	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	That will support continued growth in the economy.	22	2
201501	4311	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	The second is that the decline in actual inflation and market-based measures of inflation compensation will not be exerting significant restraint on the wage-setting process.	22	2
201501	4312	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	That will suggest there’s not feedback arising from that.	22	2
201501	4313	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	The second scenario, of course, would be if both wage compensation trends and inflation weaken.	22	2
201501	4314	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	That would be a negative development because it would mean not only less real income growth, which would have implications for the economic growth outlook, but it would also imply that there were knock-on effects due to lower inflation and lower inflation compensation into wages.	22	2
201501	4315	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	If nominal wage growth were to decline in the period ahead, that really would reduce my confidence about inflation trending higher in the future.	22	2
201501	4316	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	The second thing that’s important, obviously, is how far away we appear to be from our objectives.	22	2
201501	4317	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	This includes what happens to the unemployment rate and other indicators of labor market slack.	22	2
201501	4318	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	Less slack, broadly defined, means I’d be more inclined to lift off.	22	2
201501	4319	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	It also includes what’s happening in terms of inflation.	22	2
201501	4320	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	Here I’d look through the transitory factors pushing inflation down and focus more on aspects of inflation, such as services price inflation, that are less likely to be influenced by oil prices and the exchange value of the dollar.	22	2
201501	4321	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	A third factor that’s important is how fast are we likely to close those gaps?	22	2
201501	4322	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	On the economic growth side, this would include financial market variables, such as exchange rate value of the dollar and developments abroad.	22	2
201501	4323	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	For example, is the foreign growth outlook improving or not?	22	2
201501	4324	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	On the inflation side, as I said before, what’s happening to wages and inflation expectations?	22	2
201501	4325	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	Finally, what are the risks associated with the outlook?	22	2
201501	4326	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	Right now there is considerable concern about the outlook for foreign economic growth.	22	2
201501	4327	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	If that subsided, then I’d be more inclined to lift off.	22	2
201501	4328	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	With respect to the statement language, I think that what’s been proposed is pretty good, but one problem with it is it doesn’t really fit all the circumstances that we might find ourselves in in March.	22	2
201501	4329	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	I can imagine a situation in March in which we think that the probability of moving in June is quite low, and if we thought the probability of moving in June was quite low, then we probably would want to stick with the “patient” language.	22	2
201501	4330	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	I can imagine the second possibility, under which the probability of moving in June was moderate.	22	2
201501	4331	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	We weren’t really sure whether we wanted to move in June, and we wanted to keep our options open.	22	2
201501	4332	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	I think in that case you’d instead want to have the kind of language that President Williams suggested, that is more open ended—putting it on the table without committing ourselves.	22	2
201501	4333	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	But we could find ourselves in March in a situation in which the economy is doing really well and we’re really sure, highly confident that we want to move in June.	22	2
201501	4334	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	In that case, the language that was suggested might be appropriate, that is, “a couple of meetings.”	22	2
201501	4335	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	I would actually prefer to have language that was crafted for the degree of confidence that we have in March, frankly, because I don’t want to get into a situation in which we’re saying, “Oh, well, we can’t move to this language, because that’s going to pre-commit us to June too strongly.”	22	2
201501	4336	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	It seems to me we need to craft language that gives us the degree of optionality that we actually want to have.	22	2
201501	4337	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	I would actually suggest that the staff develop a couple of alternatives that map into highly likely we want to move in June, not so likely—I don’t know, perhaps two or three alternatives.	22	2
201501	4338	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	Then, I think that will be easier to get the Committee to a consensus if the language actually matches the probability of when we think we will actually move.	22	2
201501	4339	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	This also should be a way of making sure we communicate more clearly to the market.	22	2
201501	4340	2015-01-28	meeting	DUDLEY	Thank you, Madam Chair.	22	2

201501	4346	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	In the language we’re using now, as Vice Chairman Dudley has just said, March would be our last opportunity to send a message that we might move in June.	22	2
201501	4347	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	So if we don’t send that message, I think we’re saying we’re going to not move before September, and I’ll come back to that.	22	2
201501	4348	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	What would we want to see?	22	2
201501	4349	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	Well, we’d obviously like to see continuing increases in employment and declines in unemployment.	22	2
201501	4350	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	We’d like to see some signs of a return of either inflation or nominal wage growth or both, and the question is, what inflation?	22	2
201501	4351	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	Well, we tend to say “core,” because core leaves things out.	22	2
201501	4352	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	But what core inflation doesn’t leave out are the secondary effects of oil that operate through the prices of other goods.	22	2
201501	4353	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	We also have commodity price declines affecting inflation.	22	2
201501	4354	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	I don’t think that looking through the effect of oil and looking at core inflation are the same thing.	22	2
201501	4355	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	We are likely to see a decline in core inflation, a decline that is likely to go away as the oil price stabilizes, wherever it stabilizes, and which could turn around rather quickly if, as some people think, we might see the oil price back in the range of $70 per barrel or so later in the year.	22	2
201501	4356	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	The question that I’d like to ask is if we relate to core inflation, when do we think we’ll move?	22	2
201501	4357	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	It’s very unlikely we’re going to see very much by September, unless the price of oil turns around, which seems to mean that we’d move in December if we’re waiting to see core inflation, say, getting up to 1½ percent.	22	2
201501	4358	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	We need to think about whether that’s what we’d like to do or whether we want to craft language that will give us some possibility of changing our mind on having to have core inflation, let’s say, above 1.4 percent.	22	2
201501	4359	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	Now, there’s a range of views about whether 1.5 percent is enough.	22	2
201501	4360	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	I, deep down, believe that the Phillips curve exists and has a negative slope.	22	2
201501	4361	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	I’m not certain that I believe that it’s vertical in the long run, but I believe that it’s a lot more vertical than it has been at rates of unemployment that, until recently, were high and inflation very low.	22	2
201501	4362	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	I think we’ll need to weigh what happens to our credibility if we have to wait longer than we now think, and you can say a lot of things about that, but we have to remember that there are two sides to that issue.	22	2
201501	4363	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	You remember that, in 1994, the FOMC waited.	22	2
201501	4364	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	It added to its credibility because it turned out to be right, or at least the former Chairman turned out to be right.	22	2
201501	4365	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	It’s a question of whether we’re going to be confident that what we do is correct, and I think there will be some questions about that.	22	2
201501	4366	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	I’d like to add a few comments on two issues about the question of early and gradual versus late and steep.	22	2
201501	4367	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	The staff’s stochastic simulations show outcomes are very similar.	22	2
201501	4368	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	Well, I’m not absolutely sure of the reasons, but if we are looking at a fully rational set of expectations, the similarity must come from the fact that they’re looking to future interest rates and future interest rate paths because, within two years, the two paths of interest rates converge.	22	2
201501	4369	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	Future interest rate paths will look very alike.	22	2
201501	4370	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	I suppose that’s one factor.	22	2
201501	4371	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	The other factor, which is very important, I think relates to something President Lacker said or somebody down there said.	22	2
201501	4372	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	I’ll take credit if it’s a good thing.	22	2
201501	4373	2015-01-28	meeting	LACKER	[Laughter]	22	2
201501	4374	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	Somebody implied that the shocks are different in the two cases.	22	2
201501	4375	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	But the shocks are the same.	22	2
201501	4376	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	They run it in such a way that the two policies face the same set of shocks, and so that, as well as the fact that the expectations are the same, gives a certain similarity to the policies.	22	2
201501	4377	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	I don’t know which is more important.	22	2
201501	4378	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	I suspect that the role of the shocks is, and what that means, and it’s something that I think we need to bear in mind, is that we really can’t confidently say “gradual.”	22	2
201501	4379	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	We are going to be driven by future shocks, as much as anything.	22	2
201501	4380	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	The shocks in the stochastic simulations are not chosen to be particularly large; they’re drawn from the history of past shocks.	22	2
201501	4381	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	And I think—and I’ve heard it said by several people, and I think I’ve heard the Chair say it on some occasions—the argument that we need to try and get a bit away from forward guidance during this period, which was just made by somebody up there [laughter]—by President Williams—is particularly valid because we are going into a stochastic world and that means that forward guidance is going to be a problem, and we should forget about it.	22	2
201501	4382	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	Now, just building on that, with regard to the statements, I particularly value in the statement that it goes in the direction of making it clear that we will react to events as they happen and that we might—and there’s an explicit statement to this effect—change direction at times if the data come in that way.	22	2
201501	4383	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	I think that’s very important because it is striking that, looking at the sequences of interest rate paths since 1994, there really is a tendency to keep going for a long time in one direction and there are very few reversals.	22	2
201501	4384	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	Maybe that reflects how deeply the business cycle is the driving force in this economy and that it’s obvious to everybody.	22	2
201501	4385	2015-01-28	meeting	FISCHER	I suspect that we have a very high weight on not wanting to change direction, and we need to think about that as we move ahead from the decision that we make.	22	2
