201501	4391	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Governor Tarullo.	22	2
201501	4392	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	Thank you, Madam Chair.	22	2
201501	4393	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	Let me begin by joining President Williams and Vice Chairman Dudley and, I think, Governor Fischer in suggesting that the question before us is not whether we want to wait too long or we want to go too early.	22	2
201501	4394	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	The question is trying to select the best moment to go, and I, at least, read the staff memo not as posing that question to us, but instead trying to make us think about what the costs of going too early or too late would be if, ex post, we figured out that we had erred a bit.	22	2
201501	4395	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	In that spirit, I guess I would say that an important going-in position for me is that in the current circumstances, with inflation running as persistently below target as it has been, I actually see us having an opportunity to fulfill more the mandate of maximum employment by not prematurely removing accommodation, allowing what I believe to be continued substantial slack in the labor market to further dissipate, but as the dual mandate instructs us to do, making sure that we are doing that in that famous Federal Reserve phrase, “in the context of price stability.”	22	2
201501	4396	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	As I suggested yesterday, I think there is a good argument to be made for the proposition that the natural rate of unemployment is actually lower and perhaps significantly lower than the current rates that many of us have been specifying.	22	2
201501	4397	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	I forgot to mention yesterday that some of the staff in the pre-FOMC briefings had made the very good point that the part time for economic reasons statistic not only suggests that there are people who would like to be working full time and aren’t, but if you push behind those numbers you’ll see that the number of multiple job holders is lower than it has been historically, suggesting that there is yet another dimension of slack there.	22	2
201501	4398	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	But even with that predisposition, I have had to ask myself and the Kiley-Nelson- Reifschneider memo pushed me to ask myself, “Okay, what’s the limiting principle here?”	22	2
201501	4399	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	That is, what are the conditions under which we should be lifting off as opposed to why I should be inclined to delay to allow the further improvement in the labor market to take place?	22	2
201501	4400	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	I don’t think it’s easy.	22	2
201501	4401	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	I haven’t really heard anything today that makes it any easier, although I think, as he often does, President Lockhart gave a very balanced and fair-minded set of conditions that we might look to, which I thought were helpfully supplemented by a number of you, most recently Bill and Stan.	22	2
201501	4402	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	But, again, being honest with myself, I don’t think there are going to be particular triggers that are going to be particularly convincing to me and probably to many of you, except for those of you who have wanted to raise rates for some time now, and so you’re not going to need any additional trigger to think that it ought to go up.	22	2
201501	4403	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	Under those circumstances, yes, I’ll be looking for some of the things that many of you have indicated.	22	2
201501	4404	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	However, I’m not sure how much guidance I’m giving myself or we’re giving one another in talking about these things because I suspect, in the end, as with many of the decisions that we reach, they will be data dependent, but because the data are not all that predictable and the mix of data and the conditions are not that predictable, it will end up being a kind of gestalt-like judgment.	22	2
201501	4405	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	Here I have been skeptical about a lot of predictions about where wages and other things were going to go based on past patterns just because so much has been different.	22	2
201501	4406	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	When President Williams was alluding to the 1965 experience today what immediately leapt into my head was, “Oh, but this was the classic period of the Johnson Administration wanting guns and butter.”	22	2
201501	4407	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	It was a period of enormous increases in federal government expenditures, which, of course, did lead to a bunch of inflation and eventually led to the demise of the Bretton Woods system.	22	2
201501	4408	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	There was an awful lot going on in the background.	22	2
201501	4409	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	I don’t think the risks of big fiscal stimulus are all that great right now.	22	2
201501	4410	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	All of that leads me, actually, to what is, in many respects, is the most important point for me, and this, again, is one that President Williams, Vice Chairman Dudley, and Governor Fischer, have all addressed, and that is the language.	22	2
201501	4411	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	The reason, for me at least, that the language is important is that I had perhaps mistakenly understood the insertion and contemplated removal of the “patient” language not as flipping the kitchen timer and saying, “Okay, the egg is going to be done in three minutes,” but instead as meaning that we would collectively have seen enough improvement in the economy that we were now close to the more normal circumstance in which federal funds rate actions are potentially on the table at any FOMC meeting, not that we are in some strongly presumptive mode of saying two meetings from now it goes up.	22	2
201501	4412	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	I fear that President Lockhart is right and that markets actually do believe that right now “patient” comes out and the clock starts and, two meetings later, rates go up.	22	2
201501	4413	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	If that is, indeed, the case, then my threshold for agreeing to the removal of that language is essentially going to be, am I ready to raise rates—which obviously is a higher threshold.	22	2
201501	4414	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	How do we avoid getting to that point?	22	2
201501	4415	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	I think there are two complementary ways of doing it.	22	2
201501	4416	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	The first is through the Chair’s statements—and Vice Chairman Dudley and Governor Fischer, perhaps, complementing the Chair’s statements—that give more of a sense that I’ve just given of what “patient” would mean.	22	2
201501	4417	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	I know there are already planned opportunities for the Chair in the month of February to do that and perhaps derivable opportunities for Vice Chairman Dudley and Governor Fischer to do the same thing in that period.	22	2
201501	4418	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	It will be a lot of work because I think we’re running against expectations that this is now going to be something like an automatic move, but I think we have to do that.	22	2
201501	4419	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	The second way, as a number of you have suggested, is to make changes in the language from what the staff suggested.	22	2
201501	4420	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	I don’t have language, but from my point of view, the desideratum would be basically language that said, “In light of improvements in the economy, the Committee anticipates that increases in the federal funds rate may be considered beginning in the relatively near future.”	22	2
201501	4421	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	But then there’s no preset course, and there’s data dependency and all the other things that we start to say, but basically we’re trying to support this notion that we’re now moving into a normal analytic mode, as opposed to the “considerable time” mode or the in- between “patient” mode.	22	2
201501	4422	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	I think that has a beneficial side effect for financial stability, and here’s why.	22	2
201501	4423	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	As I said, I think, at the previous meeting, or maybe it was the one before, my guess is that when I’m actually motivated to think it’s time to begin liftoff, I’m as likely, and perhaps more likely, to be motivated by financial stability considerations than fears of price inflation getting substantially and persistently above target.	22	2
201501	4424	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	On financial stability, I have now a very precise metric for thinking about financial stability considerations and when we should be worried about them.	22	2
201501	4425	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	It basically builds on the observations of many market participants that—and these are their terms—there’s going to be turbulence when you guys move.	22	2
201501	4426	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	That’s what they say.	22	2
201501	4427	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	My very precise metric is that it’s definitely okay to have landing-in-Logan-type winds, and, as President Rosengren will tell you, there’s always wind when you land at Logan.	22	2
201501	4428	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	It may be okay to have a landing at O’Hare after a line of storms has passed through, which is a little bit more bracing, but it’s still sort of okay.	22	2
201501	4429	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	What we really don’t want is, when you’re over the North Atlantic and the pilot comes on and tells the flight attendants to take their seats because—and some of you, I’m sure, have been through that—that’s when things can, in fact, get out of hand a bit.	22	2
201501	4430	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	I believe that if we change the language in a way that I suggested, it’s basically saying to the world, it’s now on the table:  The possibility of federal funds rate increases is going to be actively debated at probably each succeeding meeting now that rates are in play—we may not do it, but it’s going to be a real discussion at each succeeding meeting.	22	2
201501	4431	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	If so, I think you’re going to get a fair amount of movement in financial markets because people who have thought that things are more or less a one-way bet, which they had to turn around during the “taper tantrum” and slipped back there, are going to once again be rethinking.	22	2
201501	4432	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	People are going to be making different calculations.	22	2
201501	4433	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	Everybody is going to be a little bit more sensitive to “Gee, what do you think?	22	2
201501	4434	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	Are they at the point of doing it now?”	22	2
201501	4435	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	That will entail some measure of de facto tightening and a little less accommodation in financial markets.	22	2
201501	4436	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	But I think that’s a reasonable price to pay in order for us to be able, in a macroeconomic sense, to lift off at the right time as opposed to at a time when we still may have some uncertainty about the strength of the labor market, when, as Governor Brainard was alluding to yesterday, we may still be worried that further strengthening of the dollar will have a further disinflationary effect, or the like.	22	2
201501	4437	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	I realize that most of the early part is not as precise as it may be, but I really hope that we can come up with, not just different language, but a very clear and agreed-upon understanding of what that different language means so that people like myself are not placed in a position of opposing the removal of “patient” on the grounds that it’s a liftoff, but instead we can support the removal of “patient” on the grounds that it just gets things into play and actually will cause market participants, as us, to make different kinds of bets and have different kinds of expectations.	22	2
201501	4438	2015-01-28	meeting	TARULLO	Thank you, Madam Chair.	22	2

201501	4441	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	Thank you, Madam Chair.	22	2
201501	4442	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	On “too soon” versus “too late,”	22	2
201501	4443	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	I continue to think that the risks of going a meeting too soon are greater than the risks of going a meeting too late.	22	2
201501	4444	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	I think as we get closer to the event—and we are really talking, for the most part, about differences of a meeting or two—that consideration weighs less and less for me.	22	2
201501	4445	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	My simple model of this situation is as follows.	22	2
201501	4446	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	First, the real economy is eliminating slack at a gallop, and on that path some slack remains, but essentially all of it will be gone by the end of this year, roughly speaking.	22	2
201501	4447	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	Inflation and inflation expectations and interest rates, at a minimum, haven’t gotten the memo on that—and it may in fact be that they are sending signals of possibilities of bad outcomes.	22	2
201501	4448	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	Policy is in a position to be patient, to see whether these bad outcomes materialize, to see whether we start to see a shrinking deviation from our inflation goal rather than a growing one.	22	2
201501	4449	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	But policy can’t be indefinitely patient in this situation, in which slack is being eliminated so quickly.	22	2
201501	4450	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	For me, what that means, ultimately, is that it will be appropriate to lift off in June or September.	22	2
201501	4451	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	Now, as others have remarked, putting June on the table would mean taking the “patient” language out of the statement at the March meeting, which is seven weeks away.	22	2
201501	4452	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	It is, I would say, not more than 50 percent likely, and probably significantly less than 50 percent likely, that we will get incoming data that would provide confidence to do that in seven weeks.	22	2
201501	4453	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	In fact, it is probably equally likely that we will get data that suggests we are still moving further away on some measures, either in inflation expectations or in core inflation.	22	2
201501	4454	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	The other problem here is that making that language change in March could potentially trigger liftoff, because the opposite of “unlikely to lift off for at least two meetings” is “likely to lift off in the next two meetings”—specifically, two meetings out.	22	2
201501	4455	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	I’ll come back to that language change in a second.	22	2
201501	4456	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	I actually think, if the January and February employment reports are really strong and global conditions settle down and that kind of thing, I could well be standing at the June meeting thinking it would be good to lift off now.	22	2
201501	4457	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	I think it’s a lot less likely that I would be in a position of feeling so confident as to do that at the time of the March meeting.	22	2
201501	4458	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	As I said, fortunately, conditions are such that the Committee can be patient, and I would add to those, frankly, at least domestically and importantly, financial conditions.	22	2
201501	4459	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	I have been concerned that there would be bubble conditions and things like that, which would suggest that we should move faster rather than sooner.	22	2
201501	4460	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	I don’t see that at all.	22	2
201501	4461	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	Again, I come down on June or September.	22	2
201501	4462	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	Now, let me talk for a minute about what I would need to see on inflation.	22	2
201501	4463	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	For me, the strength of economic growth and employment is an important indicator, potentially, in giving confidence that inflation will indeed trend back toward our goal.	22	2
201501	4464	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	I can’t really answer the question about inflation in the abstract.	22	2
201501	4465	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	I would say, as a general matter, I’m concerned about low inflation, but perhaps less so than some, for two reasons.	22	2
201501	4466	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	First, we’ve got transitory shocks in oil and with regard to the dollar that I don’t see as a threat to the longer-term anchoring of expectations.	22	2
201501	4467	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	I wouldn’t personally be alarmed by small fluctuations in the Michigan survey during this unusual period.	22	2
201501	4468	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	Of course, those things may or may not be transient, if the dollar and oil keep moving.	22	2
201501	4469	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	Second, it would be one thing if these readings were coming in at a time when the economy were weakening, instead of at a time when slack is disappearing very quickly.	22	2
201501	4470	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	I feel differently about them because of that factor.	22	2
201501	4471	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	On wages, I would not make that a requirement.	22	2
201501	4472	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	I don’t think we know enough about the relationship between wages and price inflation to effectively make that a threshold.	22	2
201501	4473	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	On core inflation, I would distinguish between what I’d like to see and what I would need to see.	22	2

201501	4475	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	Honestly, I think I’d need to see that the transitory lows that we’ve seen in the fourth quarter of last year and the first quarter of this year are in fact transitory.	22	2
201501	4476	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	We need to have good reasons to think that those are transitory, and you certainly would need not to see it moving further away from the goal.	22	2

201501	4479	2015-01-28	meeting	POWELL	Turning quickly to the statement language:  I think that folks have now put their finger on the issue, which is it would be great to have a technology for changing “patient” in a way that gives us a range of meetings—four or five meetings, a few meetings—rather than just the next couple of meetings.	22	2

201501	4527	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Governor Brainard.	22	2
201501	4528	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	22	2
201501	4529	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	My own thinking about the timing of liftoff and the pace of tightening thereafter hinges on four considerations: the underlying momentum in the real economy, and its likely ability to sustain that strength as monetary policy support is withdrawn; confidence that inflation will move back to our target in the next couple of years; recognition of the asymmetry in our ability to respond to the need for a policy correction; and vigilance about financial stability risks.	22	2
201501	4530	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	On the domestic activity front, at the time of liftoff I expect to see continued evidence that the underlying momentum is sufficiently robust to withstand a tightening of monetary policy on top of likely ongoing financial tightening associated with a strong dollar.	22	2
201501	4531	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	The Tealbook forecast of household demand and business investment through the first half of this year, with employment continuing to grow at or above 200,000 per month; consumption increasing by around 4 percent, supported by the gain in real disposable income from lower prices at the pump; and business fixed investment continuing to advance despite a temporary drag from falling drilling and mining investment would meet those requirements.	22	2
201501	4532	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	We are much less likely to see convincing evidence by the time of liftoff to provide full confidence of the return of inflation to its 2 percent target.	22	2
201501	4533	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	Because of the large influence of the recent decline in energy prices on inflation, it is highly unlikely we are going to see signs in the next few quarters of actual headline inflation moving back to 2 percent.	22	2
201501	4534	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	So we are probably going to need to rely on a pattern of improvement across a variety of related indicators for some assurance that we are on track.	22	2
201501	4535	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	Ideally, I think we would want to see monthly increases in core inflation moving up from the very low levels that have been reached, or, at minimum, to have some confidence that an inflection point has been reached.	22	2
201501	4536	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	It is also critical to be sure that inflation expectations remain well anchored.	22	2
201501	4537	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	In that regard, I think it will be, at least, necessary that survey measures remain stable, but I think it would also be encouraging to see some correction in longer-run inflation compensation from current very low levels.	22	2
201501	4538	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	I would also take reassurance from some stabilization or even a correction in the value of the dollar that the drag on inflation from declining import prices will begin to wane.	22	2
201501	4539	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	It would, of course, be reassuring to see signs of increasing wage pressures, but for reasons that I think have already been discussed, I would not necessarily expect that to be in train at the time of liftoff.	22	2
201501	4540	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	Realistically, I think it’s very unlikely we are going to have strong confidence in rising inflation by June, or possibly even by September of this year.	22	2
201501	4541	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	We should, I think, anticipate that we are going to have to make a decision in a highly uncertain environment, and, therefore, to maintain some scope to adjust course as we learn about how the market is responding.	22	2
201501	4542	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	This highlights the asymmetry in our toolkit.	22	2
201501	4543	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	In this area, I would say my risk assessment is more animated by the episode of Japan in 2000 than it is by the United States in 2004.	22	2
201501	4544	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	I would be very concerned to avoid a risk of returning to the zero lower bound shortly after liftoff, when the options for monetary policy will be limited.	22	2
201501	4545	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	In addition, in the current economic environment in which fiscal support is extremely unlikely and the global economy is exerting very deflationary pressures, I think it will make it even more difficult for monetary policy to correct for adverse shocks.	22	2
201501	4546	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	I think the same risk-management considerations point toward a relatively gradual path of policy initially, in order to leave room for adjustment as we learn more about the underlying strength of activity and inflation, and about the reaction of markets to policy adjustments.	22	2
201501	4547	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	We will also want to be attentive to the possible effects on risks to financial stability of both the timing of liftoff and the pace of our adjustment thereafter.	22	2
201501	4548	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	I think this is, to a large degree, a countervailing risk that requires a high degree of vigilance, especially in light of the puzzles that we talked about surrounding the decline in longer-term nominal Treasury yields.	22	2
201501	4549	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	It is extremely useful to have the opportunity at this meeting to deliberate now on the likely future path not just of monetary policy but also of communications surrounding the policy path.	22	2
201501	4550	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	It’s very clear from the memo that communications matter, in many respects, very consequentially, at moments of large inflections in the policy path.	22	2
201501	4551	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	I think we have heard from several people around the table, and I strongly agree, that to the extent we want to keep both June and September on the table for possible liftoff, which I would want to do, providing too much precision in our forward guidance in March paradoxically might actually take June off the table.	22	2
201501	4552	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	In particular, I would want to have the option to decide in June, based on data that are available at that time.	22	2
201501	4553	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	But if we have to pre-commit in March to a couple of meetings in specific, I am guessing that the data we have available in March will preclude at least my comfort with making a commitment about June.	22	2
201501	4554	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	I had in mind language that was quite similar to what President Williams put on the table, but I’d leave it to the staff to try to figure out how to introduce enough constructive ambiguity in the language while also putting June and September on the table.	22	2
201501	4555	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	Finally, I also resonated with a comment made by President Plosser.	22	2
201501	4556	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	The description of the path of possible future policy I think is very difficult to capture in the statement at the timing of liftoff.	22	2
201501	4557	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	Unfortunately, I don’t think the proposed language achieves what you are setting out to do.	22	2
201501	4558	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	It’s not clear, as was stated earlier, whether we’re talking about some plateau, whether we’re talking about a lower neutral rate.	22	2
201501	4559	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	In fact, I don’t think we’re actually giving much information about what will affect the path of policy.	22	2
201501	4560	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	I think it’s also an area in which I would recommend having the staff perhaps provide some additional options.	22	2
201501	4561	2015-01-28	meeting	BRAINARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	22	2
201501	4562	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Well, I’d like to thank everyone for a very thoughtful discussion and very useful suggestions pertaining to statement language.	22	2
201501	4563	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	We do have difficult choices ahead of us, and I think today’s exchange of views will facilitate our decisionmaking in the coming months and serve to improve our communications.	22	2
201501	4564	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	I know we are running late, but if you don’t mind, I’d like to add just a few thoughts of my own to this discussion.	22	2
201501	4565	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	I’d like to start with conditions that, in my view, would warrant the start of normalization, mention some factors I think should influence the subsequent pace of adjustments, and say a bit about communications.	22	2
201501	4566	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	In my view, conditions in the labor market have improved sufficiently over the past year that taking the first step toward normalization could be warranted in the not-too-distant future.	22	2
201501	4567	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	But I think we need to be careful not to jump the gun.	22	2
201501	4568	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	First of all, while it’s true that most of the policy benchmarks reported in the Tealbook prescribed lifting off today, the case for an immediate tightening becomes much less clear if one varies the assumptions used to calculate those benchmarks.	22	2
201501	4569	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	For example, if the equilibrium real interest rate is currently near zero, as the Laubach-Williams model suggests, and if the natural rate of unemployment is 5 percent, which is my own personal point estimate, then the Taylor (1999) rule currently prescribes a zero federal funds rate.	22	2
201501	4570	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	In a similar vein, an interesting exercise, reported in Tealbook B, shows that optimal-control policy under a nearly pure inflation targeting approach, one that places essentially full weight in the loss function on deviations of inflation from 2 percent, and almost none on the unemployment gap, calls for a much more gradual path to the federal funds rate than the Tealbook baseline.	22	2
201501	4571	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	I’m also wary of the prescriptions of the various policy rules, because these benchmarks don’t take adequate account of the many special factors at work in today’s unusual economic environment, including the risks posed by the zero lower bound, the highly uncertain state of conditions abroad, and the many uncertainties pertaining to the likely path of inflation, particularly the continued decline in inflation compensation and the still-weak incoming wage data.	22	2
201501	4572	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	I think, on balance, these various considerations call for proceeding cautiously.	22	2
201501	4573	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	That said, monetary policy operates with a substantial lag, and we have to act on where we judge the economy is headed, not where it has been.	22	2
201501	4574	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	For that reason, I continue to anticipate that if events develop about in line with the Tealbook projection, with real GDP expanding at a moderate pace, labor conditions strengthening further, and incoming data that allows us to achieve a reasonable degree of confidence that inflation will move up to 2 percent over the next two or three years, then it will be appropriate to raise the target range for the federal funds rate later this year.	22	2
201501	4575	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	As I see it, liftoff could come as soon as the June meeting, even if backward-looking measures of core inflation are still running in the neighborhood of 1½ percent at that time, and headline inflation is running much lower.	22	2
201501	4576	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	But I intend to be particularly alert for any incoming evidence that serves to cast doubt on our projection that inflation will return to 2 percent, in addition, of course, to evidence that might suggest that economic growth at home is faltering or that foreign or financial conditions are evolving in a manner that could cause growth to slow or stall.	22	2
201501	4577	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Such developments, in my view, would suggest the need to delay liftoff.	22	2
201501	4578	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	We have said that we intend to be data dependent, and a failure to alter our plans in response to adverse incoming data pertaining to inflation or the labor market would call that promise into question and reduce our credibility.	22	2
201501	4579	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	I think we all agree that our actions after the first rate increase should also remain data dependent.	22	2
201501	4580	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Because there is such huge uncertainty about how real activity and inflation will evolve, I also recognize that the trajectory we end up following could easily be steeper or flatter than our SEP paths and could even entail a reversal of direction if conditions turn out to be sufficiently weak.	22	2
201501	4581	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	The staff papers document that several other countries that lifted off the zero lower bound had to reverse course, and that could happen to us, too.	22	2
201501	4582	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	All that being said, based on our December SEP submissions, it looks like most of us anticipate a fairly gradual pace of normalization along our modal paths.	22	2
201501	4583	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	The median funds rate projection in the SEP increases only 1¼ percentage points per year, on average, through 2017.	22	2
201501	4584	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	I think it’s worth reflecting on the reasons most of us have written down paths that largely entail only a gradual pace of tightening if economic conditions evolve in line with our forecasts.	22	2
201501	4585	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	As far as my own submission is concerned, I would mention four factors I took into account.	22	2
201501	4586	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	First, I continue to believe that the headwinds that have restrained the expansion for so long have not yet fully abated.	22	2
201501	4587	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Although I’m optimistic they will continue to fade, I anticipate they will do so only gradually.	22	2
201501	4588	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	In other words, I think r* is currently well below its longer-run normal level and rising only gradually.	22	2
201501	4589	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Second, on account of my uncertainty about the response of the economy to tighter monetary policy, I see a rationale for proceeding cautiously, so as not to disrupt the expansion.	22	2
201501	4590	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Third, I recognize that the probability of returning to the zero lower bound after liftoff is quite significant.	22	2
201501	4591	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	As the staff’s analysis suggests, one way of mitigating this risk is to adjust policy gradually in response to changes in slack and inflation, and initially to tighten slowly.	22	2
201501	4592	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Finally, I see a modest transitory undershoot of the natural rate as entailing potential benefits.	22	2
201501	4593	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	As the Tealbook simulation shows, it will permit a somewhat faster return of inflation to 2 percent, and there is also a chance that a strong labor market might draw discouraged workers back into the labor force, boosting potential output.	22	2
201501	4594	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Obviously, proceeding too slowly for too long could eventually have undesirable effects on inflation or financial stability, but I believe careful monitoring of the relevant indicators and a quick and forceful response to credible early warning signs can contain these risks.	22	2
201501	4595	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Finally, a couple of words on communications.	22	2
201501	4596	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	The staff suggested in one of the background memos that it would be useful for us to highlight several aspects of our strategy in public communications: First, that we are not on a predetermined course of raising the funds rate 25 basis points per meeting; rather, all adjustments we make will be data dependent.	22	2
201501	4597	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Second, the data-dependent nature of our strategy, coupled with the uncertain outlook for real activity and inflation and other factors, means that the actual trajectory for the funds rate may turn out to be quite different than we or the market currently expect.	22	2
201501	4598	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Conceivably, we may have to reverse course and begin easing again.	22	2
201501	4599	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Such data driven adjustments to policy are not a policy error, but are instead a natural consequence of decisionmaking in real time.	22	2
201501	4600	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Finally, that there are special factors in the current unusual economic environment that argue for proceeding cautiously in normalizing policy, especially in the early stages.	22	2
201501	4601	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	I’ve mentioned some that are important to me, and to the extent we can reach some consensus on what factors are important, I think it would be useful to explain those to the public.	22	2
201501	4602	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Let me stop there, and I thank everyone for a very useful discussion.	22	2
201501	4603	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	I am aware of the fact that we have a lunch for President Plosser.	22	2
201501	4604	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Let me turn things over to Thomas Laubach, who is going to brief us on our monetary policy alternatives.	22	2
201501	4605	2015-01-28	meeting	LAUBACH	.1  Thank you, Madam Chair.	22	2
201501	4606	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	I will be referring to the handout labeled “Material for FOMC Briefing on Monetary Policy Alternatives.”	22	2
201501	4607	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	For my maiden policy briefing, I wanted to be sure to choose a topic that would be of interest to you.	22	2
201501	4608	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	I’m glad to report that I have been successful, because most of what I had wanted to say has already been discussed by several of you.	22	2
201501	4609	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	So I shall be very brief.	22	2
201501	4610	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	My choice of topic, of course, is the declines over the past year in longer-term government bond yields and especially long-horizon forward rates in the United States and a number of foreign economies.	22	2
201501	4611	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	As noted in the upper-left of your first exhibit, a key policy question is whether a lower path for longer-term Treasury yields going forward would call for a higher or a lower future path of short-term rates to achieve the Committee’s objectives.	22	2
201501	4612	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	A box in Tealbook A, discussed several alternative factors that might have contributed to the decline in longer-term yields, and I briefly want to ponder the potential implications of two of these explanations for the appropriate stance of monetary policy.	22	2
201501	4613	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Longer-term yields across several major economies, illustrated in the upper-right, stand now at or near record lows.	22	2
201501	4614	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	The Committee’s recent statements noted the decline in far-forward inflation compensation, shown by the black line in the middle- left, which is embedded in longer-term nominal yields.	22	2
201501	4615	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	However, more than half of the decline in longer-horizon nominal forward rates over the past year is due to reductions in longer-horizon real forward rates, shown to the right, which also stand at historically low levels.	22	2
201501	4616	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Their decline could point to a sustained reduction in expectations for global equilibrium real rates—call it “global secular stagnation.”	22	2
201501	4617	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Alternatively, or in addition, real risk premiums may have declined, perhaps because investors increasingly view episodes of low real interest rates as associated with poor economic performance.	22	2
201501	4618	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Information from surveys and financial market prices related to inflation suggest that inflation risk premiums may also have declined, even to negative levels.	22	2
201501	4619	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Longer- horizon survey expectations, including the probability distribution of 5-to-10-year- forward CPI inflation from the Desk’s survey of primary dealers (not shown), have remained stable over the past year.	22	2
201501	4620	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	In contrast, risk-neutral probability distributions derived from inflation caps and floors, shown in the lower-left panel, have shifted down, pointing to an increased desire of investors to insure against low, rather than high, inflation outcomes.	22	2
201501	4621	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	It is conceivable that investors increasingly view episodes of low inflation or deflation as associated with the risk of protracted economic weakness, perhaps reflecting the experience of recent years at the zero lower bound.	22	2
201501	4622	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	As Governor Brainard pointed out yesterday, longer-term Treasury securities with payouts in nominal terms are excellent hedges against such risks, and hence their term premiums would decline.	22	2
201501	4623	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	To the extent that policymakers share the view that such episodes are costlier or more likely than previously thought, they may want to be especially cautious in removing policy accommodation to mitigate those risks.	22	2
201501	4624	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	An alternative explanation could be that a weaker outlook for economic growth abroad or additional policy accommodation by foreign central banks are being transmitted to US long-term yields via a “global portfolio balance channel.”	22	2
201501	4625	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	A piece of evidence in support of this possibility is the similarity in the responses of Treasuries and euro-area sovereign yields to the ECB’s announcement of its expanded asset purchase program last Thursday, shown in the lower-right.	22	2
201501	4626	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Over the 60-minute window following the start of President Draghi’s press conference, 10-year Treasury yields fell by almost the same amount as 10-year bund yields and by more than 10-year Italian government bond yields.	22	2
201501	4627	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Although the similar-size decline in rates on 2017 and 2018 Eurodollar futures contracts might suggest a reduction in policy rate path expectations as far as the United States is concerned, as Simon discussed yesterday, the decline in yields probably reflected mostly a compression of term premiums on Treasuries.	22	2
201501	4628	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Reductions in term premiums resulting from a global search for yield associated with additional policy accommodation abroad, if passed through to private yields in the United States, might call for future short-term rates to be higher, all else being equal, to achieve the appropriate financial conditions; of course, less so, to the extent that is accompanied by a stronger dollar.	22	2
201501	4629	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Turning to the policy alternatives for this meeting, you may view the US economy as more or less on the track you expected at the time of your December meeting.	22	2
201501	4630	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	If so, you may prefer alternative B on page 6, which makes no change to the current stance of monetary policy or the Committee’s forward guidance.	22	2
201501	4631	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	In updating your assessment of economic conditions, paragraph 1 upgrades the description of the recent pace of the economic expansion from “moderate” to “solid” and adds the positive note that “recent declines in energy prices have boosted household purchasing power.”	22	2
201501	4632	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Paragraph 1 notes the recent “strong” job gains and again reports that underutilization of labor resources continues to diminish.	22	2
201501	4633	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Paragraph 2 indicates little change in the Committee’s assessment of the outlook for growth of economic activity or its expectation that labor market indicators will continue to move toward mandate-consistent levels.	22	2
201501	4634	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	With regard to the risks to the outlook for economic activity, alternative B offers an option to point to increased uncertainty regarding the foreign economic outlook in recent months, but, in any case, states that the risks are nearly balanced.	22	2
201501	4635	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	On inflation, paragraph 1 of alternative B indicates that inflation has fallen further over the intermeeting period and attributes the larger shortfall from the Committee’s 2 percent objective “largely” to the drop in energy prices.	22	2
201501	4636	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	It characterizes the decline in market-based measures of inflation compensation in recent months as “substantial” while continuing to report that survey-based measures of inflation expectations have remained stable.	22	2
201501	4637	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Paragraph 2 provides a clearer statement of your expectations for inflation, first recognizing the likelihood that inflation will fall further in the near term, but then stating that you still anticipate that inflation will gradually rise toward 2 percent over the medium term as the labor market improves and the transitory effects of the drop in energy prices and other factors dissipate.	22	2
201501	4638	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	The remainder of the statement is the same as in December, with the exception of dropping the sentence that you used last month to emphasize that your revised forward-guidance language did not mark a change in the stance of policy.	22	2
201501	4639	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	The retention of the “patient” language would probably be interpreted as signaling that the Committee is unlikely to begin removing accommodation at the March or April meetings.	22	2
201501	4640	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Overall, alternative B appears in line with market expectations.	22	2
201501	4641	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Respondents to the Desk’s surveys generally anticipated no significant change to the Committee’s forward guidance.	22	2
201501	4642	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Most of the updates to paragraphs 1 and 2 would not surprise market participants, although the reference to uncertainty about the global outlook, if included, would garner some attention, particularly given the ECB’s recent announcement.	22	2
201501	4643	2015-01-28	meeting	YELLEN	Alternative C, on page 8, may appeal to those of you who believe that the economic expansion has gained momentum and is likely to absorb any remaining economic slack fairly quickly.	22	2

201501	4702	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	With your indulgence and despite the pressure of time, I’m not going to be as brief as some of you would like, in view of what I think is the importance of the issue before us.	23	2
201501	4703	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	There is a building desire within the FOMC to lift the federal funds rate off the effective lower bound within the next few meetings, and in some sense this desire is quite understandable.	23	2

201501	4709	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	As you will recall, Madam Chair, I dissented from the FOMC’s decisions at the past two meetings because of my concerns about the downside risk to inflation expectations, and the evolution of the data in the intermeeting period, especially the decline in market-based measures of longer-term inflation compensation, have served to increase my concerns.	23	2
201501	4710	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	All told, the evidence points to financial market participants putting significant weight on a scenario in which inflation runs persistently below 2 percent for the next decade.	23	2
201501	4711	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	And the charts that Thomas showed us, I think, are consistent with this description.	23	2
201501	4712	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	This implicitly means that they believe that the FOMC is unwilling or unable to keep inflation at the 2 percent target over the coming decade.	23	2
201501	4713	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	This slide in inflation expectations is not an accident that has happened in a vacuum.	23	2
201501	4714	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Since May 2013, through our actions and communications, we have gradually but systematically reduced the level of monetary accommodation.	23	2
201501	4715	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	This firming of policy has taken place against a backdrop of persistently low inflation and a subdued outlook for inflation.	23	2
201501	4716	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Our actions have sent a clear, however inadvertent, message about our lack of willingness to defend our inflation target from below, and I believe that the recent behavior of financial market prices show that market participants have, indeed, received this message.	23	2
201501	4717	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Now, what is to be done?	23	2
201501	4718	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	One possibility is to continue on our current path toward a June or September liftoff unless we have even more evidence that inflation expectations have currently shifted downwards.	23	2
201501	4719	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Again, this desire to wait, to continue on our path and wait for more evidence is entirely understandable.	23	2
201501	4720	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	It allows us to continue with a very comforting back- to-normal narrative that I described earlier.	23	2
201501	4721	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Unfortunately, history tells us we do not have that luxury of waiting for more information.	23	2
201501	4722	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The experiences of Japan, Europe, and Sweden all suggest that if we wait for clear evidence, incontrovertible evidence, we will have waited too long.	23	2
201501	4723	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The whole point is that we need to avoid a trap of low inflation, low inflation expectations, and low interest rates that other countries have not been able to escape.	23	2
201501	4724	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We can’t wait to make sure that we’re actually stuck in this low inflation trap before deciding to act to try to escape it.	23	2
201501	4725	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We have to be proactive with this risk.	23	2
201501	4726	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We cannot be reactive.	23	2
201501	4727	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In my assessment, the next three or four meetings are likely to be critical ones.	23	2
201501	4728	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We need to send strong signals through actions and communications that we are determined to move inflation back to 2 percent in a timely fashion.	23	2
201501	4729	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In terms of particulars, at a minimum I recommend that we commit to keeping the federal funds rate in its current range until the one-to-two-year-ahead outlook for inflation has returned to 2 percent and market-based measures of inflation compensation have normalized.	23	2
201501	4730	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The problem with this minimalist approach is that it may well be too passive.	23	2
201501	4731	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We should immediately begin exploring additional actions that we could take to deal with the risks that I’ve described.	23	2
201501	4732	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Now, putting the language in paragraph 3ʹ of alternative A into the FOMC statement would be a good starting point for the aggressive, proactive approach that I see as necessary.	23	2
201501	4733	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I’ve been emphasizing the benefits of a proactive approach.	23	2
201501	4734	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	What are the costs of a proactive approach?	23	2
201501	4735	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	There are two that I see.	23	2
201501	4736	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	First, we could create too many jobs relative to what is actually sustainable over the longer run so that U falls below U* and stays below U* for possibly a long time.	23	2
201501	4737	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We have debated whether such an outcome is actually costly, but I would like to think that whatever our view is about the size of these costs, we can agree that they are ones that we should be willing to bear if we’re to fulfill job one of a central bank, which is to keep inflation expectations well anchored.	23	2
201501	4738	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Second, there is the possibility that such accommodative policy could create macroeconomic risks through financial instability.	23	2
201501	4739	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The good news is that the QS report suggests there are few signs of such risk at this time.	23	2
201501	4740	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The one thing I don’t think we emphasize enough during our discussions is—that I think deserves attention—a permanently low inflation rate will create a permanently low level of nominal interest rates.	23	2
201501	4741	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	If we get stuck at 1.2 percent, that will translate into lower nominal interest rates forever.	23	2
201501	4742	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	That is not good for financial stability.	23	2
201501	4743	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Madam Chair, I spent my Christmas vacation in a way I thought I should, reading FOMC transcripts.	23	2
201501	4744	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	[Laughter]	23	2
201501	4745	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I went back to the late 1960s and actually read some of what President Williams was making reference to earlier.	23	2
201501	4746	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The transcripts are in some ways quite poignant.	23	2
201501	4747	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The Chairman at the time was William McChesney Martin, one of the great figures in the history of this institution.	23	2
201501	4748	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	But as he reached the end of his time as Chairman, he was painfully aware that future Committees would have to deal with, and I quote him, “an inflationary psychology that has resulted from the cumulative heritage of past failures of public policy.”	23	2
201501	4749	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	As we look around the world in 2015, we see Martin’s accumulated heritage in country after country, but of course, it’s a low inflation psychology rather than the high inflation psychology to which he referred.	23	2
201501	4750	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We need to do all that we can to avoid creating that same kind of legacy for our own successors.	23	2
201501	4751	2015-01-28	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2

201501	4817	2015-01-28	meeting	PLOSSER	Market participants, as reflected in the futures path, moved out their expectations of liftoff from June toward September.	23	2
